Good man, it is like the Jade Capital, which possesses supreme wondrous medicines—pine resin and Solomon’s seal. If one consumes them, though in an evil realm, thought-moment after thought-moment perishing, by the power of the medicine, one is ultimately not harmed."

Good Youth further asked: Though one may long cultivate pure precepts amidst afflictions, by what cause do those who study the Dao uphold precepts, concentration, and wisdom? You should know that such a person draws near to the secret treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness. For this reason, how should one cultivate precepts, how concentration and wisdom, to attain the Dao?

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed Good Youth, saying: Excellent, excellent, good man! If there are beings who receive and uphold the prohibitive precepts yet do so only for self-benefit, seeking wealth and joy among humans and gods, unable to act universally for all sentient beings, not for the protection of the supreme Dao and its Dharma, but only for self-nourishment—fearing the three evil destinies, fearing the paths of the six domestic animals, fearing the laws of worldly rulers, fearing the evil reputations of the world—they seek immediate results. Such guardianship of precepts cannot be called the cultivation of pure precepts.

Good man, what is meant by cultivating and upholding pure precepts? If there is one who liberates all sentient beings, this is called upholding pure precepts. Those who have not yet crossed over are crossed over; those who have not yet understood are made to understand; those who have not yet cultivated are made to cultivate; those who have not yet practiced are made to practice. For this reason, when cultivating such precepts, one does not perceive the marks of precepts, does not perceive the marks of cultivation, does not perceive the marks of self, does not perceive the marks of retribution. Good man, if one can be thus, this is called the cultivation of true precepts.

Good man, what is meant by cultivating concentration and wisdom? If there is one who exalts and liberates only themselves, seeking self-nourishment and self-benefit, not for the sake of sentient beings to uphold the true Dharma, who reads, recites, and contemplates merely to perceive the sins of greed, desire, and the various karmic offenses—such as thoughts of male and female, the three poisonous actions of body, speech, and mind, quarrels, disputes, beatings, humiliations, and mutual killings—because of these, they cannot be called cultivators of the pure and true Dharma.

Good man, if there are beings who cultivate concentration and wisdom, practicing equanimity toward all sentient beings, universally mindful that all beings attain the subtle and wondrous Dharma, mindful that all beings attain the wheel of the true Dharma, for the sake of enabling all beings to realize the marks of the Great Vehicle, to contemplate the meaning and flavor of the teachings, to read, recite, praise, revere, and uphold the supreme true Dharma, for the sake of enabling all beings to abide in the treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness, to attain vajra wisdom, to settle in concentration and contemplation, to swiftly ascend to the Mystery, to attain unimpeded power, and to comprehend the true marks of the Dao—when perceiving thus, there is no division, no distinction, no marks of distinction; no other, no self, no marks of other or self.

Without hatred, without love, without marks of hatred or love;
without greed, without desire, without marks of greed or desire;
without cultivation, without practice, without marks of cultivation or practice;
without cause, without effect, without marks of cause or effect.

Good man, if one can be thus, this is called cultivating the treasury of concentration and wisdom, the Ocean of Emptiness.

Good man, if one can destroy all marks of greed, desire, and the like in sentient beings, this is called cultivating wisdom. Through cultivation, one shatters the mind of doubt, for the sake of cultivating the Dao. Through cultivating the Dao, one sees the nature of the Dao. Seeing the nature of the Dao, one enters the treasury of the One Vehicle, the Ocean of Emptiness. Having entered this treasury, one severs all dharmas of birth-and-death and all dharmas of affliction in sentient beings. Once all demonic influences are severed, one attains constant bliss, purity, and freedom, entering the treasury of the One Vehicle, the Ocean of Emptiness Dharma.

Sudhana further said:
What has been spoken of as "without division, without distinction" is called the treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness. Why is it not said that "with division, with distinction" is the treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness?

Then the Heavenly Worthy replied to Sudhana:
Good man, it is just as you say. As you have spoken, "with division, with distinction" is called the treasury of the wisdom of the Ocean of Emptiness. But this is not so. Why?

"Because there is beginning and end, there is birth-and-death."

Sudhana further said:
"These dharmas of birth-and-death have no beginning or end. Because they have no beginning or end, they are called 'constant'—this is what is meant by the Ocean of Emptiness. Why then is it not said that the dharmas of birth-and-death and affliction are the treasury of the wisdom of the Ocean of Emptiness?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied:
"Good man, these dharmas of birth-and-death all possess cause and effect. Because they possess cause and effect, they cannot be called the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness. Why? The emptiness of the Ocean of Emptiness is without cause or effect, without beginning or end."

Sudhana further said:
"As you have said, the emptiness of the Ocean of Emptiness is without cause or effect, without beginning or end. Why then do you speak of cultivating practice to see the nature of the Dao? Rebirth in the heavens arises from causes, and the enjoyment of bliss arises from causes—is not the constant bliss of the Ocean of Emptiness also a fruit? Why then do you say the emptiness of the Ocean of Emptiness is without cause or effect?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied:
"Good man, when I speak of the cause of cultivating practice in the Ocean of Emptiness, this is the nature of the Dao. The nature of the Dao-nature is without birth or extinction. Because it is without birth or extinction, it is the Ocean of Emptiness. The emptiness of the Ocean of Emptiness is without cause or effect. Because it is without cause or effect, it severs afflictions. For this reason, it is called 'cultivating practice.'"

Sudhana further said:
"As you have said, the nature of the Dao-nature is without birth or extinction. Is the Dao-nature of sentient beings shared by all, or does each possess it individually? If it is shared, then when one being enters the treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness, all sentient beings should likewise enter. For example, if there are a hundred or a thousand enemies, when one makes peace, all hundred or thousand are at peace; when one bears enmity, all hundred or thousand bear enmity. The Dao-nature is also thus: when one attains it, all attain it; when one does not attain it, none attain it. If each possesses it individually, then it is impermanent. Why? Because it can be counted. How then can you say the Dao-nature of sentient beings is neither one nor two? If each possesses it individually, you should not say the Dao-nature is equal, like empty space."

The Heavenly Worthy replied:
"Excellent, excellent, good man! What you have questioned is this: the Dao-nature of sentient beings is neither one nor two, ultimately equal, like empty space, and shared by all sentient beings. Good man, deep in the mountains there is a treasure called Supreme Victory. If a person takes it, they become wealthy. The Dao-nature of sentient beings is also thus."

Sudhana further said:
"As you have said, is this treasure of Supreme Victory one or many? If it is one, then once one person obtains it, it should be exhausted, and the mountain would be empty of treasure. How then can you say that all sentient beings who cultivate pure precepts enter the secret treasury of the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness? If it is many, how can you say the Ocean of Emptiness is not all dharmas, and that the Dao-nature of sentient beings is also thus?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied:
"Good man, it is like a single road, whether wide or narrow, where all sentient beings walk without obstruction. The Dao-nature of sentient beings is also thus. Good man, it is like a jewel with only one gate. Though many people pass in and out, there is no crowding or hindrance; nor does anyone break or take away the jewel. The Dao-nature of sentient beings is also thus. Good man, it is like a bridge that bears all travelers, whether heavy or light. The bridge itself neither increases nor decreases. The Dao-nature of sentient beings is also thus."

Then Sudhana said to the Heavenly Worthy:
"Such analogies are difficult to fathom; their meaning is profound. Yet this cannot be so. Why?"

Those who walk ahead on the road obstruct those who follow. How then can you speak of there being no hindrance?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "What you describe does not accord with principle. Are these analogies not merely partial, rather than encompassing all? If it were a worldly path, there would indeed be obstruction, with distinctions between this and that, and no equality. But the Dao-nature of the sea and sky allows sentient beings to proceed without hindrance, equal and undivided, without distinction between this and that. Such is the true Way, which serves as the illuminating cause for the Dao-nature of all sentient beings, not as a generating cause. It is like a lamp that illuminates objects.

"Good man, all sentient beings arise from the conditions of afflictions and ignorance. One cannot say that after a single course of afflictions and ignorance has run its course, the rest should be absent. All sentient beings possess the conditions of ignorance, and thus it is said that the conditions arise in sequence, all equally. When sentient beings cultivate the true Way of non-action and sever the afflictions and delusions of sentient beings, this is called equality—seeing all dharmas as without this or that, without hindrance. Therefore, the Perfected One is named Fragrant Youth, who gains the power of wisdom and clearly perceives the minds of others."

Sudhana said: "All sentient beings have dissimilar bodies—some tall, some short, some with heavenly bodies, some human, some animal, some hungry ghost, some hell-being. Such bodies differ in every way. How then can you say the Dao-nature is one?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Good man, it is like salt placed in various substances, even in water, where all become salty. The substance is not called salt, nor is the salt called the substance, yet even in water it is thus. Though the name changes, the nature of salt remains unchanged, and its saltiness pervades all five flavors. If one drinks the water, the saltiness is strongly present, though no salt is seen within the water. The Dao-nature of sentient beings is also thus. Though the five destinies differ in body, long or short, the Dao-nature remains constant and unchanging.

Upon hearing this, the four assemblies were filled with joy, their hearts leaping with delight. They rose to bow, then returned to their seats.

Then Sea-Sky Treasury of Wisdom rose, prostrated at the Way’s feet, bowed, and asked: "Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, you have expounded the wondrous scripture of the One Vehicle, the *Sea-Sky Treasury of Marvels*, fully revealing its aspects for the sake of sentient beings, teaching its profound meaning and inconceivable merit. Excellent indeed, Heavenly Worthy, that you have spoken thus! How is it that sentient beings dwell in the city of birth-and-death, giving rise to various illnesses—bodily sickness, mental sickness—and through these, their bodies, speech, and minds commit manifold evils? By committing evil, they cycle through the three realms, enduring all manner of suffering. How does the Perfected Immortal, the Supreme Youth, dwell in the jeweled and radiant royal city, endowed with excellent marks, profound wisdom, constant joy, and freedom, skillfully upholding the secret treasury, contemplating its meaning, and inquiring into the scriptures for the sake of all sentient beings, becoming their refuge?"

Having spoken thus, he gazed up at the Heavenly Worthy’s face, his mind free of other thoughts.

Then the Heavenly Worthy answered in a gentle voice: "Excellent, excellent, good man! Sea-Sky Treasury of Wisdom, for the sake of sentient beings, you ask thus. In asking thus and speaking thus, you seek to benefit all beings and open the eyes of the blind. Good man, how is it that sentient beings dwell in the city of birth-and-death, giving rise to various illnesses?

"Good man, when I previously expounded this scripture, seven thousand people were present to hear it. Among them, three hundred and three generated thoughts of ignorance, spoke various words, slandered the true Dharma, and gave rise to disbelief. They rose from their seats, departed, and returned to their own lands. Then, they prepared boats to cross the sea. An evil wind blew their vessels, drifting them into the sea of ignorance, where they contracted grave illnesses—bodily sickness, mental sickness, sickness of mind, sickness of speech, and the like. They thought, ‘Why do we, as cultivators, suffer such afflictions?’ Then they invoked the Treasury of Sea-Sky Wisdom of the One Vehicle. At once, all their bodily afflictions vanished. Yet due to these conditions, they cycle through birth-and-death, abiding in the three evil destinies, enduring manifold sufferings. Thus they stray far from the true path of the Three Vehicles, fall into the land of ignorance, take human form but have the hearts of beasts, grow evil roots, devour others, and are born and die day after day, their wails filling the roads without end.

"Good man, the Perfected Youth observes these conditions and, within his own body and mind, generates great fear. He abandons all evil and dwells in the jeweled city, constantly contemplating the secret treasury of the One Vehicle, the Sea-Sky.

"Good man, it is like a great king who orders a man to feed and care for four fierce tigers, tending to their every need, bathing and grooming them. If even one tiger grows angry, the king declares by law that the man’s life will be forfeit. Hearing the king’s decree, the man is filled with terror, trembling in fear. He considers fleeing, abandoning the tigers. When the king learns the man has fled, he sends a young warrior with a drawn sword to pursue him. The man looks back, sees the young warrior behind him, and flees even faster. The young warrior, employing a cunning stratagem, hides his sword and secretly sends another man, pretending to be a friend, to call out: ‘Come back!’ The man does not believe him and enters an empty city to hide. Once inside, he sees that all the monasteries are deserted. Finding no one, he sits and lies down. Then he hears a voice from the void: ‘Alas, man! This city is desolate, with no one dwelling here.’"

Tonight, four hundred bandits will come—should you encounter them, your life will not be safe. What will you do to escape this fate?"

Then the man’s terror grew even greater, and he fled once more. His path was blocked by a river, its waters rushing and surging, with no boat or ferry in sight. His heart filled with sorrow and distress, he gathered all manner of grasses and wood to fashion a raft. Yet he thought further: "If I remain here, I will surely be harmed by the fierce tigers. But if I cross this river, the raft cannot be trusted—I may drown in the waters, yet I will not be torn apart by those tigers." So he pushed the wooden raft into the river, leaned his body upon it, and paddled with hands and feet, cutting through the current until he reached the far shore. There, he found safety as before, and his heart swelled with joy.

"Good man, all beings who hear and uphold the *Sutra of the One Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Subtlety* perceive this body as a dead dog upon the road, as a poisonous tiger. All beings who encounter this poison pity their own lives, and for this reason, they distance themselves from all evils—just as that man fled the tigers."

Then *Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury* bowed his head in praise and said: "So it is, so it is—truly as you have spoken. All dharmas are utterly not empty. Because they are not fixed, know that all dharmas are also not fixed. As you have said, the true person, the youth who cultivates the *One Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Treasure Treasury*, hears what has never been heard before. Why is *Ocean-Empty* called the great treasure hoard? How does this treasure hoard skillfully ferry all beings?"

Then the Heavenly Worthy praised *Ocean-Empty*, saying: "Excellent, excellent, good man! If there is one who reflects and cultivates wholly, they can inquire as you have. Good man, it is like when people of the world speak of the great ocean, the great river, the great mountain, the great earth, the great city, the great king, the great person, the great heaven, the great Dao. *Ocean-Empty* is also thus: there is *Ocean-Empty*, and there is the *Great Ocean-Empty*; there is the *Treasure Hoard*, and there is the *Great Treasure Hoard*. What is *Ocean-Empty*?

"Good man, it is like a starving person who obtains a little food—this is called bliss. Such bliss is also called *Ocean-Empty*. Like one who recovers from illness and finds bliss—such bliss is also called *Ocean-Empty*. Like one who, in terror, finds a place of refuge and thus attains bliss—such bliss is also called *Ocean-Empty*. Good man, it is like a poor person who obtains the seven treasures and thus attains bliss—such bliss is also called *Ocean-Empty*. Yet this is not called the *Great Ocean-Empty Treasury*. Why? Because it is bliss born of hunger and thirst, of poverty and illness, of terror—thus it is called bliss, thus it is called *Ocean-Empty*. This is the *Great Ocean-Empty*, yet not the *Great Ocean-Empty*.

"Good man, if there are faithful beings who, whether in the mundane world or the Dao of immortals, sever all fetters completely, they attain bliss. Such bliss is also called *Ocean-Empty*, yet it is not called the *Great Ocean-Empty Treasury*. Why? Because afflictions may arise again, and habitual tendencies remain—it is not constant bliss.

"Good man, only one who abides in perpetual ease and freedom may be called the *Great Ocean-Empty Treasury*. Good man, it is like a place that receives all streams—this is called the great ocean. Wherever the hundred rivers come and go, that is called the *Wisdom Treasury*. Good man, if there are beings who clearly perceive the nature of the Dao, they may be called the *Great Ocean-Empty Treasury*. For this reason, the *Ocean-Empty Treasury* is neither existent nor nonexistent, neither arising nor ceasing.

"Good man, if there is a great lord or a lesser king who, over years and months, cannot reach a certain place, that place is called a great city. A city that transmits and transforms many names is called a small city. Wherever there is transformation is called a great king; wherever the king transforms is called a small king. Small kings and great kings, following regions and transformations, are neither kings nor transformations, neither great nor small. For this reason, it is called the *Supreme Wheel-Turning Sage King*, adorned with the seven treasures, wondrous and rare—this is called the *Great Ocean-Empty Treasury*. For this reason, it is named *Ocean-Empty*.

"Good man, it is like a mighty warrior who enters the four kinds of armies without fear—know that such a person is called *Great Multitude of Power*. If there are beings who, in the three evil destinies and amidst afflictions and evil karma, feel no terror and can broadly ferry beings therein—know that such a person is the *Ocean-Empty Treasury*. If there is one who serves parents, reveres Daoists, bows in worship, burns incense, cultivates wholesome dharmas, speaks with sincerity, without deception, endures the unendurable, and bestows alms upon the poor—this is called the *True Person, Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury*. Why? The *Ocean-Empty Treasury* possesses great compassion, pitying all beings, acting as a great compassionate father to all beings, as a great compassionate mother to all beings, ferrying beings across the river of birth and death, revealing the subtle marks of the One Vehicle’s wondrous Dao. This is called the *Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury*.

"Good man, the *Ocean-Empty Treasure Hoard* is inconceivable—all beings cannot comprehend it. Because they cannot comprehend it, they do not accept it in faith, giving rise to various thoughts and uttering various slanders. Therefore, I now call it *Ocean-Empty*. The mark of *Ocean-Empty* is only emptiness with emptiness—only thus can emptiness be understood. The emptiness of understanding emptiness is emptiness without being empty, understanding without being understanding. For this reason, know that it is called *Ocean-Empty*—this is called the *Wisdom Treasury*."

Then the four assemblies, having heard these words, rejoiced greatly, leapt up in reverence, surrounded the Heavenly Worthy, bowed, and praised him: "Excellent, Heavenly Worthy! You have expounded such profound and rare teachings!"

"Among us four assemblies, there is that which we cannot comprehend."

At that moment, a youth named Marvelous Thought arose from his seat, approached the Heavenly Worthy, clasped his feet, held a lotus flower in hand, gazed up at the Heavenly Worthy, bowed his head, and inquired: "Excellent, Heavenly Worthy! You have expounded such joyous and profound teachings, so deep in meaning as to be beyond conception. What is meant by *Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury*? Is the emptiness of *Ocean-Empty* empty yet not empty, or not empty yet empty? Is the emptiness of the not-empty empty of emptiness? For this reason, is it the emptiness of many bodies, the emptiness of one body, the emptiness of dust-motes, or the emptiness of transformations? What is the meaning of emptiness? Is it emptiness of self-nature, emptiness of other-nature, or emptiness of both self and other? Due to these causes and conditions, among us assemblies, there is that which we cannot comprehend. We only beseech the Compassionate Venerable One to specially bestow your mercy, distinguish and explain these matters, and enable all beings to decisively understand the true mark."

Then the Heavenly Worthy replied to Marvelous Thought: "Excellent, excellent, good man! Among you assemblies, you serve as bridges of the Dharma for all beings, as ladders and steps of the Dharma, as the great gate of wisdom, as the great refuge. You are the true understanding of my wisdom, you are my treasury. Were it not for you, there would be none who could ask; were it not for me, there would be none who could expound."

You, with single-minded focus, skillfully contemplate and remember—thus are you named Marvelous Thought. Now listen carefully, now listen carefully.

What is meant by "Sea of Emptiness, Treasury of Wisdom"? The emptiness of the Sea of Emptiness is neither empty nor non-empty, both empty and non-empty, neither empty nor non-empty, neither non-empty nor non-empty, neither empty nor non-empty, empty yet not empty, empty without discrimination, for discrimination itself is empty—thus is it called the Sea of Emptiness. It is neither self-empty, nor other-empty, nor empty of both self and other; neither vast-empty, nor small-empty, neither empty nor non-empty, neither vast nor small; neither many-empty, nor one-empty, neither empty of dust-motes, nor empty of transformation. For these reasons, it is called the Sea of Emptiness.

The Sea of Emptiness is without self; I name it the Sea of Emptiness. Like a dust-mote filling the ten directions and measureless worlds, the body of the Sea of Emptiness is not truly the Sea of Emptiness. By its freedom, it manifests as a dust-mote body, yet not a dust-mote body, and as a single mote filling all worlds. The body of the Sea of Emptiness does not truly fill all lands and worlds. Why? Because it is unimpeded—thus is it called the body of the Sea of Emptiness, Treasury of Secret Wisdom, filling the world.

The body of the Treasury of Wisdom is not truly the Treasury of Wisdom. For these causes and conditions, the Sea of Emptiness, Treasury of Wisdom, abides unmoving, yet manifests in measureless forms across all directions, each inspiring reverence and praise in those with minds, desiring that all beings attain eloquence. The body of the Sea of Emptiness constantly abides in one direction, yet is seen by all in other directions. The body of the Sea of Emptiness, adorned with seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences, cannot be perceived by seeing form, hearing sound, smelling fragrance, distinguishing taste, sensing touch, or knowing dharmas. The six senses of the Sea of Emptiness are utterly unknowing. Why? Because it attains freedom.

The mind of the Sea of Emptiness also has no attainable mark. Why? Because there is nothing to attain—thus is it called the Sea of Emptiness. If true persons or youths of wondrous conduct conceive the notion of attainment, even the gods cannot reach the Sea of Emptiness. The emptiness of the Sea of Emptiness is empty of attainment—thus is it called the Sea of Emptiness.

The Sea of Emptiness expounds the flavor of the One Vehicle for measureless kalpas, inexhaustibly. Sometimes it teaches the Two Vehicles of precepts, concentration, and wisdom; sometimes it expounds the Three Caverns of subtle and wondrous scriptures. At such times, it observes without generating the thought, "I speak, they listen," nor does it produce even a single phrase of thought. Why? I adapt to beings, speaking more or less, following convention—thus is it called "speaking." The nature of the Dharma-nature expounded by the Sea of Emptiness is also without speech—thus is it called the Sea of Emptiness expounding the Dharma-nature.

Good man, it is like empty space: the nature of empty space cannot be seen. The expounding of the Sea of Emptiness is likewise unknowable. Good man, it is like a treasure hoard, filled with many rare and wondrous things, complete in every variety—thus is it called the Treasury of Wisdom. The profound and mysterious treasury of the Tathāgatas of the three times is also like this, filled with many marvels, complete and without lack—this is called the One Vehicle’s profound and mysterious treasury.

Good man, boundless things are called a treasure hoard; within this treasure hoard, nothing is exhausted—this is called the Treasury of Wisdom.

Then Marvelous Thought said: Venerable One, what you have expounded is truly profound. The meaning and flavor of the Sea of Emptiness perfects all beings of the future, enabling them to cultivate the foremost merit of the treasure hoard. The various analogies are inconceivable. Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, what is meant by the seven treasures’ adornment, the fulfillment of merit?

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy replied to Marvelous Thought: Excellent, excellent, good man! What is meant by the wondrous marks of the seven treasures’ adornment, the fulfillment of merit? Good man, the adornment of merit has two aspects: inner adornment and outer adornment. Outer adornment consists of the seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences. Inner adornment is the cultivation of the One Vehicle, the secret treasury of the Sea of Emptiness.

Good man, it is like a jade mountain: outwardly radiant, inwardly luminous with pure brilliance, unimpeded by measureless dust-motes. Why? Because its nature does not shift—thus is it called a jade mountain. The wondrous merit of the seven treasures’ adornment is also like this.

Furthermore, good man, I now adorn my transformed body with expedient means, manifesting as vast or small, pervading the world. With this vast body, I enter a single minute dust-mote, yet my body does not become small. Though true immortals adorn their transformed bodies to fill the world, they cannot, at such a time, make their vast bodies enter a minute dust-mote—even this they cannot do, let alone keep their minds from being disturbed. True immortals’ minds do not follow their bodies.

Good man, though true immortal youths possess divine powers to shake the world, so that all beings see and hear, their minds never conceive, "Let this divine power pervade the world, enabling beings to hear what they have never heard before." For these reasons, true immortal youths never say, "It is by my power that beings now hear what they have not heard before." If someone claims, "Because I expound the Dharma, beings hear what they have not heard," know that such a person will never attain the *Sutra of the Equal One Vehicle, the Secret Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*. Why? The mind that thinks, "Beings do not hear, so I speak for them," is a mind of birth and death. All true immortals have exhausted this mind. For these reasons, the body and mind of true immortal youths do not follow one another.

Good man, the bodies and minds of all ordinary beings follow one another. True immortals are not so. To transform beings, they manifest only small bodies, yet their minds are not small. Why? The nature of the minds of my disciples is always vast and expansive. Though they manifest vast bodies, their minds follow vastness.

How is it that a vast body fills the world? How is it that a small mind performs the conduct of an infant, wailing all day yet never hoarse? For what reason? By this cause and condition, the mind does not follow the body. The true immortal youths have already distanced themselves from the dust of sensual desires; though they dwell in the demon’s city, their minds remain unmoved. Because they are unmoved, know that the true immortals’ bodies and minds are free—manifesting as a single mote of dust, a body of afflictions. Yet each being sees them differently.

Then Miao Si again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "As you have said, the true immortal youths’ bodies and minds are free. Though they dwell in the demon’s city, their minds remain unmoved, manifesting as a single mote of dust, a body of afflictions. For this reason, doubts arise among the assembly: How do the true immortal youths cultivate practice to attain spiritual powers, shaking beings to awaken them to the *Secret Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and the Equal One Vehicle*? We beseech the Compassionate Worthy to explain this for all beings, that we may hear what we have never heard before and see what we have never seen."

Then the Heavenly Worthy replied to Miao Si: "Excellent, excellent, good man! How do the true immortal youths cultivate practice to attain the spiritual penetrations and unlock the *Sea of Emptiness Treasury*? These true immortals of old offered their kingdoms, cities, wives, children, kin, and the seven treasures as offerings. They further praised and made offerings with wondrous sounds, recited, contemplated, and expounded the meaning and flavor of the teachings. By this cause and condition, they were able to dwell in the world of Adorned Benefit, their bodies and minds no longer following one another. For what reason? They had departed from the marks of self, person, reliance, action, thought, cause, and effect. By this cause and condition, though dwelling in the demon’s city, their minds remained unmoved.

Good man, if there are beings who dwell in the demon’s city and uphold even a single phrase or word of the *Secret Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and the Equal One Vehicle Sutra*, such persons will certainly perfect their merit and virtue, abiding in eternal joy, purity, and freedom, far removed from the marks of person, self, action, and thought. Good man, if there are beings who make offerings with their beloved kin, the seven treasures, or vaidūrya, it is likewise so. For what reason?"

Such persons know cause as non-cause, for cause arises from cause, and since cause is impermanent, what is born is also impermanent. For this reason, they make offerings while far removed from all attachments.

Good man, if there are beings—good men and good women—who hear even a single word or phrase of the *Sea of Wisdom Treasury of the One Vehicle* yet do not grasp at the mark of words, the mark of phrases, the mark of hearing, or the mark of speaking, such is the mark of no-mark. By the mark of no-mark, they attain eternal joy, purity, and unimpeded freedom. Their bodies and minds become resolute, and they shall surely become the true immortal youths of the ten directions, generating a heart of compassion. This is called the body of eternal joy and freedom—neither a body nor apart from body, nor yet non-body.

For this reason, the true immortal youths cultivate the *Subtle Sutra of the Sea of Wisdom Treasury of the One Vehicle*, attaining the resolute body of profound principle and freedom.

At that time, Miao Si again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "What has been spoken is truly most profound. How do such true immortals, as fields of merit, attain the successive realization of eternal joy and freedom?"

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy replied: "Excellent, excellent, good man! How do the true immortal youths, as fields of merit, attain the resolute realization of eternal joy and freedom? Good man, true persons who uphold the precepts—even down to the various immortals—are called fields of merit. If someone declares that such beings are true fields of merit, know that this person possesses good roots, serves as a good refuge, and is the support upon which immeasurable beings rely.

Good man, the true immortal youths contemplate all immeasurable beings as none other than fields of merit. For what reason? Because of good roots, they regard beings as true fields of merit. There are three fields, six fields, eight fields, nine fields—such fields of merit give rise to immeasurable fields. According to the inclinations of beings, they expound and distinguish four kinds of fields. What are the four?

1. The impure field,
2. The pure field,
3. The field that is both pure and impure,
4. The field that is neither pure nor impure.

What is the impure field? Good man, if the donor upholds the precepts and knows the wisdom of giving, like water flowing to the stream, yet the recipient violates the precepts, clings to perverse views, and neither gives nor receives reward—due to this cause and condition, it is called impure.

What is the pure field? Good man, if the donor violates the precepts and clings to perverse views, denying the wisdom of giving and its karmic reward, yet the recipient is pure and expansively teaches the Dharma, knowing the wisdom of giving and its karmic reward—this is called the pure field.

What is the field that is both pure and impure? Good man, if both donor and recipient uphold the precepts, possess vast wisdom, and know the wisdom of giving and its karmic reward—this is called pure.

What is impure? If both donor and recipient break the precepts, violate the true statutes, and give rise to deluded confusion—this is called impure.

What is the field that is neither pure nor impure? Good man, when the most supreme donor gives to the most supreme field—this is called the neither-pure-nor-impure field. These are the four kinds of fields.

If there are beings who conceive of giving in their minds and await its karmic reward, know that such persons cling to perverse views, violate the prohibitions, and destroy the mind of the Great Vehicle. If good persons expound and distinguish between giving and receiving, such persons are called right-viewed. If they rely on the *Sutra of the Wisdom Treasury of the One Vehicle*, rightly perceive the wisdom of giving and its karmic reward—such persons are called precept-keepers, ever abiding in right view.

Good man, the true immortal youths, wherever their thoughts arise, through cultivation, perceive beings as upholders or violators of precepts, as givers or receivers, and their karmic rewards. For this reason, they are called precept-keepers, right-viewed, and they also perceive the four kinds of fields of merit and non-fields of merit."

At that time, Miao Si again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "What is called a pure land?"

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy replied to Miao Si: "Excellent, excellent, good man! You all see that I am about to return to the Land of Eternal Joy, and so you ask this question at the right time. Good man, there are four kinds of lands. What are the four?

1. The impure,
2. The both pure and impure,
3. The neither-pure-nor-impure,
4. The non-non-pure.

What is the impure? Good man, if there are beings who greedily cling to desire, slander with perverse views, and thus are born in a lower land—overgrown with thorns and poisonous grasses, barren and uneven, ugly in form, generating many evils, killing and harming living beings, with short lifespans—due to this cause and condition, they are born in a lower land. This is called impure.

What is the both pure and impure? Good man, all beings have differing thoughts and dispositions—some purify the three karmas, while others defile the body. Such beings are born in mixed lands. This is called both pure and impure.

What is the neither-pure-nor-impure? Good man, like the Land of Difficult Victory, with its extraordinary and wondrous forms, surpassingly beautiful and rare—due to this cause and condition, it is called neither-pure-nor-impure.

What is the non-non-pure? Good man, the Land of Wondrous Joy is not non-pure. For the sake of beings, it is expounded in various ways as pure in the Dao-fruit, neither existent nor non-existent, nor yet both existent and non-existent. If there are beings who cultivate the *Subtle Sutra of the One Vehicle*, generate a mind of equality, and with these good roots, vow to share this land with the immortal youths—with long lifespans, great power, and vast spiritual penetrations—then, by the power of this vow and cause, when they attain the Dao in the future, they shall see all lands as non-non-pure. This is called non-non-pure.

These are the four kinds of wondrous lands. Good man, if there are good persons who contemplate the *Subtle Sutra of the One Vehicle* with joyful minds, broadly ferrying beings across, and with these good roots, vow to share this land with all beings—far removed from desire, anger, delusion, and attachment to all things, without hunger, thirst, or afflictions in body—such is the land."

Furthermore, good man, those born among the lower ranks receive three kinds of retribution: first, the retribution of perception; second, the primary retribution; and third, residual retribution.

What is the retribution of perception? Good man, if there are beings who fully commit the ten evils, defy their parents, and slander the *Subtle Sutra of the One Vehicle*, such persons will suffer from malignant diseases, festering sores, the six illnesses, deafness, blindness, lameness, and various ailments, enduring manifold sufferings. For this reason, it is called the retribution of perception.

What is primary retribution? Good man, if there are beings who, upon birth, suffer from grave illnesses and, upon death, enter hell—abiding in gloom and darkness, dying and being reborn day after day without respite—such suffering is called primary retribution.

What is residual retribution? Good man, those reborn from hell assume the bodies of the six kinds of livestock, becoming owls, parrots, or other ill-omened birds; or they become turtles, fish, or venomous creatures; or they take the forms of macaques, deer, tigers, or leopards. Even if they attain a human body, they suffer from blindness, darkness, or the six afflictions; though they possess human form, they lack human sentiment. They are fully endowed with the ten vicious traits and all manner of foul appearances. If they leave the household life, they violate grave precepts, transgress regulations, and break the moral code. This is called residual retribution. Such residual retribution is the lingering effect of afflictions.

However, true youths who cultivate the *Subtle Sutra of the One Vehicle, the Ocean of Emptiness* can eradicate all such residual retribution and abide in the realm of true emptiness.

Furthermore, good man, how do pure and true immortal youths uphold the precept of non-killing? They perfect the five contemplative minds—lower, middle, upper, supreme, and superior—culminating in right view. These fifty minds constitute the initial arising of the aspiration, and when fully determined, they complete the fifty minds. This is called fulfillment. One hundred such minds constitute a hundred virtues, and when the hundred virtues are perfected, they form a single mark. Through such transformation and accumulation, the seventy-two marks of excellence are fully achieved. This is called the pure and wondrous body.

Good man, true youths constantly cultivate purity of body. Why? Because all gods, humans, and beings revere and submit to them. Therefore, true youths perfect the eighty-one secondary marks of excellence, their bodies unshaken, so that all beings, following their faith, pay homage, revere, praise, and honor them with minds of equality. For this reason, true youths cultivate purity of body.

Good man, it is like a wise minister who, wishing to receive the great king, first adorns and prepares the palace and halls, ensuring the provision of various delicacies, fragrant and delectable flavors. Only then does the great king proceed accordingly. True youths are likewise: desiring to invite the Wheel-Turning Saintly King of the supreme Dharma, they first cultivate and purify themselves. Only then does the Wheel-Turning Saintly King follow and abide in that place. With fragrant, sweet, and pure celestial delicacies, they make offerings skillfully. The king rejoices greatly and proclaims in praise: "Excellent, excellent! I now receive these offerings of manifold fragrances and flavors. I prepare a magnificent and wondrous jeweled throne. Reflecting thus, I shall distribute these fragrant delicacies to all impoverished beings, sating them so that they are free from hunger and thirst."

Good man, true youths are likewise: with pure bodies and minds, they invite the supreme *Ocean of Emptiness of the One Vehicle*, the ambrosial flavor of the Dharma, for the benefit of all beings, leaving none displeased.

Good man, it is like the spring month when the heavens send sweet rain, and all grasses and trees, great and small, sprout forth. The ambrosial flavor of the *Ocean of Emptiness* is likewise. Good man, if there are beings with pure minds, in a single thought-moment, their bodies transform and abide in the realm of the *Ocean of Emptiness*, attaining adamantine bodies. They sever the afflictions of the thirty-two heavens in the ten directions. Why? Because the adamantine purity perceives the mark of non-perception: though they see male and female, there is no mark of male or female; though they see form, there is no mark of form; though they see day and night, there is no mark of day or night; though they see afflictions, there is no mark of afflictions; though they see the *Ocean of Emptiness*, there is no mark of the *Ocean of Emptiness*. Why? Good man, because all dharmas are without marks, like an illusion, like a dream, like the flash of lightning or the spark from striking stone.

True youths, by this cause and condition, perceive the mark of non-perception and abide in the mark of non-abiding. Therefore, they are called those who abide in the realm of the *Ocean of Emptiness*.

Upon hearing this teaching, the four assemblies all rose, paid homage, rejoiced exceedingly, and took their leave.

*The Supreme One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom Sutra, Scroll Two* concludes.
*The Supreme One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom Sutra, Scroll Three* begins.

**Dharma Marks Chapter**

At that time, *Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom* rose from his seat, adjusted his robe and stole, held an incense burner, and stood reverently facing the Heavenly Worthy. His gaze was fixed, his eyes unturning, his mind free of stray thoughts.

Then the Heavenly Worthy asked in a gentle voice: "Virtuous one, why do you stand so earnestly, bowing so deeply? Do you have some decision to make, or is there something pressing?"

"I am the master of the great Dao for gods and humans, my eloquence unbounded, my insight penetrating the subtle and profound. I am well able to expound the treasury of immeasurable meanings, to comprehend the ten transformations of all dharma gates, and to discern the wishes of others’ minds—nothing escapes my illumination. You should ask whatever you wish without hesitation. I shall resolve the deepest roots of the Dao."

Thereupon, *Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom* answered composedly: "Greatly Wise Heavenly Worthy, I wish to ask a question but dare not speak first. The Heavenly Worthy, knowing the time, first bestowed compassionate encouragement, filling me with kindness and joy, easing my heart. Thus I know the Heavenly Worthy is surely the father of the world, the refuge of all beings, the object of veneration for the ten thousand multitudes. Now, relying on your great spiritual power and out of pity for me, I venture to speak my humble words. I pray you will heed and accept them.

Great Sage Heavenly Worthy, earlier the greatly wise one posed a weighty doubt, asking among the four paths which differ, how their fruits vary, and how their attainments diverge. The Heavenly Worthy’s answer dispelled all obstructions like melting ice, leaving no trace of hesitation, directly pointing to the source of wisdom.

The Heavenly Worthy further answered the subtle inquiry, saying that all good and evil arise from conditions, and conditions depend on the mind. You also resolved the principle that the mind’s power, being unstable, gives rise to good and evil. Such wondrous teachings are all clear and lucid. Yet I still have doubts and wish for their resolution.

Heavenly Worthy, for what reason do the roots of all dharmas arise? Are the marks of all dharma roots, being conditioned, real? Are they empty? Are they neither empty nor real?

If they are real, they should be eternally fixed, without change or transformation. If they are empty, their nature and marks are distinct, with their own forms and characteristics. If they are real, there should be no diminution or extinction. If they are empty, there should be no arising or manifestation. If they are real, they should have form and substance. If they are empty, there should be no evidence or verification.

If they are real, where do the dharmas reside after all sages attain the Dao? If they are empty, how do all sages cultivate and abide in the supreme wisdom? If they are real, when all sages relinquish these dharma marks, how do the dharma marks exist or cease? When they attain these dharma marks, from where do the dharma marks arise?

If they are empty, there is no difference between relinquishing and receiving dharmas. If they are real, where do they reside within sentient beings? If they are empty, sentient beings have no dharmas and cannot be established. If they are real, going and coming, departing and returning, should entail obstructions. If they are empty, going and coming, departing and returning, should encounter nothing.

For these reasons, the marks of all dharmas cannot be fathomed; the boundaries between emptiness and existence remain unknown. I only pray the Heavenly Worthy will descend and resolve these doubts with your eloquence."

Then the Heavenly Worthy answered *Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom*: "Excellent, excellent! True man and great being, your mind comprehends dharma marks, pure and unburdened—thus you are able to ask this question today. This will benefit all, accomplishing immeasurable merit and fruition, which are now manifest.

I shall distinguish and explain for you, so that all present and future beings may gain clear understanding, cross beyond birth and death, and enter the source of dharmas.

*Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom*, all dharma marks arise from conditioned existence; their source is not real, and their return is also empty. Why is this so? The arising of dharma marks is due to sentient beings; sentient beings being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks is due to spirits; spirits being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks is due to the world; the world being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks is due to the teachings; the teachings being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks depends on provisional names; provisional names being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from creation; creation being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from good methods; good methods being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from evil; evil being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from insufficiency; insufficiency being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from contentment; contentment being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from the eye faculty; the eye faculty being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from the ear faculty; the ear faculty being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from the nose faculty; the nose faculty being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from the tongue faculty; the tongue faculty being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from the body faculty; the body faculty being empty, dharma marks are also empty. The arising of dharma marks arises from the mind faculty; the mind faculty being empty, dharma marks are also empty.

For these reasons, know that the essence of dharma marks all arises from emptiness, from emptiness generating emptiness. Thus know that emptiness is empty, without any actuality.

When transforming sentient beings, and sentient beings receive transformation, attain the root of dharmas, and cross the sea of suffering, the dharma marks they practice immediately return to emptiness. Why is this so? If they did not return to emptiness, how could they abide? Where would they abide? Having no place, this is called emptiness."

What is meant by "from emptiness generating emptiness"? Dharma marks are not fixed; if they arose from the actual, they could not transform and adapt. Thus know that dharma marks do not arise from the actual. Not arising from the actual, they arise from emptiness. Arising from emptiness, this is called emptiness. How can the essence of emptiness generate empty dharmas? Thus know that emptiness does not depart from emptiness; if it departed from the actual, there would be no such place.

How are dharma marks due to sentient beings? Without sentient beings, there would be no dharma marks. Because of sentient beings, boundless dharmas arise. Thus know that dharma marks arise from sentient beings. How are all sentient beings empty dharmas? All sentient beings are fundamentally empty, their constructed essence also empty. Like the great plantain, like mirages and illusions, suddenly arising and swiftly vanishing—this is called emptiness. How do dharma marks follow the emptiness of sentient beings? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when sentient beings are extinguished, dharmas are also extinguished; while sentient beings are not extinguished, dharma marks are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from spirits and deities? Without spirits and deities, there would be no reverence for dharmas. Because of spirits and deities, reverence for dharmas arises of itself. Thus know that reverence for dharmas arises from spirits and deities. How are all spirits and deities empty dharmas? All spirits and deities do not abide in fixed existence; they relinquish bodies and receive bodies, ultimately returning to the true Dao. This is called emptiness. How does reverence for dharmas follow the emptiness of spirits and deities? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when spirits and deities are extinguished, reverence for dharmas is also extinguished; while spirits and deities are not extinguished, reverence for dharmas is not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How are dharma marks due to the world? Without the world, there would be no distinct dharmas. Because of the world, distinct dharmas arise of themselves. Thus know that distinct dharmas arise from the world. How is the world entirely an empty dharma? All worlds are impermanent, ultimately returning to emptiness—this is called emptiness. How do distinct dharmas follow the emptiness of the world? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the world is destroyed, distinct dharmas are also extinguished; while the world is not destroyed, distinct dharmas are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How are dharma marks due to the teachings that gather? Without the teachings that gather, there would be no ritual dharmas. Because of the teachings that gather, ritual dharmas arise of themselves. Thus know that ritual dharmas arise from the teachings that gather. How are all teachings that gather empty dharmas? All teachings that gather exist because of people; people are not actual dharmas—this is called emptiness. How do ritual dharmas follow the emptiness of the teachings that gather? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the teachings that gather are extinguished, ritual dharmas are also extinguished; while the teachings that gather are not extinguished, ritual dharmas are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How are dharma marks provisional upon expedient names? Without expedient names, there would be no skillful means. Because of expedient names, skillful means arise of themselves. Thus know that skillful means arise from expedient names. How are all expedient names empty dharmas? All expedient names are established according to conditions—this is called emptiness. How do skillful means follow the emptiness of expedient names? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when expedient names are extinguished, skillful means are also extinguished; while expedient names are not extinguished, skillful means are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from construction? Without construction, there would be no dharmas of craftsmanship. Because of construction, dharmas of craftsmanship arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of craftsmanship arise from construction. How is all construction an empty dharma? All that is made is ultimately worn away—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of craftsmanship follow the emptiness of construction? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when construction is extinguished, dharmas of craftsmanship are also extinguished; while construction is not extinguished, dharmas of craftsmanship are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from virtuous methods? Without virtuous methods, there would be no dharmas of benevolence and compassion. Because of virtuous methods, dharmas of benevolence and compassion arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of benevolence and compassion arise from virtuous methods. How are all virtuous methods empty dharmas? All virtuous methods do not attain perfect fulfillment—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of benevolence and compassion follow the emptiness of virtuous methods? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when virtuous methods are extinguished, dharmas of benevolence and compassion are also extinguished; while virtuous methods are not extinguished, dharmas of benevolence and compassion are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from evil? Without evil, there would be no dharmas that harm beings. Because of evil, dharmas that harm beings arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas that harm beings arise from evil. How is all evil an empty dharma? All evil ultimately returns to the source of goodness—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas that harm beings follow the emptiness of evil? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when evil is extinguished, dharmas that harm beings are also extinguished; while evil is not extinguished, dharmas that harm beings are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from insufficiency? Without insufficiency, there would be no dharmas of seeking. Because of insufficiency, dharmas of seeking arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of seeking arise from insufficiency. How is all insufficiency an empty dharma? All insufficiency has an end—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of seeking follow the emptiness of insufficiency? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when insufficiency is extinguished, dharmas of seeking are also extinguished...

While insufficiency is not extinguished, dharmas of seeking are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from contentment? Without contentment, there would be no dharmas of weariness. Because of contentment, dharmas of weariness arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of weariness arise from contentment. How is all contentment an empty dharma? All contentment is not wholly correct—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of weariness follow the emptiness of contentment? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when contentment is extinguished, dharmas of weariness are also extinguished; while contentment is not extinguished, dharmas of weariness are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from the eye faculty? Without the eye faculty, there would be no dharmas of form. Because of the eye faculty, dharmas of form arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of form arise from the eye faculty. How is the eye faculty an empty dharma? Through undetermined observation—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of form follow the emptiness of the eye faculty? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the eye faculty is extinguished, dharmas of form are also extinguished; while the eye faculty is not extinguished, dharmas of form are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from the ear faculty? Without the ear faculty, there would be no dharmas of sound. Because of the ear faculty, dharmas of sound arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of sound arise from the ear faculty. How is the ear faculty an empty dharma? Hearing and receiving are impermanent, arising and ceasing moment to moment—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of sound follow the emptiness of the ear faculty? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the ear faculty is extinguished, dharmas of sound are also extinguished; while the ear faculty is not extinguished, dharmas of sound are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from the nose faculty? Without the nose faculty, there would be no dharmas of scent. Because of the nose faculty, dharmas of scent arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of scent arise from the nose faculty. How is the nose faculty an empty dharma? Receiving all scents, arising and ceasing moment to moment—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of scent follow the emptiness of the nose faculty? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the nose faculty is extinguished, dharmas of scent are also extinguished; while the nose faculty is not extinguished, dharmas of scent are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from the tongue faculty? Without the tongue faculty, there would be no dharmas of taste. Because of the tongue faculty, dharmas of taste arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of taste arise from the tongue faculty. How is the tongue faculty an empty dharma? Receiving all flavors, arising and ceasing moment to moment—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of taste follow the emptiness of the tongue faculty? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the tongue faculty is extinguished, dharmas of taste are also extinguished; while the tongue faculty is not extinguished, dharmas of taste are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from the body faculty? Without the body faculty, there would be no dharmas of attachment. Because of the body faculty, dharmas of attachment arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of attachment arise from the body faculty. How is the body faculty an empty dharma? Receiving all textures, arising and ceasing moment to moment—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of attachment follow the emptiness of the body faculty? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the body faculty is extinguished, dharmas of attachment are also extinguished; while the body faculty is not extinguished, dharmas of attachment are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

How do dharma marks arise from the mind faculty? Without the mind faculty, there would be no dharmas of affliction. Because of the mind faculty, dharmas of affliction arise of themselves. Thus know that dharmas of affliction arise from the mind faculty. How is the mind faculty an empty dharma? Receiving all mental proliferations, arising and ceasing moment to moment—this is called emptiness. How do dharmas of affliction follow the emptiness of the mind faculty? Because their arising and ceasing are the same. For this reason, when the mind faculty is extinguished, dharmas of affliction are also extinguished; while the mind faculty is not extinguished, dharmas of affliction are not extinguished. Arising through dependence, rising and ceasing together, inseparable—this is all emptiness.

These sixteen dharma marks all arise from provisional causes and conditions; when the marks of causes and conditions cease, the dharma marks also cease. Thus know that all conditioned dharmas are empty. The reason is this: conditioned dharmas are subject to destruction and cessation, to arising and rising. When all beings attain the supreme fruit of the true and correct Dao, the substance of conditioned dharmas reverts to the unconditioned. Therefore, all conditioned dharmas are a great mass of emptiness, while all unconditioned dharmas are the profoundly still dharma, free from the realm of emptiness and existence.

The reason is this: if one speaks of emptiness, it can effect transformation; if one speaks of existence, it cannot be sought. This is the realm of neither non-existence nor existence. You who cultivate the dharma should cultivate the supreme, unconditioned, profoundly still dharma; do not practice conditioned dharmas of attachment to marks.

At that time, Haikong Zhizang again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "The Great Sage’s words are truly subtle. My mind still harbors doubts; I humbly request further explanation to attain thorough understanding. The Heavenly Worthy now says that conditioned dharmas are unreal in their marks, while unconditioned dharmas are not empty in their principle. Yet the conditioned dharmas we presently see have manifest real marks, their forms and qualities easily discerned, their movements and activities perceptible to reason. Why does the Heavenly Worthy today declare them empty? Unconditioned dharmas are secluded and profoundly distant, without trace or influence, impossible to contemplate or fathom with thought. Why does the Heavenly Worthy now declare them existent? These two paths seem contradictory, leading future beings astray—how should they cultivate to reach the true source of the Dao?"

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy replied to Haikong Zhizang, saying: "Do not harbor perverse doubts. If one clings to existence and attaches to marks, how can one seek the supreme and true Dao? A true adept should know that all conditioned dharmas in their marks and natures are subject to decay and destruction, without anything abiding permanently. Why is this so? All dharmas within the Three Realms arise through the power of sentient beings’ minds, and the nature of sentient beings is momentary arising and ceasing. Conditioned dharmas are likewise—momentary arising and ceasing. At the very moment of their arising, they are already marked by cessation; at the very moment of their existence, they are already marked by emptiness. Because they are not permanent, they are called empty. Unconditioned dharmas cannot be destroyed or measured. If there is a response, they manifest according to circumstances; if there is no response, they abide serenely and eternally. From this, you should understand: that which follows conditioned dharmas has the mark of cessation, and because it has the mark of cessation, it is called empty. That which has no successor cannot be destroyed, and because it cannot be destroyed, it is called existent. You should contemplate this and carefully discern the source of all wondrous dharmas."

Thereupon, Haikong Zhizang, having heard these words, awakened in his heart and attained great clarity. Rising from his seat, he knelt and bowed his head, addressing the Heavenly Worthy: "The explanation of emptiness and existence is truly extraordinary, profoundly aligning with the ultimate principle, beyond thought or conjecture. I shall uphold and practice it, spreading it throughout my worn and weary land. I only beseech the Heavenly Worthy to accompany me back to my kingdom today, employing your great spiritual power to transform and guide those who have not yet heard the teaching, delivering them all and bestowing the most excellent benefit."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy replied to Haikong Zhizang: "The time is not yet ripe; you should go first. I shall know the proper time and enter your kingdom to instruct and admonish the people, enabling them all to comprehend the boundless profound meaning."

Haikong Zhizang again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: "This is precisely the right time. I implore your compassion to enter that kingdom without hesitation." He entreated repeatedly, bowing without cease.

The Heavenly Worthy remained silent, then assented to his plea. Turning to his disciples, he commanded: "Prepare the various implements for the journey. Today, I shall accompany you and follow Haikong Zhizang into the Land of Ultimate Bliss to proclaim and perform the Dharma, delivering sentient beings, serving as a bridge of the Dharma, a ladder of the Dharma, a great illuminating torch, a great vessel and ferry, enabling all in the world to awaken and realize the fruit of the supreme and true Dao."

Having spoken these words, the Immortal Minister and youths stepped forward, bowed, and knelt, addressing the Heavenly Worthy: "Great Sage Heavenly Worthy, you discern the proper time and expedient means, skillfully assessing the myriad practices and varying capacities of sentient beings. Where transformation is possible, we rejoice greatly and shall diligently prepare the various implements."

Thereupon, they advanced and, through the power of their spiritual feet, manifested four hundred million true immortal Daoists. Each stood twelve feet tall, their bearing and appearance surpassing all, their dignity and beauty unmatched in the world. All wore dark crowns and jade-green sashes. Each immortal held a seven-jeweled lotus flower, twelve feet in height, their blossoms fully opened, fragrant and radiant, illuminating the entire kingdom with a crimson glow. Reciting the hidden verses of the sacred scriptures, their voices shook the world as they encircled the Immortal Minister as his retinue.

Upon entering the kingdom’s gates, immeasurable multitudes of faithful men and women lined the roads to welcome them, scattering flowers upon the ground until no space remained empty, the blossoms piling several feet deep. The incense they burned formed dense clouds in the sky, bringing coolness to travelers and relieving them of heat and affliction.

On that very day, they entered the Jeweled Assembly City. Within the city was a king named Good Seed, accompanied by his retinue, ministers, officials, and people numbering in the thousands of millions. Queen Good Seed also led the entire palace retinue, one hundred thousand in number. They prepared a lofty and expansive seat, adorned with rare treasures, the couch, mat, and curtains all exquisitely beautiful. The king and his ministers, along with the queen, each took their places on one side, sitting in silence to listen to the Dharma.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy and the true adepts ascended the seat and sat down. Their majestic spiritual power blazed forth, surpassing the world, their radiance towering and immeasurable. The Immortal Minister stepped before the assembly and proclaimed in a loud voice: "The Dao is not far. Those with deep aspiration need only earnestly seek to attain it. All of you, my retinue, now single-mindedly observe the dharmas of the body as illusory, magical, like lightning, like wind, without any true master, all subject to destruction. Why, then, do you drown in these decaying dharmas, deeply attached to the six senses, unmindful of the true Dao? When your life ends, your spirit departs forever, passing through the Three Paths, lost and cut off eternally, with no hope of emergence, sinking into the sea of suffering, enduring countless agonies—how can they be fully described? You should all know to depart from these calamities."

Having spoken these words, the entire assembly was seized with terror, trembling and sweating, at a loss for words. The Immortal Minister, seizing this opportunity, transformed his body into a vast ocean, boundless and immeasurable, without visible shores. He placed the assembly on one side, the Jeweled Assembly City remaining unchanged as before. Gazing across the expanse, they saw an island of extreme splendor, its jeweled terrace towering high, brushing the sun and moon above and obscuring the clouds below. The Immortal Minister stood upon the terrace, his appearance majestic, attended by an infinite retinue. Surrounding the terrace on all four sides were bottomless deep pools, their winds and waves surging to the heavens, shaking the sun and moon.

The Immortal Minister raised his hand and called out from afar: "Great King Good Seed and all your retinue, this vast ocean can wash away all defilements and obstructions, purifying and making flawless, accomplishing the supreme Dharma. If any among you are weary of the dust and filth and seek the Dao, you should enter these waters and receive my instruction."

Thereupon, the entire assembly, without distinction of men or women, removed their garments and competed to enter the water. Some, wading only to their knees, turned back, thinking: "How can this vast ocean be crossed? The far shore is not yet in sight. To drown in it would be of no benefit to the true Dao."

Some, wading only to their waists, turned back, thinking to themselves: "I have not yet gone far into these waters, yet the pearl of the sage already seems distant and unreachable. Why should I drown myself and vainly lose my life?"

At that moment, eight hundred thousand among the assembly thought: "This body and life are the root of all suffering, destined to decay and rot. Why cling to them? Nurturing the source of evil, even if we cannot reach the far shore, to drown in these waves is no loss."

Yet when they plunged forward and reached the other side, their resolve was not steadfast, and they could not enter the supreme Dharma gate.

Then, seventy-seven myriad and two thousand great worthies among the assembly thought: "I have heard the scriptures’ admonitions and followed the sage’s teachings—there is nowhere one cannot go. On the terrace of the far shore dwell divine powers and sagely virtue. With but a beckoning hand, we shall surely be delivered. My heart now knows no fear or hesitation." Filled with joy, they threw themselves forward with all their might. In an instant, they reached the far shore, and through the power of their resolve, they awakened to the true, unconditioned, supreme Dharma.

These seventy-seven myriad and two thousand great virtuous ones, having awakened to the Dao, radiated light from their bodies, illuminating all realms beyond. Then the Immortal Minister gathered his divine power and returned to his former state.

The awakened ones’ forms and appearances were transformed, astonishing the crowd. They said to one another in amazement: "Those who entered the water earlier—some drowned in the deep pools. How is it that today they appear thus?" Each marveled, sighing in wonder, and doubt arose: "Where now is the vast ocean of before? Those who drowned show no sign of it, yet their benefit is even greater. Such matters are unfathomable. If one were to hear their profound and wondrous essence, the heart would surely open in awakening, free from the net of doubt."

Then the Heavenly Worthy declared: "Let none among you doubt. The ocean just now was vast and measureless, its depths unfathomable. This was none other than the divine transformation of the Immortal Minister, not something truly existent. To discern the weight of all dharmas of joy and the measure of deliverance, he manifested this auspicious sign. You should know that those who cherish the true Dao and spare not their bodies or lives attain the greatest, boundless merit and fruit, beyond all reckoning.

All of you should know: I recall that in the beginning of the Dragon Han kalpa, there was a world called Ever-Joy. Its people were diligent in practice, observing long fasts and reciting scriptures day and night without cease. At that time, a Heavenly Worthy, also named Yuan Shi, dwelt in that world, expounding the wondrous Dharma of the Numinous Treasure. With compassion, he transformed the five directions, using the *True Writs and Sacred Talismans* to deliver all beings. All those multitudes received benefit. Later, at one time, he returned to the world of Ever-Joy to teach and guide all people.

Yet because their causal conditions were not yet determined, he displayed great divine power, raising his hand to screen the heavens. His radiance concealed itself, transforming into a mass of fire two thousand *zhang* high. He then manifested his own body within the flames. Through his divine power, his brilliance shone clearly in all four directions, visible to all without exception. From within the fire, he proclaimed the great Dharma sound: 'All you great assembly and retinue, if you seek long life, enter this fire and receive my teaching.'

At that moment, those of steadfast resolve spared not their bodies or lives and rushed into the fire to seek the Dao. Then Yuan Shi, within the flames, bestowed upon them the scriptures and vanished from sight. All attained the Dao of long life and deathlessness.

You, great assembly, should understand the meaning of the sage’s transformation of beings—its methods are not one. All serve to deliver the people of the world. Why is this so? Great fire and vast waters are places of terror, not to be lightly risked. If there are beings who do not shrink from suffering, who value the Dharma above their bodies and spare not their lives, know that such people, through the causal conditions of the Dharma, will never be stingy. They will reach the source of the Dao without slackening.

For this reason, those who entered the waters earlier all attained the fruit of the Dao, truly because their love for the Dharma was sincere and steadfast. You should know that the Heavenly Worthy Yuan Shi of former times is none other than today’s Immortal Minister. Those seventy thousand and more who attained the Dao in the past did so because in former lives they loved the Dharma and, rushing into the fire with unwavering resolve, never retreated. Today, seeing the ocean, they were able to plunge forward and accomplish the supreme, unconditioned practice."

When the Heavenly Worthy had spoken these words, all those who had earlier not entered the water aroused the great mind, awakening to the turning of no-sorrow. They lamented their former lack of resolve, having lost the root of the Dao’s lineage, and sighed: "What use is regret now?"

Then Haikong Zhizang arose, knelt, and praised: "The wondrous Dharma spoken by the Heavenly Worthy delves into the profound and extraordinary, bringing boundless benefit. All beings gain the ladder of the Dharma, reaching the realm of quiescence. Yet I still harbor a small doubt, and all in this great assembly share this perplexity. Thus, I repeatedly beseech the Heavenly Worthy: may you grant compassion and graciously resolve our confusion.

The Heavenly Worthy earlier spoke of a past-life practitioner of the Dao, the Heavenly Worthy Yuan Shi. This title is lofty and exalted, majestic and supreme, the great model for all things, revered by immortals and sages. Why then does he now occupy the position of a disciple, unable to attain the highest rank and deliver the world? By what causal conditions has he descended to such a station?"

Then the Heavenly Worthy smiled and replied: "Haikong Zhizang, do not harbor such deep doubts. I shall explain and distinguish this for you, that you may awaken and ascend to the supreme Dao.

Haikong Zhizang, the sage is unconditioned, yet for the sake of beings, he manifests conditioned activity. The sage’s mind is ever quiescent and still, yet because beings make different karmic connections, the sage’s responsive manifestations also differ in form."

Know then that the sage’s form cannot be fathomed or measured, for it takes shape only in response to the karmic connections of beings. Why is this so? When beings invoke this Great Sage Master, the Sage Master immediately responds with a corresponding form; when beings invoke this Secondary Sage Master, the Sage Master immediately responds with a corresponding form; when beings invoke this Lesser Sage Master, the Sage Master immediately responds with a corresponding form.
