The Sage Master’s mind remains ever unchanged; it is the karmic fruits of beings that differ in principle and effect.

It is like a sounding bell suspended in the void: though never struck, the potential for sound abides eternally. Why does the potential for sound abide eternally? Because it awaits the striker. When struck, a great striker produces a great sound, a moderate striker a moderate sound, a small striker a small sound—yet the essence of sound within the bell remains unchanged. Each sound differs according to the strike. The sage is likewise: the principle of his quiescence is uniform and unchanging, yet in response to beings, he manifests myriad forms in endless variety.

Haikong Zhizang, know that today all beings invoke me as their Great Master due to prior karmic conditions; they invoke the Immortal Minister Lad as their Secondary Master, also due to prior karmic conditions.

Then Haikong Zhizang addressed the Heavenly Worthy once more: "Earlier, you explained that the sage is unconditioned, yet manifests conditioned activity in response to the minds of beings, appearing in various forms according to their karmic connections. This principle is subtle and profound, its truth deep and recondite. Later, you further stated that all beings, by virtue of karmic conditions, invoke the Heavenly Worthy as their Great Master, and all beings, by virtue of karmic conditions, invoke the Immortal Minister Lad as their Secondary Master. We now wish to hear of these karmic conditions. We pray that the Heavenly Worthy will expound further, fully revealing the wondrous principle, that all in this great assembly may be fully enlightened and free from doubt."

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed Haikong Zhizang, saying: "Listen carefully now, and do not grow weary. I shall explain in full detail for you.

Do you not recall? In the distant past, eighteen thousand kalpas ago, there was a world called Square Citadel. Within this world stood a royal capital named Wondrous Ultimate, which is the present Land of Ultimate Bliss in the world of Square Citadel. Its land was level and smooth, without hills, pits, gravel, or thorns. All four directions were pure and clean. The world bore only sweet fruits, and all springs and pools were clear and sweet. All beings drank the water and ate the fruits without contention. Everywhere stood mountains of the seven treasures."

Those who sought anything would journey to these mountains, and their desires would be fulfilled the moment they wished, with nothing lacking. The beings there enjoyed bliss and freedom, free from all illness, their lifespans fixed at seven hundred years. When the time of death arrived, they would go to the burial grounds of their own accord and depart with parted sleeves.

In the Land of Wondrous Bliss there was a great king named Ruler of the Dharma, who was exceptionally wise and discerning, his talents and skills all-encompassing. His appearance was fair and upright, like the full moon, and his virtue and adornments were flawless in every way. The king had a thousand sons, all of them bright and astute, their various skills fully mastered, with nothing they did not comprehend.

King Ruler of the Dharma would often expound the wondrous Dao at midday, and his sons would attend him without ever leaving his side. All the people would likewise accompany him, never growing weary. Among these sons was a prince named Victorious Cause, the ninth in line, whose divine brilliance stood out uniquely, his fame surpassing all others. The other princes regarded him as the foremost.

When the great king lectured on the wondrous scriptures, if anyone in the assembly had doubts, there was a great minister named Advancing Goodness who, whenever anyone was entangled in the web of doubt, would consult Victorious Cause to seek clarification. Victorious Cause would then explain and distinguish the teachings, resolving all uncertainties so that everyone attained full understanding.

On days when the great king did not lecture, Advancing Goodness would petition the king to command Victorious Cause to expound in his stead. This continued for over six hundred years, and all the people of the land would often say: "We are fortunate to serve King Ruler of the Dharma, who establishes teachings and rules, propagates the Dao, and expounds the supreme fruit of the true and non-action. Though we enjoy such bliss, we daily hear what we have never heard before and see what we have never seen, and we are certain to achieve all wondrous sources. Yet our minds are sometimes dull and obstructed, giving rise to doubts and hindrances. Some things we fail to grasp, others we cannot resolve, leading to frustration and self-inflicted affliction. Fortunately, Victorious Cause dissects our deep doubts, elucidates the true principle, and awakens our minds to clarity, so that not a single matter remains forever obscure. These two sages guide and instruct us with profound kindness. We only wish that in the future they will forever serve as the great masters of the Dao for us. The great king is supreme, and Victorious Cause is next. All four kinds of beings will surely be spared the sufferings of the three evil paths, the five agonies, and the nine dark realms."

For this reason, the karmic reward of Prince Victorious Cause surpassed that of King Ruler of the Dharma. Why was this so? Though King Ruler of the Dharma proclaimed the wondrous teachings, there were those among the assembly who did not understand. Not only did they fail to cultivate wisdom, but they also accumulated boundless afflictions. Prince Victorious Cause, however, was able to dispel the afflictions of beings and establish the causes of wisdom. For this reason, his karmic reward was greater.

Haikong Zhizang, was King Ruler of the Dharma someone other than myself? I am he, and Prince Victorious Cause is now the Immortal Minister Youth. Advancing Goodness is your present self. Relying on our past lives, for having skillfully resolved afflictions and benefited beings, you first attained perfect enlightenment before me. At the beginning of the Dragon Han kalpa, you expounded the Dharma and taught beings, while I have only now, at the dawn of the Kaihuang era, ascended to the supreme fruit. The Immortal Minister Youth, having once assisted me in clarifying the subtle and wondrous teachings, and because all beings made vows, has now, in response to the inclinations of beings, manifested again in this land.

Do you now harbor doubts and thus have forgotten? Having spoken these words, Haikong Zhizang immediately recalled his past affairs, and all was restored without loss. He attained the wondrous Dao and, in this very lifetime, will achieve full and perfect realization, equal in power above, benefiting beings without limit.

Then Haikong Zhizang again bowed and, kneeling, asked: "The words the Heavenly Worthy has now spoken are most rare and subtle. May I inquire by what name this sutra should be called? What karmic blessings arise from upholding, reciting, and venerating it?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "This sutra was brought to fruition through your own initiation and guidance, and thus should be named *The Sutra of Haikong Zhizang*. It is also the gathering of all treasures, and should be called *The Adornment of the Seven Treasures*.

If any being in the world upholds even a single line or verse of this sutra, reveres and honors it, and enshrines it—whether in a brocade bag, an embroidered case, or a jeweled casket—with such offerings, then those who make such offerings will be loved and respected by all sentient beings in water, on land, and in the air. They will be venerated by countless deities, constantly protected and guarded, and will become fields of merit.

If any being can recite even a single phrase of this sutra, know that this person has entered the source of the Dao and will surely attain fruition in a future life. They will be able to recognize and read boundless scriptures, fully comprehend all written characters of beings, and penetrate the hidden texts of the heavens without obstruction.

If any being can chant even a single phrase of this sutra, know that this person has tread the root of the Dao and will surely attain fruition in a future life. They will be thoroughly versed in boundless wondrous meanings, clearly understand all celestial golden scriptures and true texts, and never forget them.

If any being transcribes this sutra, know that this person is a true companion of the Dao and will surely attain fruition in a future life. They will possess wondrous spiritual powers, be able to proclaim the great Dharma, and save and deliver beings.

If any being explains this sutra, know that this person has entered the nine transformations and will surely attain fruition in a future life. They will penetrate the profound and subtle, comprehend the wondrous meanings, resolve doubts for all people, benefit countless beings, and accomplish the great Dharma.

If any being reveres this sutra, know that this person has entered the mysterious realm and will surely attain fruition in a future life, possessing the thirty-two marks and a majestic, wondrous body.

If any being bows in worship to this sutra, know that this person has awakened to the nature of the Dharma and will surely attain fruition in a future life, obtaining a vajra body, firm and indestructible."

If any being praises this sutra, know that this person has already expounded the supreme and wondrous meanings. In a future life, they will surely attain fruition, their subtle and marvelous voice resounding throughout the infinite trichiliocosms. All beings who hear it will grasp the essentials of the Dao, and how much more so those who further receive, uphold, read, recite, transcribe, explain, reverently worship, praise, and proclaim it? The blessings of such a person are boundless, majestic and venerable, attaining the foremost realization.

O Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky, I recall that in the past three thousand kalpas, I constantly cultivated this Dharma with utmost sincerity, never slackening or retreating. Through this cause and condition, I have now attained the wondrous fruit of supreme wisdom.

You should now single-mindedly uphold and maintain it, accomplishing the formless, most supreme Dharma-body.

At that time, the Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: "I humbly inquire, what methods should one employ to receive and uphold such a wondrous scripture? I only wish for a thorough explanation, so that in future ages all may hear and know, obtaining great and excellent benefits."

Then the Heavenly Venerable replied: "Great Sage, you are indeed capable of this, striking the great Dharma-bell for all beings of the future, seeking the supreme resonance. Truly, this is compassion, bringing boundless benefit. I shall now explain its meaning and purport for you.

O Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky, this sutra is profound and wondrous, treasured and revered as most precious by all the great sages of the Mysterious Capital and Jade Capital. It is difficult to obtain and rare to encounter. Because your heart is earnest and single-minded, I today transmit it to you orally. You must receive it with utmost reverence and not lose it. If you proclaim it to the world, you must carefully select those who are fitting and only then may you impart it.

What kind of person is fitting? The essence of fitness comprises six principles. What are these six?

First, if there are practitioners who from their youth have entered the treasury of the Dao and Dharma, have already received and upheld the *True Writ of the Numinous Treasure*, thoroughly comprehend the profound and subtle purport of the *Cavernous Mystery*, and can explain its meaning without doubt or obstruction—only such persons may be imparted this teaching.

Second, if there are practitioners whose minds are not attached to the phenomena of conditioned dharmas, who skillfully discern the emptiness of the foremost meaning, thoroughly perceive the nature of dharmas, and see all as empty and quiescent, regarding self and others equally without notions of inner and outer; who, having understood in their own minds, can also teach others—only such persons may be imparted this teaching.

Third, if there are practitioners who diligently cultivate vigor, ceaseless day and night, not for their own sake but solely to deliver beings, sparing not their own bodies to benefit all things—only such persons may be imparted this teaching.

Fourth, if there are practitioners who skillfully uphold the precepts, their deportment complete, serving as models for all people; who teach and transform their disciples not with a mind burdened by attachment but constantly with the mind of the great and small formless Dharma, imparting all teachings—only such persons may be imparted this teaching.

Fifth, if there are practitioners who practice great forbearance, able to endure all insults and base treatment, ascribing good deeds to others while returning defilement and evil to themselves, their minds penetrating and thorough, not calculating self and other—only such persons may be imparted this teaching.

Sixth, if there are practitioners who skillfully contemplate the subtle, their powers of thought and mindfulness never scattered, single-mindedly and earnestly reflecting, diligently practicing the Dao and Dharma, penetrating the wondrous marks without clinging to self and other—only such persons may be imparted this teaching.

O Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky, know that only these six kinds of practitioners may be imparted what is spoken today. The reason is that these six kinds of persons can practice this Dharma, illuminate the wondrous teaching, and benefit and deliver beings. Therefore, you should impart this esoteric instruction to them.

If, however, there are those attached to conditioned dharmas, submerged in the six sense-contacts, unable to establish the causes of the supreme Dharma; or who deceive and delude themselves regarding what they see—such persons, upon hearing this wondrous teaching, will surely be startled and dismayed, exclaiming that it is unreal, generating various heterodox views, entangled in the net of doubt. Not only will they be unable to practice it, but they will also slander it. For this reason, you must not proclaim the *Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky*.

The merit of this sutra surpasses all other scriptures. The wondrous teachings of the Three Clarities and the supreme words of the Three Caverns do not compare to it. If there are worldly persons who disrespect these words, slight and scorn them, or generate slander, claiming that this sutra is not the teaching of the supreme sage, know that such persons are already companions of the three evil destinies and causes for hell. In this present life, they will inevitably encounter boundless terrors, afflictions, and bitter poisons. In future lives, they will endure burning, boiling, flaying, and roasting, suffering pains beyond measure, as the *Code of Illuminating Reality* clearly states without fail."

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable praised the matter as excellent and spoke these verses:

"O Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky,
Great indeed is the true adept,
Who emerges from this realm,
Virtue and conduct perfectly fulfilled,
Expounding the Dharma and delivering beings,
Boundless and measureless.
All revere and honor,
Heavenly and human beings praise as excellent.
Able to strike the Dharma-bell,
Able to beat the Dharma-drum,
Able to draw forth the Dharma-stream,
Able to proclaim the Dharma-teaching.
This is the root of the Dharma,
The bridge of the Dharma,
The ladder of the Dharma,
The nectar of the Dharma;
The father of beings,
The refuge of beings,
The life of beings,
The essence of beings.
Virtue and conduct fully possessed,
Majestic bearing manifest,
Speech and utterance,
Naturally harmonious and refined.
Coming to my presence,
Seeking the supreme Dharma,
Undeterred by peril and distance,
Unafraid of toil and hardship,
Seeking only the Dharma,
No other thoughts.
My heart rejoices,
And I utter wondrous sounds.
The two marks of emptiness and existence,
Clearly discerned and distinguished,
No more doubts or obstructions,
Washed clean and clearly explained.
All beings
Attain the true fruit,
Hell becomes cool,
Heavenly and human realms expand.
This Dharma is profound and recondite,
The refuge of all beings;
The immortals of the Jade Capital
All revere and practice it.
I now appoint you
As the Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky,
To expound this profound Dharma,
Having delivered the perfected person,
And also benefiting the great assembly.
You should know
That the Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky
Is your teacher,
Able to create for you
Great and excellent karmic merit."

You should all
Reverently prostrate and pay homage,
With earnest devotion and utmost sincerity,
To seek and receive this wondrous Dharma.
Their minds, wisdom, and eloquence
All respond without exception.
I now bestow in full
This supreme Dharma,
Entrusting and commissioning
The Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky.
You, the great assembly,
And all learners of future ages—
If any doubts arise,
You may consult and resolve them,
Naturally attaining awakening,
No more doubts or obstructions.
Bowing in reverence, they paid homage.

The Third Scroll of *The Supreme One’s One Vehicle Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky* concludes.

The Fourth Scroll of *The Supreme One’s One Vehicle Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky*
Universal Discourse Chapter

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed the Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky, saying: "Good son, in the kalpas of the distant past, I wandered through the Radiant Seven-Jewel Flower Grove, accompanied by a great assembly of sages—innumerable and boundless heavenly youths: the Youth of Majestic Light, the Youth of Moonlight, the Youth of Universal Light, the Youth of Jeweled Clarity, the Youth of Jeweled Form, the Youth of Jeweled Adornment, the Youth of Empty Treasury, the Youth of Empty Thought, the Youth of Empty Seal, the Youth of Right Mind, the Youth of Right Concentration, the Youth of Right Speech, the Youth of Right Compassion, the Youth of Right Giving, the Youth of Dragon Majesty, the Youth of Dragon Wisdom, the Youth of Dragon Flower, and the Youth of Dragon Virtue. Such multitudes, innumerable and boundless, formed My retinue as I expounded the Dharma.

At that time, there were also the Perfected of Pure Form, the Perfected of Pure Precepts, the Perfected of Pure Clarity, the Perfected of Dharma Kingship, the Perfected of Radiant Light, the Perfected of Wondrous Penetration, the Perfected of Wondrous Contemplation, the Perfected of Wondrous Wisdom, the Perfected of Wondrous Conduct, the Perfected of Universal Attainment, the Perfected of Universal Receptivity, the Perfected of Pure Fragrance, the Perfected of Pure Flower, the Perfected of Left Mystery, and the Perfected of Right Mystery. Such hosts, innumerable and boundless, formed My retinue as I expounded the Dharma.

At that time, there were also the Great Wisdom Immortals, the Great Brahmā Immortals, the Dharma-Upholding Immortals, the Vast-Giving Immortals, the Ever-Protecting Immortals, the Wondrous Conduct Immortals, the Wondrous Form Immortals, the Wondrous Adornment Immortals, the Wondrous Contemplation Immortals, the Compassionate Immortals, the Flying Heaven Immortals, and the Wisdom Light Immortals. Such multitudes, innumerable and boundless, formed My retinue as I expounded the Dharma.

At that time, there were also innumerable earthly immortals, including the Hundred Million Wondrous Dao Earthly Immortals who uphold and rely upon the true Dharma. Such hosts, innumerable and boundless, formed My retinue as I expounded the Dharma.

At that time, there were also the Daoist masters of the heavenly realms: the Daoist of Superior Form, the Daoist of Superior Wisdom, the Daoist of Eloquence, the Daoist of Diligent Recitation, the Daoist of Faithful Conduct, the Daoist of Precept-Holding, the Daoist of Incense-Holding, and the Daoist of Dharma-Teaching. Such multitudes formed My retinue as I expounded the Dharma.

At that time, the great kings of the nations, lesser kings, elders, good men, and good women all came to the seat to hear the Dharma.

Good son, I now turn the great Dharma wheel of this profound and true Dharma, extolling the root of the Dao, proclaiming and expounding the great compassionate Dharma rain. You, the fourfold assembly, should exert your very lives, bowing in reverence with single-minded devotion to receive and uphold it, entreating protection for all past, future, and present kin.

Thereupon, the fourfold assembly bowed their heads in unison to the Supreme Heavenly Worthy, their faith sincere and unwavering, ever abiding in the fruit of the Dao. Gazing up in admiration, they praised the inconceivable.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, moved by great compassion, radiated light from His entire body, universally illuminating the ten directions. His harmonious voice resounded with virtuous words, shaking the lands. The sound was like thunder, like a lion’s roar. His radiance shone boundlessly, compassion descending to the world, universally moistening all beings—whether human or non-human—all receiving benefit.

Thereupon, the fourfold assembly each rose to bow, prostrating in reverence and praising the subtle and wondrous virtues, manifesting forms never before seen in the world. The great assembly of the Heavenly Worthy guided them to the gate of good destinies, revealing the secret essentials. The precious treasury of the Dharma rain of the Empty Sky was sprinkled across the ten directions. The radiant forms stood majestic and resplendent, like the sun at dawn, like the moon among stars, universally illuminating the lands of the ten directions—beyond thought or measure.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy joyfully replied: "Excellent, excellent, good son! You and your retinue should listen single-mindedly, universally practicing the supreme treasury of the true Dharma, beholding the One Vehicle Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky, seeking the ultimate fruit, realizing the Dharma body, neither coming nor going.

You, My retinue, now contemplate thus: by taking refuge in the supreme Dao, you escape the thousand poisons of the sea of birth and death—beyond thought or measure."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, his heart suffused with great compassion, spoke in verse:

The Empty Sky knows no bounds,
Its form and response defy description.
The true nature abides eternally,
Expounding the constant and the inconstant.

I now open the ears of the deaf and eyes of the blind,
Taking refuge in the Great Compassionate Worthy.
For the sake of the Treasury of Wisdom of the Empty Sky,
The gateway of the Well-Gone One in the world.

It becomes the supreme medicine,
Universally bestowed upon the destitute and hungry ghosts.
By the power of wisdom and skillful means,
It is universally established among humans and gods.

The supreme true Dharma is proclaimed,
Its prophecy transmitted to descendants.
The profound scripture of the One Vehicle,
Discussed by immortals and the Dao.

Without form, without shadow,
It becomes the root of the field of merit.
With single-minded contemplation,
One ultimately attains the garden of true fruit.

The Perfected, youths, and others
Proclaim and penetrate the gate of the true Dharma.
Subduing all heterodox paths,
They perfect humans and immortal youths.

With the three karmas ever reverent,
Bowing to the compassionate and sagely teacher.
The Lord of the Great Dao of the Three Times,
Followed and understood according to one’s portion.

Only wishing for embrace and acceptance,
Attaining thorough penetration, forever unobstructed."

At that time, the Youth of Great Wisdom among the assembly, having heard the verse, single-mindedly bowed in reverence, joining his palms to pay homage. He addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Great Compassionate One, long have You adorned the distant past. The subtle seven treasures radiate light, universally illuminating Your body."

The one who skillfully comprehends the nature of dharmas,
Neither ceasing nor abiding.
Extolling the treasure of the Dao, its merits peerless;
Extolling the treasure of the Dharma, most boundless,
Its merits lofty and wondrous.
Further extolling the treasure of the teacher,
Who skillfully guides all beings,
Benefiting without obstruction,
Skillfully leading devas and humans—
Among devas, the world’s finest physician.
Deeply penetrating wisdom,
Skillfully employing expedient means.
All beings in samsara make offerings,
Gaining great benefit.
How could this be common or long-lasting?
Transcending the heavens with immortality.

Now my retinue,
Immeasurably rejoices,
Encountering the rare.
For this cause and condition,
I speak verses in praise:

Great wisdom opens the blind and dark,
All humans and non-humans.
Like the light of the sun of wisdom,
Discerning the false and true.
Universally attaining equal awakening,
The mind may extinguish without remainder.
Abiding in virtue, perfect wisdom,
Following the great compassion.
The nature of suffering beings,
Deeply understood, ascends the four classes.
Roaming and transforming the ten directions,
Expounding the Dharma to guide their minds.
The original body relies on the Dao’s wisdom,
Never violating the spirits of beings.
Understanding the supreme wisdom,
Not dwelling near birth and death.
Ever arising great compassion,
Not entering defiled dust.
Universally establishing expedient gates,
Naturally attaining the truth of the Dharma.
With body, speech, and mind,
I bow to the supreme benevolent one.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, with great compassion, addressed the Youth of Great Wisdom: "Good son, it is just so, just as you have said. Now your retinue, from immeasurable kalpas past, has gained the power of wisdom, skillfully comprehending the true King of Physicians. Good son, it is like fragrance completely dispelling all dust. Such fragrance does not come from without, nor does it arise from seeds. For this cause and condition, it is called habitual qi. Good son, it is like vajra: because the mind is unimpeded, it can dispel all delusions. Why? Because one contemplates the true Dao. Dispelling false delusions, like fragrance.

You should know that the Heavenly Worthies of the Three Times manifest wondrous forms, emitting great light that illuminates the ten directions and countless worlds. Yet all beings cannot see or hear it. Good son, it is like a foolish person born blind: though there is light, they never behold it. Those of unwholesome dharmas are likewise. Good son, all beings drowned in the sea of birth and death, clinging to sensual desire and affectionate bonds—through such causes and conditions, this city of afflictions, with its inverted arising and ceasing, covers their bodies. Their sins are boundless, entwined with the roots of afflictions. Today, I universally expound the treasury of the One Vehicle Dharma, enabling them to generate understanding and sever the defilements of afflictions.

Good son, it is like a person who obtains this wondrous Dharma and transmits it to all good men and women. Through this cause and condition, like a wheel-turning king, those not yet subdued are subdued; those already subdued are guarded and protected, never to waver again. Like the wondrous Dharma, those whose afflictions are not yet destroyed are enabled to destroy them; those already destroyed are prevented from arising again. For the benefit of all beings, I expound the three wisdoms as expedient paths, causing their afflictions to be forever extinguished without remainder. At one time, for all beings, with a single principle, I universally expound it, desiring that all beings—whether human or non-human—each gain wisdom and understanding, perceiving all immortals as like empty space. All myriad things fill it, for space is eternally one.

Good son, these divine worthies, for all beings, are likewise. These divine ones constantly abide in emptiness and quiescence, without employing the mind, manifesting bodies in the ten directions, displaying various wisdoms, expounding the Dharma to teach and transform, benefiting equally. Without hatred or love, without greed or desire, their merits are boundless. Benefiting birth and death, neither can obstruct; accomplishing compliance, they act as the wisdom of all for beings."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy spoke verses:

Excellent is the true mark,
Cause and effect, expedient means differ.
The three trainings and fruition,
Wisdom boundless in aspiration.
In the lands of the ten directions,
All see the youths in attendance.
Entering the city of empty space,
Faith’s benefits boundlessly heal.
This realm has no end or beginning,
All dharmas depend on their stations.
If there are Daoists
And those of great universal wisdom,
Dharmas abide in the treasury,
Able to act as seed-benefits.
This is called the adamantine Dao,
I constantly expound it.
Grasping and discerning coarse and fine,
Seeds eternally flow.
For the foolish and ordinary, I expound,
Do not cling and take it as sorrow.
Alone practicing ignorance,
Great compassion is vast.
Expedient means without distinction,
Also called nothing un-subdued.
No self, no clinging to marks,
A single lifetime without flow.
In the neutral of good and evil,
I should never cease.
Departing from the defiled mind,
Dust and filth cannot consume.
Without all this,
Neither poor nor rich.
Attaining the true meaning,
How could delusion and hindrance thrive?
Constantly practicing the One Vehicle Dao,
Name and essence alone are not fathomed.
Diligently contemplating without retreat,
This is called the wealth of kings.

At that time, Prince Sheng of the Square City, through the Youth of Immortal Ministers, heard the Heavenly Worthy expound the profound, subtle, and wondrous true Dharma: "Excellent is the Dharma-joy! Compassionately extolled, the supreme great teacher is thus rare—like the seven-jeweled flower, the purple-gold treasure flower, rare indeed, rare indeed!" Having spoken these words, Prince Sheng of the Square City, through the Youth of Immortal Ministers, opened his mind and gained understanding: the sea of the One Vehicle’s emptiness, the emptiness of no-emptiness, the emptiness of no-self, constant joy and self-mastery, subtle and complete, inconceivable.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, with the eye of wisdom, immediately addressed the Youth of Immortal Ministers, Prince Sheng: "Good son, the treasury of wisdom is like the great ocean: whatever comes to it, its taste remains constant. Though it is the refuge of many seeds, the water’s taste does not change or differ. All various things come to rely on it, yet the ocean’s water is likewise unchanged."

"Good son, the secret treasury of wisdom of the One Vehicle’s sea of emptiness is likewise thus. Abiding in the worlds of the ten directions, all sentient beings come and go as they please, yet this treasury of wisdom likewise waxes and wanes.

Good son, just as the form realm and the formless realm, and suchlike states, are either covered or uncovered—speaking of these two realms’ afflictions, they can never be attained.

Good son, though the sea of emptiness and the treasury of wisdom dwell within the city of birth-and-death and afflictions, the mind constantly contemplates the flavor of the One Vehicle’s meaning, expounding it for others, unfolding its profound significance. Body and mind are pure, like the formless realm, yet the three inversions repeatedly assail and harass. Even so, the formless realm is never defiled—likewise thus.

Good son, the sea of emptiness that emerges from the world brings great benefit and manifold virtues, like empty space, boundless and inexhaustible, empty and without possession. For this reason, emptiness is without end.

At that time, Prince Sheng of the Square City, the Youth of Immortal Ministers, bowed his head in reverence, gazed up at the guide before him, and spoke in verse:

Within and without, unclear,
In the two, only provisional names—
Neither real nor substantial,
Yet forming the seeds of dharma.
Thought after thought, both perish together,
Pursuing even to namelessness.
Determinedly observing causes and conditions,
Just as fruit arises from the tree.

Firm and untainted,
Forever parted from form and sound.
The ultimate pure dharma,
Expounded for sentient beings.
The six consciousnesses respond without fail,
The three destinies never afflict.
Thought after thought, not coexisting,
Clearly seeing the sea of emptiness and the city.

Within and without, these seeds,
Flourish throughout the three realms.
Seeds arise from continuity,
Their fruits ripen in fullness.
Like moistened seeds,
Sweet dew gives rise to all.
Without inner or outer conditioning,
How can there be the name of seeds?
Equal and without conditioning,
Fruits arise yet do not arise again.

What has been done and what is yet to be done,
Gain and loss enter demonic essence.
These inner and outer seeds of mine,
Give rise to sentient beings according to kind.
First, called conditioned consciousness,
Clearly receiving the welcome of the gods.
Second, called receiving consciousness,
The two paths of destiny already incline.
Following discourse, entering the treasury of emptiness,
The wise and dharma are both at peace.
The enlightened take it as their field,
Whether already arisen or yet to arise.
The good spiritual friend of cause and effect
Then departs from the city of the five demons.
Following transformation without end,
Neither ceasing nor eternal.
Cause and effect without distinction,
Transformation and guidance likewise without measure.
Responding to things with a mindless penetration,
The receiver is forever without misfortune.
Where do seeds arise?
Coming and going, discourse is not forgotten.
Whether human or non-human,
Who is not liberated in measureless numbers?
Difficult to extinguish, difficult to untie,
Expounding it causes others to flourish.
The minds of practitioners differ,
Dharma teachings are likewise not constant.
The pure person has not perished,
Yet the cloud chariot’s fruit is already ascended.
Accomplishing the pure land realm,
Attaining the wisdom of the pure Way.
Manifold vows and visions,
Universally seeing things without alarm.
Practitioners can accomplish,
Following their intentions to fulfillment.
What is grasped is only consciousness,
Attaining the Way in profound obscurity.
Consciousness of form, formless consciousness,
If what is known is not at peace,
Later consciousness does not arise,
Former consciousness alone does not proceed.
Without a body, abiding in empty space,
Tamed and without suffering’s affliction.
Liberated from the bonds of demonic error,
All fetters no longer arise."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, hearing the words of Prince Sheng of the Square City, the Youth of Immortal Ministers, said: "Excellent, excellent, good son! You are Prince Sheng of the Square City, the Youth of Immortal Ministers, decisive in the essentials of the Dharma. You have long accumulated practice, your merit and deeds are complete—thus you are called Prince Sheng. You have contemplated the supreme emptiness of the foremost discourse, the secret treasury of the sea of emptiness, with an unshaken body and mind. For this reason, you are named Sheng.

Good son, you are skilled in medicine, curing the sick with remedies, benefiting all sentient beings, whether human or non-human. For this reason, you are named Sheng.

Good son, you act as a guide, opening the treasury of the One Vehicle, transforming sentient beings, expounding for them the treasury of wisdom of the sea of emptiness, reciting, contemplating, and deeply penetrating its secret flavor and profound meaning. As a great compassionate father, you benefit sentient beings. For this reason, you are named Sheng."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy opened his mouth in a smile, and five-colored light radiated forth, filling the lands and great earth of the ten directions with immeasurable countries. A hundred kinds of tremors shook the ground, the five sufferings were all dissolved, lotuses bloomed in hell, a hundred kinds of fragrant incense arose, a thousand streams of pure water appeared, those burdened by sins received joy, and the dark were illuminated.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy again addressed the youth of true insight, Great Wisdom: "You have already realized the constant joy of the foremost meaning, the inconceivable, the treasury of wisdom of the sea of emptiness, and its profound virtues. Now I receive you, transformed into the Heavenly King of Great Wisdom. You are most inconceivable, skillfully accomplishing virtues, revealing the marks of the Dharma, benefiting all. Excellent, Great Wisdom! You are a child of the Dao, rare indeed, rare indeed!

Great Wisdom, you are truly the King of Physicians, reviving all children and curing all illnesses. A true field of good karma, neither barren nor defiled.

Good son, Great Wisdom, you have entered the Garden of Pure Fragrance and beheld the treasury of the One Vehicle’s sea of emptiness. Good son, it is like a person crossing the river or sea, not encountering evil winds, safely reaching the other shore. You are likewise: the sick are cured, the cold are clothed, the hungry are fed, the dead are revived, fathers, mothers, brothers, wives, uncles—separated for so long—suddenly meet again, leaping with joy.

You are likewise: having attained the pure eye of the Dharma, your power is unmatched, your wisdom unimpeded. You have penetrated the foremost emptiness, the treasury of the sea of emptiness. You benefit others without harming yourself.

Great Wisdom, your causes and conditions are long-standing, not something that can be praised or spoken of merely today."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy spoke in verse:

Excellent, supreme immortal of the Sea of Emptiness,
Expounding all dharmas to attain purity.
Benefiting all who practice the right path,
Compassionate and wondrous Dharma abides long.

Like a bright lamp or the light of sun and moon,
Or wisdom’s eye illuminating all beings.
Relying on the threefold understanding, one gains clarity,
Penetrating without obstruction, the Dao shines forth.

The Supreme Heavenly Worthy expounds the true Dharma,
The subtle Sea of Emptiness, the treasury of wisdom.
Excellent, the truth unfolds in due time,
Dispelling the afflictions of skin, flesh, and heart.

Such sacred words, this wondrous Dharma,
Can resolve subtle principles and enlighten beings.
If the mind is scattered and forgetful, one speaks thus,
Unaware of coming and going, past and future.

Good sons and good daughters, all reverently pay homage,
Revealing the true Dao of the supreme master.
Following the treasury of wisdom in the Sea of Emptiness,
Expounding boundless, excellent, and virtuous paths.

Wisdom illuminates, penetrating true principle without remainder,
Discerning for ourselves, we naturally understand.
With sincere hearts and hands clasped in reverence,
This is our self-realized Dharma, unshakable.

If one violates the mind’s Dharma and strays from the teachings,
Or slanders the sacred texts, losing the true Dharma,
Such practitioners wander lost,
Falling into the three evil destinies.

Like clothing dyed but not truly pure,
Like flowers bright in the morning yet withered by dusk,
They enter the dark hells of the five paths of suffering,
Assuming the form of hungry ghosts, endlessly starving.

Their wails and lamentations resound like thunder,
Striking terror into humans and non-humans alike.
By my great compassion, with but a snap of the fingers,
The three paths and five sufferings are instantly illuminated.

You see the past evil causes of yourselves,
Difficult to overcome, yet vows dissolve the fetters of sin.
Thus, those in the three paths and five sufferings
All at once behold the treasury of wisdom.

I proclaim the meaning of the Great Vehicle in a single phrase,
Abiding in the three realms as the Dharma’s decree.

When the Heavenly Worthy had spoken this verse, he addressed the Youth of Victorious Causes in Square City: "Good son, such scriptures are inconceivable. This Dharma serves as medicine for all beings, circulating in the world. Like the purple radiance of flowers, rare and wondrous; like the brilliance of the sun, the pure light of the moon—likewise rare and most delightful. Such flowers are exceedingly difficult to behold.

Good son, if you and others propagate this scripture, and in future generations even one person upholds it, all mighty spirit-kings and demon-kings will guard their body, ensuring no harm or loss. Why? Because this scripture possesses vast and far-reaching power, mighty and formidable, like a lion’s roar, like thunder shaking the earth, indestructible as vajra. Those who uphold this scripture will see great spirit-kings and demon-kings join their hands in reverence, their minds single-pointed, free from afflictions.

Such scriptures are expounded by the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion, the true teaching of the One Vehicle. For this reason, they benefit all beings. Why? Because faith in the true teaching gives rise to right practice. And why is that? From right practice comes right fruition, inconceivable, attaining the true Dharma. Thus, the true Dharma abides long in the world.

My heart pities the boundless, immeasurable multitude of beings, widely delivering and rescuing them through

If one does not cultivate the true Dharma of the Real Ground, they will be beset by sorrow, grief, suffering, and affliction—all impermanent ills—bound to birth and death, with afflictions clinging to the body.

Good son, if there are beings whose minds attain clear vision of majestic wisdom and power, who can subdue what is hard to subdue, see what is hard to see, hear what is hard to hear, and practice what is hard to practice, they will perceive all dharmic appearances with sovereign freedom, yet without discrimination. For this reason, they become undivided and non-differentiated, replete with merit and virtue.

Then the Heavenly Worthy spoke these verses:

I expound the meaning of the Real Ground,
The rare and supreme Dharma,
Pervading the most excellent principle,
Ever-flowing and ungrasped.
Without distinction, without defilement or purity,
Variously explained through discriminations.
Neither increasing nor diminishing the wisdom of all modes,
The meaning of refuge in sovereign freedom.
Sovereign action yields great benefit,
Cultivating the radiant and wondrous honored one.
Emptiness and existence are without divided being,
Just as the nature of the world.

When the Heavenly Worthy had finished reciting the verses, he again addressed the youth of Victorious Causes in Square City: Good son, in the distant past, before I had realized the transcendental scriptures and teachings, I now begin to attain boundless causes and conditions, filled with great joy and ceaseless delight. By practicing this sutra, contemplating its meaning and flavor, I gradually perfect all beings.

Good son, the Treasury of Oceanic Emptiness and Wisdom, for the sake of all beings, adapts to their root capacities. With the rain of Dharma, I constantly pour forth, able to dispel the scorching heat of afflictions in beings, to wash away the dust and filth of the three obstructions, to nurture the single-vehicle roots of goodness in beings, and to benefit all—whether human or non-human.

Good son, it is like sweet rain that moistens all things, whether mountains or marshes, high or low. All grasses and trees receive its benefit without exception.

Good son, it is like rice grains that sprout stems, grow flowers and fruits, and yield sweet dew, bestowing nourishment in all directions. All beings are sated without exception.

Good son, I now expound the causes and conditions of good action, universally enabling all beings to cultivate and grow the single-vehicle Treasury of Oceanic Emptiness, just like this.

Good son, you should bestow this Dharma, expounding for others the secret treasury of the single-vehicle Ocean of Emptiness. Contemplate its meaning and flavor, teach the meaning of emptiness, so that all beings—whether good sons or good daughters—may arouse the mind of dedication, prostrate before the Three Jewels, reverently touch the honored feet, generate manifold thoughts, and form manifold intentions. Exhausting all they possess, with single-minded reverence, they offer fine blossoms and fragrant incense, presenting these in devotion and making open confession.

Good son, by such contemplation, this brings great benefit. The body becomes adamantine, forever unshakable, abiding as the Heaven among Heavens, ever dwelling in the Pure Land, attaining the subtle and wondrous fruit.

Then the Heavenly Worthy again spoke in verse:

Excellent, good son,
Victor of Square City, master of Dharma causes.
Skillfully requesting the true teaching,
Benefiting self and others.
I now speak for you,
Think well and receive it with care.
If good sons and daughters
Revere and uphold it with devotion,
Sweet dew pervades the empty body,
And they ascend to heaven in broad daylight.
But if men or women
Deceive with perverse minds and slander,
They contract red disease in life,
And at death fall into the bottomless hell.
Those who practice this sutra
Purify themselves like blue lotuses.
Through wisdom and faith,
They bow to the true and real meaning.
Mindfully invoking the universal teacher,
They ascend the city of afflictions.
For this reason,
They contemplate all dharmas as universally empty.
The wisdom of the Dao is pure,
A fine field of blessings for the world.
Those who hear the wisdom of the Victorious Teacher
Are like great physicians.
They heal the sick child,
Dispelling all afflictions.
Victor of Square City, youth of supreme wisdom,
Because of the Treasury of Oceanic Wisdom,
You are like a magically born king.
This is the foremost rarity,
Good sons, for you.
Like the magically born great king,
These causes and conditions are long-standing.
Therefore, I teach this Dharma,
To practice goodness and enter therein.
Vast as the empty earth,
It perfects the king of the world.
The pure and subtle fruit,
Good sons, is for you.
You are the teacher of the world,
With utmost sincerity, you should bow in reverence.
Seek the fruit of the eternal Dao,
Assembly of disciples on the sacred path.
You act as the world’s refuge,
As medicine for the world.
In total, you cure the arrogant and haughty,
Who abandon compassion and forsake cultivation.
Long sunk in the three paths,
Even after ten thousand kalpas, remorse is useless.
You speak of what is beneficial,
But the true principle is not what they realize.
True persons, youths, and others,
Rely on the radiance of the sun.
Illuminating all dharmic appearances,
Unmoving and transcendent.
I proclaim equally,
The true meaning of the true Dharma.
Like the pure sun and moon,
Profoundly illuminating all things.
This is my reliance on the scriptures,
Enabling the wise to enter.
With humble mind, arise in reverence,
For the subtle and hard-to-fathom Dharma.
Skillfully knowing without attachment,
Beneficial to the eight worldly concerns.
The mind is ever without defilement,
Spoken of as unobstructed renown.
Ever compassionate, ever upholding,
Known by humans and devas alike.
Bow at the feet of the great teacher,
Who discourses on the constant and inconstant.
Pouring forth the sweet dew of medicine,
Relying on and understanding according to capacity.
Like a feathered bird,
You peruse the city of concentration in order.
Selecting and embracing the Great Vehicle,
May these words bring benefit.
Disseminating to those in the sea of suffering,
To the Dharma persons and the meaning of Dharma.
Nature, summary, and extensive names,
From impurity to ultimate purity.
Thus called the peerless king,
Who thoroughly understands the goodness of the Dharma realm.
Attaining birth in the eternal Great Dao,
Through conditions of supreme penetration.
Neither forgetting persons nor dharmas,
Through the knowledge of non-discrimination.
From the wisdom of non-inversion,
As the Dao is broadly expounded.
The good Dharma established for peace,
The essence of cultivation and wisdom.
The two wisdoms dwell in tranquil repose,
Like the measureless and boundless.
The misfortunes of a hundred thousand kalpas,
Constantly cultivated in accord with number.
Now, having attained the wheel-turning king,
If one can skillfully cultivate the Dao,
In a single thought, all is perfected,
Like the Brahma devas.
Attended by the power of the Heavenly Worthy,
Universally manifesting manifold doors.
Attaining boundless and constant seeds,
Within the expedient means of the Dao.

Perceiving the eternally formless,
Names and meanings become mutual guests.
The true person should constantly practice,
In the two contemplations ever reflecting.

Ascending yet without grandeur,
From this arises true wisdom.
Attaining departure from dust’s increase,
As one sees all as non-existent.

Entering the uncollapsing,
The true person remains ever pure.
Neither delighting nor glorying,
Abandoning external dust-marks.

Entering the city of wisdom’s treasury,
What is grasped is non-existent.
Gradual expedient means arise,
Benefiting without obstruction.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken this verse, addressed Śubhahetu:
"Good son, if there are beings who contemplate the emptiness of all dharmas—
all emptiness, the emptiness of emptiness—
there is no self, nor world, nor even empty emptiness.
For example, when beings wish to perceive forms,
the prior form is already empty, the subsequent form is also empty;
this is called empty emptiness.
In a single moment, countless afflictions arise, and so it is likewise.

Good son, first cultivate the lesser Dao, and when the lesser Dao is empty,
then cultivate the middle Dao;
when the middle Dao is empty, then cultivate the higher Dao;
when the higher Dao is empty, through this condition,
this is called empty emptiness.
Through this emptiness, one abides in constant bliss and non-action.

Good son, it is like a goldsmith refining pure gold:
first removing coarse impurities, then fine dust,
until it is called hundred-times refined true gold.
Good son, refining body and mind to seek the supreme Dao is likewise.

Good son, this is called expedient means.
Through its lack of fixation,
and because of this lack of fixation,
the true person and divine youth may accomplish the subtle Dao and dharmas at will,
responding to conditions as they wish, and abiding long therein.

Good son, those not yet attained are enabled to attain,
those attained are enabled to fulfill,
and those fulfilled do not regress.
In present and future lives,
wherever they are born and wherever they practice,
they receive manifold benefits.

Good son, all beings who practice thus
are replete with merit and virtue.
When the Heavenly Worthy appears in the world,
they hear the true Dharma—
this is called the supreme birthplace.
This arises from concentration.

The true person and divine youth,
in the supreme birthplace,
attain a dwelling and abode,
using it at will without regression or deviation,
their fame pervading the two vehicles.
All beings—human and non-human—
with one mind gaze upon the supreme birthplace of the true person and divine youth,
and must attain the wondrous and autonomous land,
transforming other lands,
without going or coming,
without birth or extinction,
autonomous and unimpeded,
abandoning birth and desiring birth,
once born, abiding in attainment.

Good son, according to the duration of their abiding,
they abandon birth and abandon extinction;
according to their births and lives,
they desire birth and desire extinction,
responding to conditions with discernment,
enabling unimpeded divine powers.

Good son, all beings in the boundless worlds,
dwelling in the city of afflictions,
each seeking birth after birth,
craving desire and clinging to form—
through these conditions,
they are born and extinguished, extinguished and born,
constantly born, constantly extinguished,
revolving in birth and death.

Out of my love for them,
I manifest unimpeded,
through the original vow of the true person,
the power of non-discrimination,
divine powers as they wish,
proclaiming the great essential Dharma to all beings,
enabling those who have not seen or heard to see and hear.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, with great compassion,
composed his countenance, observed the conditions,
and responded to each according to their karmic connections,
then emitted radiant light,
illuminating the lands and worlds of the ten directions,
enabling all sentient beings with karmic affinity to fulfill their aspirations
and listen to the Dharma in peace.
Thus, he emitted light,
illuminating prisoners, hungry ghosts, and hell-beings—
whether kin or not—
all beheld,
and all beings saw the hells of the nine darknesses in the ten directions.

They further saw the Heavenly Worthy expounding the Dharma,
his voice pervading empty space,
manifesting as gods and humans,
transforming and delivering beings,
responding to conditions with universally manifested divine light.

The Heavenly Worthy, seated upon a precious lotus,
surrounded by manifold lights,
expounded the Dharma,
delivering beings with great kindness,
pervading the measureless realms,
manifesting various forms
to deliver all from suffering.

All these beings,
each according to their wishes,
received the true Dharma—
the wondrous One Vehicle, the treasury of sea-like emptiness and wisdom,
its merit majestic and inconceivable.

Good son, the power of divine majesty
transforms according to consciousness,
swift as lightning,
coming and going with speed beyond compare.
If even one person beholds the true realm,
tranquil and non-active,
in a single thought awakens the supreme Dao,
their mind never regressing,
all karmic defilements completely eradicated.

Good and evil karma both arise from the mind;
when the mind is empty, mental consciousness is also empty;
when mental consciousness is empty, transformation is also empty.
Through this condition,
the mind’s consciousness transforms swiftly,
surpassing the speed of wind,
difficult to see, difficult to hear.
This arises from the mind’s activity,
instantly accomplishing what is contemplated.

Such a mind,
contemplating the absence of self,
can encompass all.
Good son, it is like a mirror’s reflection,
reflecting both large and small,
nothing unseen.
My mind’s perception is likewise.
All that exists—
so very, very much—
all appears within this body.

Good son, deluded beings cling to delusion without return,
firmly attached to false doctrines.
I observe their conditions,
like a vajra guard,
enabling them to know past lives,
causes and conditions.
Some are born in famine,
some in times of disease,
some with illness and medical treatment.
Just as the true person receives peace and bliss,
I universally enable all beings
to attain equality.

Good son, if there are those with faith,
insatiable in goodness,
seeking only the Dharma,
with nothing cherished,
I shall assist and encourage them,
proclaiming the One Vehicle treasury of sea-like emptiness,
dispelling the burning city of beings’ afflictions—
like a raging fire, unbearable and invincible.
If there are beings who seek perfection,
their minds untiring,
abandoning evil and advancing in goodness,
single-mindedly upholding,
knowing when to cease evil,
insatiable in goodness—
such is the mark of the Dharma.
I shall proclaim it for them."

"Good son, now your retinue should single-mindedly awaken the great wisdom of the Mahāyāna, transcending both existence and non-existence. Through this cause and condition, existence and non-existence become empty and pure. When the root consciousness is extinguished, it too is empty. Because the root consciousness is empty, the marks of dharmas arise in continuity.

Good son, if there are beings who can do this, they will shatter all delusions. Why is this so? The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy adapts to the faculties and afflictions of all beings, manifesting in various subtle and wondrous dharma-marks. Whether human or non-human, if even one person clings to the view of emptiness, not departing from the empty dharma, they will doubt the true Dharma. In this present life, they will gain nothing from emptiness. If one contemplates this Dharma, proclaiming it as one with the true reality, like a single flavor, they will attain peace in this life and accomplish the fruition of the Way.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy again addressed Prince Victorious Cause of the Square City: Good son, in measureless kalpas past, you cultivated the treasury of wisdom of the One Vehicle’s sea-like emptiness. Through this cause and condition, you have now realized the subtle and wondrous merit of the treasury of wisdom of the One Vehicle’s sea-like emptiness. Truly a King of Physicians—rare indeed, rare indeed! Your name is Victorious Cause, for you possess excellent methods and arts, healing the children and expounding the roots of goodness. For this reason, your name is Victorious Cause.

Good son, you have vast vows and perfect merit. What are these vast vows? First, the constant vow: to make great offerings, always offering to those of supreme merit and to the Dharma-teachers. Second, the constant vow: that I and others single-mindedly uphold the supreme and wondrous true Dharma. Third, the constant vow: to turn the great Dharma-wheel, always turning the wheel of Dharma in the great assembly. Fourth, the constant vow: to cultivate the vow of practice, always expounding the Dharma, so that all sages, true persons, and youths universally hear and see it. Fifth, the constant vow: to perfect all beings in the realm, so that they attain peace and the roots of goodness of the Three Vehicles. Sixth, the constant vow: to serve with the vow of the mind, that the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy abides in all lands, seeing all Daoists with constant reverence, listening to and receiving the true Dharma. Seventh, the constant vow: to attain a pure land, establishing the Dharma-teaching, cultivating and protecting mindfulness, so that all these beings attain peace. Eighth, the constant vow: never to depart from all beings, never to depart from the immortal Dao, practicing diligently together with true persons and youths. Ninth, the constant vow: to benefit all universally, sheltering them without fail. Tenth, the constant vow: to awaken to the true Way, transforming all beings to attain the same true fruition.

Good son, those who cultivate these ten subtle and supreme vows will ascend to the supreme ground and attain accomplishment. Why is this? Because such vows truly lead to the attainment of a pure land. Good son, I have already attained this pure land, thus emerging from the defiled land of birth and death.

Good son, it is like the Dragon King’s twelve links of dependent origination: sometimes arising from non-arising, sometimes non-arising from arising; sometimes arising from arising, sometimes non-arising from non-arising, or neither arising nor non-arising—each expounded according to what is fitting for beings. Good son, there is also dependent origination where dharmas with marks are called defiled, and dharmas without marks are called pure.

Good son, you should now know that the supreme and true matter of the wondrous true Dharma speaks of true reality and truth. How then does one speak of true precepts? Good son, these true precepts are where the *Eight Essentials* and the *Four Illuminations* converge as one. Your retinue should all contemplate this sutra, exploring its profundities. You should attentively uphold its subtle and intricate meanings. The single pure precept is the precept of nature, inherently and constantly pure. It can uphold what has been violated; once the mind confesses and reveals, purity is restored.

Next, you should observe: first, pure faith; second, pure mind; third, pure body. Awakening the supreme Way, body and mind become pure. This is the beginning of clarity and conduct, the origin of all practices. Because of this purity, great compassion arises, and all practices are undertaken. The Dharma of the Way is seen clearly, without obstruction. Through true understanding, the subtle origin is penetrated, and true principle is realized. Realm and wisdom are without discrepancy—this is called the Way. Why is this so? Because the true Way is realized. The Way responds with transformed bodies, and one should receive the teaching master.

Good son, those who uphold the true teaching and cultivate the true practice are called supreme and foremost guides, universally enabling beings to mature and understand the marks of the Way. Through various aspirations and vows, they lead all beings to seek the true and spontaneous fruition of the Way, inspiring all future beings to delight in propagating the supreme Way. They expound the treasury of wisdom of the One Vehicle’s sea-like emptiness, enabling all beings to awaken to equal benefit—rare indeed, rare indeed! Abiding in merit, they strengthen their own bodies, departing from the five dusts, relinquishing attachment and clinging, guarding their faculties, and dwelling in the unshakable realm of the supreme heavens’ constant bliss.

Good son, if there is one who relinquishes attachment and clinging, guarding the six senses and preventing evil, this person will dwell in the four fruits of mindfulness. Through mindfulness, they will thoroughly understand the profound and wondrous Dharma, without doubt or slander. Their mind will be like a lotus, radiant amidst the dust, unstained by defilements, free from thoughts of attachment and love. If one contemplates this form as empty and without substance, like a magically born prince of the great king, all virtues are pure. Born in the land of the Way, they can subdue others with the power of their virtue, seeking the Dharma and leaving the household life. Body and mind are pure, departing from the city of afflictions, ascending to the upper realms, personally attending the Divine Worthy. They deeply understand that all dharmas are empty, pure, neither existent nor non-existent, neither pure nor impure.

Why is this? Because all beings have not yet attained the understanding of emptiness. Due to the twofold contemplation of existence, they have not yet attained the subtle and profound power of samādhi and wisdom.

Good son, now that your retinue has left the household life, if you develop attachment to the profound and wondrous Dharma you have attained, because of this attachment, you will not attain purity."

Why is this so? The pure and correct Dharma has no place of existence. If one clings to the notion that dharmas possess distinct characteristics, attachment arises. Good son, this is impossible. Such attachment is the activity of ignorance—what is called "volition" is action, and action is karma. The true person, the youth, rightly cultivates the six practices, contemplating birth and death, yet has not yet relinquished them. Through abundant cultivation, one grows weary of all evils; through conditioned arising and cessation, one generates aversion toward all evils. This perception, like emptiness, has no basis and cannot endure. Each and every dharma possesses distinct meanings, yet one has not fully understood them. All beings speak differently, their causes and conditions each unique.

Good son, the Dao, through its Dharma gates, encompasses immeasurable and boundless categories of dharmas. Some take the five aggregates as a Dharma gate to embrace all dharmas. The faculties of beings are as if in the palm of one’s hand. Dull-rooted beings cannot deeply receive it. The true person, the youth, by the power of wholesome dharmas, expounds this profound teaching, enabling them to receive the supreme correct Dharma. He teaches immeasurable meanings with skillful means, wielding majestic and sovereign virtue. Again, with immeasurable and subtle correct Dharmas, he instructs in all the boundless Dharma gates. For this reason, they are immeasurable and infinite. Names, phrases, and meanings are likewise immeasurable and infinite. Subtle phrases and meanings perfect beings’ supreme eloquence. Regarding what is not difficult, they conceive difficulty, establishing all manner of challenges to confound others, leaving them unable to respond. If one answers, it enables them to attain understanding.

The ocean of emptiness, the Dao, and its fruition take the Dharma as their body. What is the Dharma-body? It has many meanings. All dharmas of the three times, whether existent or non-existent—good son, this is the gate of skillful means, the gate of great wisdom. If there are beings who lack faith, teach them the One Vehicle, the ocean of emptiness, the treasury of wisdom, cherishing and upholding it. For those who have not planted wholesome roots, nurture them with loving-kindness, strengthening their wholesome roots so all may attain accomplishment, benefiting all who have not yet accomplished, enabling them to accomplish; those not yet liberated, enabling them to attain liberation. Thus, skillful means are established in the world.

Good son, just as great wisdom augments virtue and enhances wholesome power, you have skillfully exhorted countless beings, urging them to vigorous diligence, resolutely arousing the aspiration to forever extinguish afflictions, never to arise again. Good son, Radiant Wisdom Victorious, you are rare indeed; the Dharma Realm King is also rare; the Transformation-Born Great King is also rare. Harmonious wholesome roots, beings of great wisdom—rare in the world; the Ocean of Emptiness Wisdom Treasury is also rare; the Wholesome Seed Great King is also rare.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, with the eye of great compassion, spoke these verses:

The victorious cause of the Dharma citadel
Arises from the Dharma’s manifold nature.
Thus, among the Heaven of Heavens,
There is no Dharma of existence.

Excellent is the subtle and wondrous Dharma,
Contemplating the emptiness of form’s inherent nature.
Great emptiness and small emptiness—
Both are without existence.

Originally, there is no existent Dharma,
Yet beings, through deluded thought, conceive it so.
Thus, regarding all dharmas,
The victorious cause of the Dharma citadel:

All classes of beings
Depend on the mind’s discriminations.
Like emptiness, neither empty nor existent,
Without action, without attainment.

Not by "emptiness as emptiness,"
Is form’s emptiness non-form.
Then arises non-discrimination,
No form, no empty Dharma.

Thus, form is precisely emptiness;
If form and emptiness were distinct,
The essence of emptiness would not hold—
How could it be established or not?

For example, conditioned dharmas
Do not differ from the eternal.
If one discerns their nature,
This is called emptiness.

Emptiness is then form’s emptiness—
How can form’s emptiness be empty?
Form’s characteristics are without existence,
Yet this is both existence and emptiness.

Form’s emptiness is precisely form,
Without any non-discrimination.
This emptiness is precisely form,
Emptiness, form, emptiness, emptiness, emptiness.

True nature cannot be spoken,
As if born from a pure land.
Not apart from form is emptiness,
Thus emptiness does not become form.

Form’s essence is like empty space,
Hence named "emptiness of emptiness."
If emptiness and form were distinct,
Conditioned form would differ from truth.

There would be no meaning in sagehood,
Emptiness could not dispel form.
No meaning in leaving the ordinary,
If bound to discriminative appearances.

Then arises the impure,
If bound to true reality,
It should become pure—
Thus, emptiness cannot be spoken.

What makes form "form"?
Only the name is form.
Great indeed, good son,
If apart from name, empty form.

Truly, there is no inherent emptiness,
This is self-nature’s non-arising.
No cessation, no profound purity,
This form is without existence.

With arising comes defilement—
Thus, form has no separate characteristic.
Through "without existence," it pervades,
Opposed to the provisional to establish names.

This is the work of the illusory,
Opposed to all named discriminations.
All dharmas are fundamentally empty,
Provisionally establishing appearances.

According to conditions, dharmas are expounded—
Thus, all names are like this.
The true person sees nothing,
Not seeing, nor does it arise.

This is called the peerless pair,
By this, it is spoken as the cause.
Without division, without distinction,
Extinguishing all discriminative delusions.

Name and Dharma are not distinct,
All existent dharmas—
Form’s emptiness is not empty,
Emerging as the seed.

Entering, it is without-nature arising,
Possessing this signless principle.
The Vajra Eye of the Dharma Realm
Has no wisdom prior to names.

Many names and indeterminacy
Fulfill meaning through shared essence.
Many mixed, distinct characteristics—
Through signlessness, already existent.

Without defilement yet with purity,
Thus, it is like empty space.
Through this emptiness, the Dharma is empty,
Without self-nature or other-nature.

True reality is also absent,
Like an image in a mirror.
What is seen is without existence,
Yet wholesome and unwholesome bodily karma arises.

Form follows shadow like shape,
Like echoes coming and going.
Like light and reflections,
Like the moon in water.

The water holds nothing,
The tranquil mind is likewise.
Thus, no analogy exists—
This is the supreme Dao.

Skilled in worldly affairs,
Excellent, great sagely master.
Distinguishing and expounding the profound and hidden,
Those who awaken to the One Vehicle attain realization.

At that time, having heard the Celestial Worthy recite this verse, Great Wisdom questioned the Youth of Victorious Causes of the Jeweled Citadel: "By the great compassion of the Celestial Worthy, the rain of Dharma has poured forth these words and the place of their teaching. Excellent, Youth of Victorious Causes of the Jeweled Citadel, for what meaning did the Celestial Worthy of Great Compassion speak thus? Though the Celestial Worthy traverses all heavens in every place, how does he not perceive birth and death? In the past, within *paratantra*-nature, dependent upon true reality, the coming and going of birth and death held no distinction in meaning. I wished to inquire but dared not speak. Excellent, Perfected One, Youth of Victorious Causes of the Jeweled Citadel, I only hope that you and the great kings will proceed to the Worthy One’s abode to request the resolution of these doubts. What is the intent?"

At that time, the Youth of Victorious Causes of the Jeweled Citadel replied to Great Wisdom: "Excellent, Dharma Master. I constantly contemplate the subtle and wondrous true Dharma, aspiring to propagate and uphold it. Now that you have deigned to ask, it is most fitting for one of your virtue." Thereupon, excellent indeed, they hastened together to the seat of the Celestial Worthy, King of the Dharma of Radiant Golden Light and Supreme Faith. Making obeisance and paying reverence, they addressed the Celestial Worthy: "We only hope the Celestial Worthy will take pity and answer us."

At that time, Great Wisdom further addressed the Celestial Worthy: "All sentient beings, whether with karmic conditions or without, from whence do they come? Whether eternal or impermanent, from whence do they come? The characteristics of emptiness and existence—apart from eternal and non-eternal, do the principles of scripture and reason separate? Is what is seen as form considered conditioned and possessing form, or is it formless? At that time, the Celestial Worthy joyfully replied: "Excellent, excellent, good man. What you now ask is truly no question at all; what you now speak is truly nothing spoken. Now listen carefully and sit according to your station. I shall tell you of the original causes and conditions of the past. Good man, where the impermanent is spoken of as non-impermanent, and where non-impermanent is spoken of as neither impermanent nor non-impermanent, relying on the meaning of signlessness to expound the eternal Dao—this is called the impermanent. Good man, the characteristics of *paratantra*-nature arise from true reality; the partial abiding arises from the nature of discrimination. Thus, nature is also impermanent. From the division of these two natures, neither impermanent nor non-impermanent, the meaning of eternal and impermanent is spoken as non-dual, suffering and joy as non-dual, good and evil as non-dual, empty and non-empty as non-dual, self and no-self as non-dual, pure and impure as non-dual, nature and non-nature as non-dual, arising and non-arising as non-dual, cessation and non-cessation as non-dual. Why is this so? Because through these distinctions of perception, one sees the eternal and non-eternal, sees joy and non-joy, sees purity and impurity, sees emptiness and non-emptiness, sees nature and non-nature, sees suffering and non-suffering, sees cessation and non-cessation. Because of this perception, all views harmonize into one; because of this one view, what is seen is no seeing, nor is there non-seeing. The seeing of no-seeing follows sentient beings. Speaking of eternal and non-eternal, decisively understanding the two natures, the coming and going of quiescence and extinction."

At that time, the Celestial Worthy recited a verse:

"Bridge-like, good man,
Great Wisdom, supreme master.
The true rarity of all dharmas
Is like their manifold appearances.
Revered by all sages,
Through this Dharma and non-Dharma.
Without this Dharma and non-Dharma,
Supreme good man.
This is the unconditioned Dharma,
Thus the non-dual meaning is spoken.
Depending on one aspect, it is said
To be existent or non-existent;
Depending on two, it is said
To be neither existent nor non-existent.
Because it manifests, it is not non-existent,
Thus it is not spoken of as eternal;
Because it reveals true reality,
Thus it is spoken of as not non-existent.
By its own nature being non-existent,
Its own nature not abiding.
Constantly grasping the non-existent Dharma,
The three natures attain non-abiding.
Fields, being without nature, become
The prior support for the posterior.
Without arising or cessation, originally pure,
And self-nature entering extinction.
One mind like the blue lotus,
May it attain the true golden flower.
The unconditioned light of the seven treasures,
Abiding in the realm of the Dharma King.
Not entering the wheel of retrogression,
May it be born in the Ground of Difficult Victory.
Forever preserving the unconditioned arising,
All accomplish the supreme Dao."

At that time, having heard the Celestial Worthy recite this verse, the Youth of Victorious Causes of the Jeweled Citadel said to Great Wisdom: "By the great compassion of the Celestial Worthy, the treasury of ocean-like, empty wisdom of the One Vehicle, with its boundless flavors of meaning, is provisionally expressed through words to awaken sentient beings. I now contemplate this—rare indeed, rare indeed! The Celestial Worthy skillfully expounds the characteristics of all dharmas as neither existent nor non-existent, neither non-existent nor non-non-existent, neither spoken nor non-spoken. Through the harmonious convergence of causes and conditions, he opens the gate of expedient means to guide and instruct sentient beings. For this reason, it is inconceivable. The ultimate Dao is empty and without attainment. It is like using a wedge to remove a wedge. Why is this so? It is like treating an illness: because of the illness, medicine is taken to regulate body and mind. When the illness is cured, the medicine is dissolved, leaving nothing behind."

At that time, Great Wisdom further addressed him: "The Celestial Worthy of Great Compassion expounds the characteristics of all dharmas as neither empty nor existent, neither eternal nor extinct. Now, do we know emptiness and existence, or do we not know them? It is like someone who grasps the Dharma of equality, expounding this and that, where emptiness has no place. The Celestial Worthy is also thus—his Dharma-body of equality is established in the mind, thus he speaks in this way. It is like someone saying that the past is the present. The Celestial Worthy’s accomplishment is equality of intent. It is like someone possessing one gold coin, with which they seek to obtain a thousand. It is not that they do not obtain a thousand, nor is it that one does not obtain. The Celestial Worthy is also thus—like obtaining a thousand or ten thousand coins from one gold coin. Such is the characteristic: it is like someone reciting and upholding sutras, whose merit accrues over hundreds of thousands of kalpas. All such merits of a thousand or ten thousand are likewise thus. Obtaining one gold coin and using a thousand or ten thousand is also thus. If there are men and women seeking the Dao who are also thus, able to practice small virtues yet receiving superior reward—by whose vow do they, on the path of bliss, in a pure land, proceed to be reborn, possessing the ten reflections and accomplishing their minds?"

If there are sentient beings who accomplish the Celestial Worthy, first extolling and praising the merit of almsgiving—should there be those who, whether for wealth or treasure, damage this wealth and treasure, harboring a miserly heart, not following the Dao’s grace, yet devise skillful means to ensure all myriad beings do not transgress the Dao’s teachings—it is likewise thus.

At that time, the youth *Victorious Cause of the Square City* bowed before the Worthy, joined his palms, and spoke these verses:

The Celestial Worthy, great compassionate mother,
Well expounds the supreme meaning,
Whose words, through cultivation, give rise.
All dharmas that exist,
Thus fruition is perfected.
Whether human or non-human,
Receiving the Dao, they naturally arise.
Thus it is said: the revered Brahmā master
Swiftly completes the *Ocean of Emptiness* host.
From form and views,
One should know the dharma enters illumination.
Dependent arising’s middle discrimination
Is not without true reality.
Thus, not obtaining this medicine,
My Dharma is universally equal and level.
Upholding the Dao, abiding in merit,
Goodness flourishes with manifold meanings.
Together, we set forth on the path of wisdom,
All ascending to the Supreme Capital.

When the youth *Victorious Cause of the Square City* had finished these verses, he addressed *Ocean of Emptiness*: "Great indeed is the true being! Through causes and conditions of distant antiquity, your body radiates light, your spiritual penetrations are sovereign, you emerge into the world, your virtue and conduct are perfectly fulfilled—such cannot be praised enough. Sentient beings, sunk in defilement, by what root-nature do they pose such difficulties? Entering yet not entering, departing yet not departing, clinging to both extremes—how does this occur?"

At that time, *Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom* replied to *Victorious Cause*: "Great being, benevolent one, entering is without duality. Seeing the Dharma as equal, it is neither one nor not-one. By these dharmas, there is no such place. Why? Shattering all demonic perversities, subduing all heretical minds and external paths, such merit is unmatched in the world. Heavenly demons and external paths speak of true principle, yet the Celestial Worthy’s teachings—subtle and wondrous true Dharma—establish their own Dharma, which also has no fixed nature. Why? The Celestial Worthy of Great Compassion teaches the supreme true Dao of original nature, the true Dharma taught cannot be altered or destroyed. Why?
