With wisdom perfectly fulfilled, all heavenly demons, heterodox views, external paths, and perverse minds clinging to attachments obstruct the great Dharma, giving rise to views of existence and destroying the great Dharma."

Through this cause and condition, the Radiant Light Youth manifests in various forms to expound the Dharma, liberating sentient beings and revealing his virtues—namely, by virtue of non-self, he displays pure and subtle merits. My boundless expedient virtues, like worldly dharmas, deem the higher realms as superior.

Good man, the teachings I expound exhaust the cycle of birth and death. They generate all wholesome roots in sentient beings, benefiting and bringing peace, with unimpeded merit. The Celestial Worthy of Great Compassion abides in the Dharma-realm, the supreme unconditioned Dharma.

Good man, the Dharma-realm has two aspects: first, the defiled realm; second, the undefiled realm. The undefiled realm is the purest and most supreme. Why? The Celestial Worthy of Great Compassion exhausts the limits of birth and death, benefiting and bringing peace, with boundless merit and bliss.

At that time, Oceanic Emptiness spoke in verse:

Who upholds the Dharma of great love,
Accords with wholesome roots.
Neither self nor other,
Yet brings benefit, growth, or decline.

Where does the Celestial Worthy
Expound these dharma marks?
This realm, without beginning,
Is the support of all dharmas.

If there are those on the Way
Who attain liberation,
Such original or non-original states—
Rare indeed, rare indeed.

When Oceanic Emptiness had finished speaking these verses, he further asked the Victorious Cause Youth: "You speak of Daoists and all sentient beings who initially do not comprehend, their ignorance unexhausted, bound by craving and attachment. Some drift along, now reborn as animals, now as hungry ghosts, now as humans, now as Celestial Worthies, now as Perfected Ones. Though these Daoists have left the household life, they hold inverted and perverse views, unaware and unknowing. In the world, they thus endure suffering, increasing their craving and attachment, constantly subject to karmic retribution. For what cause and condition do these Daoists remain unaware and unknowing?"

At that time, the Victorious Cause Youth replied to Oceanic Emptiness: "Excellent, true man! Though these Daoists have left the household life, they cling to attachments, their deceit and cunning ablaze. They accumulate much fraud and theft, yet claim to have left the household life, seeking fame and profit, desiring offerings.

Good man, through such causes and conditions, they constantly endure karmic retribution. Why? Whether leaving the household or remaining in it—good man, such persons constantly endure karmic retribution. The Celestial Worthy has declared this intent.

Good man, virtuous Daoists have no attachments. They seek the supreme Dharma, contemplating all dharmas as impermanent, empty, and without possession. Such leaving of the household accords with wholesome causes and conditions. Wholesome and unwholesome causes and conditions each follow their own course, unrelated to others.

Good man, the Celestial Worthy has declared: Those who uphold this admonition rely on this place, constantly without forsaking it, without any notion of self. Why? Because of the emptiness of emptiness."

The grains of sand upon the Ganges—all such merits too are without attachment.

Good man, if the treasury of the true person holds what is realized and what is not, there is no place for it anywhere. The Celestial Worthy of Great Compassion’s secret and precious treasury is neither non-being nor non-non-being, neither being nor non-being, and has no such locus.

Those who leave the household in truth rely and abide in this locus. Those who are not true renunciates cling to consciousness, engaging in many deeds, deceit, and false speech. They return to the gates of evil destinies, binding themselves, heedless of external gatherings, and cry out in lament: “Alas, suffering!”

All sentient beings are just like this.

The youth of supreme causes addressed the great perfected one, Ocean-void Wisdom-treasury, saying: “Is it thus?” He replied: “It is not.”

The true person, the great master, has causes and conditions vast and far-reaching. Today, with joyful courage, the supreme great master and his immeasurable retinue—you have aroused the mind set upon the supreme Dao, which is inconceivable.

At that time, the youth of supreme causes, amidst the great assembly, further spoke these verses:

All dharmas abide dependent on the treasury,
All sentient beings’ consciousness.
Thus it is called *kalya*—
I expound it for others.

Grasping and holding to subtle consciousness,
The seeds of dharmas flow constantly.
To the ordinary and to the “I,” I do not speak;
Let them not cling to it as “I.”

As not all activities,
All activities do not know.
The true person, in accord with wholesome consciousness,
Then departs from the five consciousnesses.

If counteracting and transforming reliance,
It does not become extinguished, thus it is not accomplished.
Cause and fruit are not distinct;
In extinction, there is encounter.

Without seeds, without dharma—
If one allows this to be transformation of reliance,
Since there is no duality and no “there is,”
The meaning of transformation of reliance does not arise.

Without residue, mind transforms dharma—
By what expedient means
Does one arrive at Ocean-void Wisdom-treasury?

Thus concludes *Scroll the Fourth of the Supreme One Vehicle’s Ocean-void Wisdom-treasury Sutra*.
*Scroll the Fifth of the Supreme One Vehicle’s Ocean-void Wisdom-treasury Sutra* begins.

**Chapter on Inquiring About Illness**

At that time, Ocean-void Wisdom-treasury rose from his seat, composed his mind, and bowed in reverence, addressing the Heavenly Venerable: "Heavenly Venerable, now free from all afflictions and ailments, beyond the suffering of impermanence, no longer subject to birth and death, you abide in constant bliss, purity, subtlety, and perfection. Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, why do sentient beings suffer from four kinds of illness? How do the four defilements—craving for sounds and forms, ignorance, arrogance, and pride—become the causes of these diseases? They drive the mind to madness, confusion, and agitation, giving rise to illness. Why is this so? Greed breeds bodily disease; attachment breeds mental disease. When body and mind are equally afflicted, the four hundred and four diseases arise: the skin withers, the flesh wastes away, the heart races in distress, the five viscera fall into discord, urine drips incessantly, eyes and ears ache, the abdomen and back throb with pain, and the four limbs and hundred joints ache ceaselessly. Such are the manifold diseases of body and mind.

The Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Venerable is forever free from illness. Yet now I see all sentient beings—whether human or non-human—suffering from disease. These very illnesses afflict me as well: abdominal disease and heart disease. I beseech the Heavenly Venerable, in your mercy toward us, to expound the healing medicines that may cure all sentient beings of the future, allowing the unseen to see and the unheard to hear."

Then the Heavenly Venerable praised Ocean-void, saying: "Excellent, excellent, good man! You know the right time, inquiring for the sake of all, moved by compassion for sentient beings, and thus speak of illness. Desiring to dispel their suffering, you ask me to prescribe the cure. Good man, you have cultivated great compassion for immeasurable kalpas, ever cherishing and benefiting sentient beings, sparing them from distress. You have offered various medicines and joys to the afflicted. Why then do you now claim to be ill? Good man, it is because you see worldly people suffering from abdominal and heart diseases, their skin and flesh wasting away, that you grieve deeply. To cure these ills, newly ordained Daoists, in their greed, hoard all manner of impure things. In truth, you are not ill; you wish only to guide all deluded sentient beings toward the single vehicle of the Ocean-void Wisdom-treasury, removing their afflictions—greed, anger, ignorance, and wrath.

Good man, the true person, the youth who cultivates great compassion, provides medicine to all the sick, constantly vowing: *May all sentient beings forever sever their diseases and attain the true adamantine body; may all infinite beings always encounter wondrous medicines, cutting off all deafness, blindness, and malignant illnesses.* By severing disease, they gain the medicine of wisdom; by the power of this medicine, they eradicate all venomous afflictions. These sentient beings, in the medicine of wisdom, attain non-retrogression and swiftly accomplish the supreme medicine of the Dao, dissolving all heavy views and afflictions. Diligent in practice, they perfect the wisdom-heart of the Heavenly Venerable. They concoct the medicine of equality, universally curing all diseases, preventing sentient beings from harboring slanderous thoughts. With the medicine of equality—its roots, trunks, branches, and leaves—this medicine of equality heals all grave illnesses, grave views, grave afflictions, and grave hearts. May all beings escape the city of afflictions, depart from the prison of craving, and accomplish the Heavenly Venerable’s pure, luminous, radiant wisdom, entering the secret treasury of Ocean-void.

Good man, the true person, the youth, has already made vast vows across the infinite worlds and lands of the ten directions: *May all sentient beings be freed from the roots, trunks, and branches of disease.* These diseases, empty, pure, cool, and blissful, are ever at ease, subtle, and perfect, equal and beyond equality in aspect."

Then Ocean-void addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "How can you say I am not ill when I am? Now I reflect: in this world, the sick cannot sit or rise, their movements labored, food and drink obstructed, their mouths unable to speak. Like a lost son managing the family estate, when the time comes, kin—parents, spouse, siblings, and friends—each scatter, knowing birth must end in death. Heavenly Venerable, I am just the same. I see sentient beings dwelling in the city of afflictions, beholding only iron pellets glowing red-hot, hungry ghosts wailing skyward, their cries thunderous, eating embers when hungry, drinking fiery essence when thirsty. Hell’s wardens, ox-headed, eyes like bright stars, wield iron forks, circling cauldrons of boiling water. They seize the damned by hand and foot, casting them in, their bones and flesh dissolving. For these reasons, I see myself as ill—abdominal disease, heart disease. How can you say I am not?"

Having spoken thus, Ocean-void composed a verse before the Venerable, entreating:

Greatly Compassionate, Greatly Virtuous One,
Rare in the Three Realms, all look to you.
I pray you expound the equal,
The root of the wisdom-medicine tree.

Now I, a child of many diseases,
From dawn to dusk, barely endure.
My abdomen aches, my heart writhes,
My spirit dims, my breath grows faint.

The lowly, foolish common folk—
How could they know the gate of good medicine?
Like the blind who cannot see the path,
Advancing a foot, they know not an inch.

Though four roads lie before them,
They gallop as they please.
Father of compassion through the three times,
You ever teach the gate of the wisdom-treasury.

When the four diseases of affliction arise,
Body scatters, spirit and soul disperse.
In the dark depths of hell,
How can they see their children and grandchildren?

Day by day, they are born and die again,
Forever parted from the Blissful Venerable.
I pity all sentient beings,
And beg for the medicine of equality.

Whether human or non-human,
Whoever partakes shall endure.
Like sweet dew raining down,
Every branch and leaf receives its grace.

Sprouts, flowers, roots, and trees,
Fruit ripens for all to consume.
I only pray, O Heavenly Venerable,
Expound the single-vehicle Dao.

For those lost in the darkness of suffering,
Who see and yet remain deluded, resentful—
Pity the multitudes yet to come,
Who bow in reverence, forgetting body and soul.

They see only the children of hungry ghosts,
Seeking kin in the three wretched paths.
Ox-heads drag them into cauldrons,
Hell’s wardens flip them with iron forks.

Their wails shake like thunder,
Their bones pile like mountains.
"

When hungry, they eat burning coals;
When thirsty, they drink flames of fire.
Only by Your great compassion’s teaching
May all escape the gates of hell.

These multitudes of sentient beings
Bow their heads to the Supreme Venerable.
Then, the Heavenly Venerable, his heart suffused with boundless mercy, answered Haikong, saying:
“Excellent, excellent, good man! You know well the time and have made this inquiry for the sake of all beings.
These sentient beings, each born from their own thoughts, give rise to manifold distinctions. Within these distinctions, they seek manifold forms, manifold sounds, manifold scents, manifold tastes, manifold touches.
From these causes and conditions arise diseases of the eye, ear, belly, heart, and body—four hundred and four afflictions in all.
You, wishing to accord with all sentient beings and to benefit them, have composed verses to make this inquiry.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable sat upright upon his throne, his countenance radiant and joyful as a red lotus, his majestic bearing luminous as the sun and moon.
Then the Heavenly Venerable emitted a great light, suffusing the empty sky. This radiance, surpassing that of a hundred thousand suns, illuminated the eastern, southern, western, and northern quarters, the four intermediate directions, the zenith and nadir, all lands, and other worlds, bestowing upon all beings the torch of the equality-medicine, extinguishing their four hundred and four afflictions, and establishing all sentient beings in unwavering steadfastness, granting them the mind of equality.

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable, in tranquil contemplation, manifested a wondrous form adorned with seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences, his body resplendent.
From each mark and excellence upon his body bloomed a precious flower, exquisitely subtle, each with a thousand petals—a pure red lotus with a lapis lazuli stem, coral branches, amber roots, and pearl leaves, its form towering and majestic like a jeweled banner.
These precious flowers emitted manifold hues of light—azure, yellow, crimson, white, red, green, vermilion, and purple.
These lights universally illuminated the hells of ignorance, the uninterrupted hell, the wailing hell, the weeping hell, the hell of fire chariots, the hell of fire beds, the hell of iron pellets, and the hell of iron cauldrons.

At that time, within the hells were also hungry ghosts—lonely-form hungry ghosts, solitary-body hungry ghosts, solitary-bone hungry ghosts, solitary-touch hungry ghosts, withered-form hungry ghosts, withered-skin hungry ghosts, withered-bone hungry ghosts, withered-flesh hungry ghosts, empty-eating hungry ghosts, coal-eating hungry ghosts, formless hungry ghosts, and weeping hungry ghosts. Such ghosts constantly endured the suffering of cold, tormented by impermanence, their heads and faces shattered, their bodies broken and torn, mutually harming one another.
When these hungry ghosts beheld the light, all such sufferings vanished without trace, and they were immediately pacified, their bodies soothed and at ease.
They also saw within the light the secret treasury of Haikong’s jeweled terrace, where it was proclaimed that all sentient beings, even these hungry ghosts, possess the nature of the Dao.
Upon hearing these words, the hungry ghosts each repented, and at once their lives ended, and they were reborn among humans and gods. All the hells became utterly empty, with none left to suffer punishment.
Only those who disbelieved and slandered the single-vehicle treasury of Haikong’s wisdom remained, tormented by hunger and thirst, abiding in those hells for hundreds of thousands of years, never having heard the name of sweet dew, never having received the moisture of sweet rain.

At that time, the hells stood empty.
Then, within the light, appeared hundreds of thousands of perfected immortals and youths, each holding golden lotuses and jade flowers. Within each lotus sat a Daoist adept, supremely adorned, unmatched in the world.
From the flowers emerged true-form Daoists, true-aspect Daoists, true-wisdom Daoists, dharma-joy Daoists, dharma-accomplished Daoists, dharma-liberated Daoists, dharma-blessed Daoists, dharma-true Daoists, dharma-delight Daoists, wondrous-adornment Daoists, wondrous-mind Daoists, wondrous-vision Daoists, wondrous-garden Daoists, wondrous-flower Daoists, and wondrous-aspect Daoists.
These Daoists gathered together, some walking, some sitting, some reclining, some standing, each producing wondrous sounds—playing phoenix flutes, zithers, harps, zhu, and konghou, while phoenixes, peacocks, lions, and white tigers roared and sang in harmonious melody.
Whether male or female, all who followed the sound beheld the hells, the animal realms, the hungry ghosts, and all beings, human and non-human, who rejoiced as one.

Then the Heavenly Venerable expounded for all sentient beings the treasury of the single vehicle. He taught the luminous canons of the Three Caverns, the cinnabar scriptures, and the accomplishment of the three vehicles for the benefit of all.
He spoke of leaving the household life, sitting in the empty city adorned with the seven treasures, and turning the wondrous Dharma wheel.
Having turned the Dharma wheel, all the people of that land and all sentient beings received benefit: the blind saw forms, the deaf heard sounds, the mute spoke, the lame walked, the poor became rich, and poverty and wealth were equalized. Those who disbelieved came to believe.
Thus, boundless multitudes of sentient beings cultivated the treasury of the single-vehicle, Haikong’s wisdom.

At that time, gods, dragons, ghosts, and spirits—celestial dragons and aerial ghosts, the eight fierce deities of the swift steed, Qiang, Hu, Di, and Lao peoples, humans and non-humans—all joined their voices in praise, saying:
“Excellent, excellent, Supreme Heavenly Venerable! You have brought great benefit to all.”
Having spoken thus, they leapt and rejoiced, some singing, some dancing, bowing in reverence, circumambulating, and extolling him. They burned incense, scattered flowers, raised banners and canopies, and played music of manifold wondrous sounds, filling the seat with their offerings.
They made offerings to the Heavenly Venerable, the Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, lamenting:
“We, dwelling in borderlands, bear human form yet lack the seed of wisdom. How is it that You, upon the seven-jeweled terrace of Haikong’s vehicle, expound the treasury of the single-vehicle wisdom for all sentient beings? Such rarity is difficult to see, difficult to hear. How can it be said that even Your own body suffers illness?”

May the Heavenly Venerable deign to expound and clarify, that all may see and understand.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable replied to the heavenly dragons: Excellent, excellent, good man! You have already perfected profound wisdom, offering pure and manifold incense and flowers, manifold sweet flavors, manifold music, and manifold jeweled banners. Good man, you have attained wisdom and eloquence, having made offerings to measureless and boundless Heavenly Venerables of the three times. Therefore, you now skillfully purify with incense and make manifold offerings.

Good man, in the past, through measureless and boundless ages—dim and obscure, in the Longhan and Chiming kalpas—I appeared under various names, formless and nameless, expounding for gods and humans this single-vehicle treasury of Haikong’s wisdom. I revealed and distinguished it, pondered its meaning and flavor, and for the multitude unfolded, recited, transcribed, and adorned its scrolls, disseminating it throughout the ten directions of the world, so that all sentient beings received benefit.

Good man, from that time until now, I have never harbored evil, afflictive karmic obstructions, never slandered, never disbelieved, never opposed, never destroyed. Since that time, body and mind have been at peace, free from all suffering and distress.

Good man, you sentient beings dwell in the city of afflictions, beset by manifold illnesses and torments—abdominal ailments and heart ailments—unaware of the secret treasury of the single vehicle. Following expedient speech, you say that Haikong suffers from abdominal and heart ailments. Heavenly dragons, you say that the treasury of Haikong’s wisdom is a great dharma master expounding the teaching for the multitude, yet Haikong is not truly Haikong. Heavenly dragons, you say that the treasury of wisdom is the treasury of wisdom, yet the treasury of wisdom is not truly the treasury of wisdom. Heavenly dragons, you say that the treasury of Haikong’s wisdom is a true immortal, yet Haikong is not truly an immortal. Heavenly dragons, you say that the treasury of Haikong’s wisdom is human or beast, bird or insect, grass or tree, water or fire, stone or earth, yet Haikong is not truly human or beast, not truly bird or insect, not truly grass or tree, not truly water or fire, not truly earth or stone. Such expressions are all the secret treasury of Haikong.

Good man, you say that Haikong is like the waters of the sea, yet Haikong is not truly saline. You say that Haikong is like father, mother, brothers, wife, or children, yet Haikong is not truly father, mother, brothers, wife, or children. You say that Haikong is a great shipmaster, able to ferry across the great sea, yet Haikong is not truly a great ship, nor does he ferry across the great sea. You say that Haikong suffers from abdominal and heart ailments, yet Haikong is not truly afflicted by illness. You say that Haikong dwells in a seven-jeweled city, yet Haikong does not truly dwell. You say that Haikong requests a prescription, yet Haikong does not truly make requests. Through such emptiness is the treasury of Haikong’s wisdom, the city of Haikong.

When the Heavenly Venerable had spoken thus, the assembly—men and women alike—awakened the mind of equanimity. Skillfully cultivating the karma of body, speech, and mind, at the time of death, they entrusted their parents, brothers, and spouses: when my body is taken, let my bones be cast into water, or into a pyre, or upon the mountains and wilds, where jackals, wolves, tigers, and leopards, owls, and mandarin ducks will vie to devour them. Yet their souls, minds, and consciousnesses, bright and clear, will be reborn in the good destinies, in the human realm as kings, transforming and liberating all, governing the world with benevolence, and making offerings with a good heart to the single-vehicle treasury of Haikong’s wisdom.

At that time, in the kingdom there was an elder named Fasheng, who, in the assembly, was afflicted by the four great pains, lying propped upon his bed, day and night without seeking food or drink, his life seeming near its end. His family and wife surrounded him, weeping. The elder entrusted them: Tend diligently to the household affairs, and practice compassionate giving. Now my illness has reached its source, and my life is nearing its end. Birth, aging, and death—how can death be avoided? Hearing these words, his wife and children wailed even more, stirring the assembly. Then, young and old among the multitude snapped their fingers, exclaiming: By the power of the secret treasury of Haikong, how can sentient beings grieve so bitterly?

Suddenly, the elder was cured, as if never afflicted. Thereupon, the elder thought to himself: The majestic and awe-inspiring spiritual power of the single-vehicle Haikong, the wondrous and peerless honor of the three realms, is inconceivable. Now I contemplate the single-vehicle Haikong—it is my bodily life, my vital resource, my alms-food, my dharma-drink. What shall I do? Then he selected from his family and descendants—men and women, thirteen in all, wise and sagacious—and sent them forth to leave the household life, to cultivate the *Treasury of the Single-Vehicle Haikong’s Wisdom*, burning incense, making prostrations, transcribing, reciting, pondering its meaning and flavor, and expounding it for the multitude.

He further donated golden chariots, silver chariots, jade chariots, coral, amber, and pearl chariots, as well as granaries of rice, salt, and the five grains, silks of damask, brocade, and figured weaves, all freely given. Oxen, horses, donkeys, and mules were set loose to roam. He constructed spirit terraces and seven-jeweled luminous halls, chambers and galleries, front halls and rear halls, front palaces and rear palaces, nine-tiered seven-jeweled wondrous spirit terraces, nine-tiered seven-jeweled wondrous pavilions, layered in all four directions. Zithers, harps, and konghous harmonized, their sounds deep and resonant.

Then, people of the kingdom—old and young—passing by the tranquil site, each sighed: Excellent, excellent! Such merit is majestic and inconceivable. Thereupon, each awakened their own resolve, constructing halls and dwellings, large or small, making offerings according to their means—palaces, jeweled terraces, pavilions, and galleries.

Then, within these halls, luminous masters gathered the assembly to expound the single-vehicle treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness, the secret storehouse. At that time, among the kingdom’s people—whether men or women—those of virtuous heart who recited even a single word or phrase, a single line or verse of *The Treasury of Ocean-Emptiness Wisdom of the Single Vehicle*, or who uttered its name, *Treasury of Ocean-Emptiness Wisdom*, all such persons would attain rebirth among humans and gods, enjoying carefree bliss, never falling into hell, the animal realm, or the realm of hungry ghosts. They would be freed from all afflictions and distress, entering the treasury of the single vehicle. This is called the rarity of invoking its name.

Virtuous man, if any being hears the name of this sutra and, having heard it, reveres and believes, all their afflictions and grave illnesses will be utterly eradicated. The sin of disbelief and slander is like a wondrous medicine: though it can cure all manner of grave illness, it cannot revive the dead.

Then, Ocean-Emptiness addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: How are sins extinguished and the slander of disbelief severed? How is virtue attained so that deeds and their retribution follow one another? How does one cultivate the precious treasury of the single vehicle with equanimity and single-mindedness?

The Heavenly Worthy replied: Virtuous man, what does it mean for deeds and their retribution to follow one another? Virtuous man, if any being openly confesses and repents, revealing all the evils committed from the beginning of samsara until they are without sin—by this cause and condition, this is called receiving retribution. Virtuous man, it is like a great king traveling the royal road: all within the empty city flee. So too does the revelation of all evils unfold.

Virtuous man, how are the slanderers not extinguished? If any being disbelieves in *The Treasury of Ocean-Emptiness Wisdom of the Single Vehicle*, harboring arrogance and pride, though they commit manifold evils, they never turn back from such deeds. For this reason, they do not enter the single vehicle, nor is their slander extinguished. Virtuous man, even if countless beings simultaneously enter the *Treasury of Ocean-Emptiness Wisdom* with single-minded devotion, not one among them who slanders or disbelieves will enter the single-vehicle treasury of Ocean-Emptiness Wisdom. Thus, those who do not believe cannot have their slander extinguished.

Furthermore, virtuous man, how does one cultivate the precious treasury of the single vehicle with equanimity and single-mindedness? If any being, whether walking or sitting, contemplates the Great Vehicle, seeing neither the mark of self, nor the mark of others, neither the mark of greatness nor smallness, neither long nor short, white nor black—such marks being devoid of any conceptualization—then the single vehicle is equanimous, like empty space, without great or small, without sage or ordinary. Why is this? If one claims, "This is my body," it is the seed of the Dao, the nature of the Dao. Because the nature of the Dao is present, the body possesses the seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences. Therefore, what I say does not differ from the golden words and jade decrees of the Heavenly Worthy, the sage. Virtuous man, to speak thus is to be Ocean-Emptiness, to be the Treasury of Wisdom. After immeasurable kalpas, one is freed from all afflictions and beholds the equanimous mark of Ocean-Emptiness. Why is this? What I now proclaim is truly without the mark of self, without self or mine. By this cause and condition, the teaching accords with the text, ultimately equanimous.

Virtuous man, it is like a performer who, through various skills, follows the king’s command to travel to another land, even at the cost of their life, never daring to disobey. The wise say that all beings possess the nature of the Dao, and thus, in accord with conditions, they expound without惜ing their lives—just as the performer does not disobey the king’s command.

Furthermore, virtuous man, if any being disbelieves in the precious treasury of the single-vehicle Ocean-Emptiness, calling it unwholesome, not its teaching, not the true word—virtuous man, any being who speaks thus is an evil companion, a great offender of the five heinous crimes. Such a person must not be approached or dwelled with. Why is this?

This person in the present life immediately contracts diseases of worm-infested scabs and festering sores, with foul-smelling worms oozing forth and pus and blood flowing out, whether great or small—all keep far away. Virtuous man, if any being hears the sutra of the single vehicle and rejoices in their heart, snapping their fingers in praise, such a person comes from the heavens above, their form and marks outstanding, moving as a Dharma master, revered and looked up to by all. Such a person immediately leaves afflictions behind, is born from the body of birth-and-death, and attains the vajra body, ascending in broad daylight to the seven-jeweled mystic terrace. Virtuous man, if any woman beholds the Ocean-Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom of the single vehicle and immediately pays reverence, burning incense and making vows, in but a moment she sees her body transformed, becoming a man. Virtuous man, the majestic spirit of this sutra can cause all—whether formed or formless, with life or without—to arouse the mind if they have not yet done so; bring peace and bliss to those who lack it; and raise to heaven those who have not yet ascended.

Those who have not yet escaped suffering are all enabled to escape suffering; those who have not yet attained the Dao are all enabled to attain the Dao.

At that time, Ocean-Emptiness addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: "How can it be said that those who have not yet aroused the mind are all caused to arouse the mind?"

The Heavenly Venerable replied: "Virtuous man, it is like a person dreaming. If in a dream one falls into hell and suffers manifold afflictions, one immediately generates a mind of remorse, lamenting: 'Alas, my own body has brought this retribution upon itself! Now that I have escaped, I must certainly arouse the mind of great compassion. What I have witnessed is most bitter and urgent.' Upon awakening, one knows the supreme right Dharma. One thinks: 'There is a majestic spirit that can gradually bring accomplishment to us all.' This is called arousing the mind.

"Virtuous man, if there are virtuous and devout Daoists—whether men or women—or if there are heavenly demons and heterodox practitioners who can well arouse the mind, receive and uphold the *Ocean-Emptiness Treasury of the Single Vehicle*, recite and copy it, contemplate its meaning and flavor, and expound it to others, then all beings will attain liberation and depart from the city of afflictions.

"Virtuous man, those heavenly demons constantly receive from the great king various offerings—elephants, horses, chariots, kingdoms, wives, and children. They say to the king: 'I went to the mountain and saw an old man expounding the supreme great Dao to the multitude. In truth, my Dharma contains no such teachings. Now the king has heard the old man’s illusions. Perhaps he will gather people and sages from the eight directions. I and the king together transform beings. If you do not send him away, the kingdom will be destroyed.'

"At that time, the great king, having heard these words, dreamed that night of an old man in the mountains—his own father—who wished to expound the *Treasury of the Single Vehicle* to the king. Upon awakening, the king pondered: 'What is the meaning of the Single Vehicle?' He then addressed his master, saying: 'The king has dreamed of an old man in the mountains who wishes to expound the secret treasury of the Single Vehicle.'

"At that time, the heavenly demon, with a humble countenance, replied to the king: 'The kingdom is about to be destroyed.' The king’s mind became scattered. Thereupon, the heavenly demon displayed supernatural powers, causing wind, rain, and great floods for seven days and seven nights, with the rain unceasing. The king, greatly terrified, addressed his master, saying: 'The king has had an inauspicious dream, yet his mind remains unshaken. I only beseech the sagely master to dispel this calamity.' The entire kingdom then pledged to follow the master, daring not to disobey.

"At that time, the old man’s body radiated light, illuminating all the kingdoms. He then pointed his hand toward the heavenly demon. Thereupon, the demon’s supernatural powers vanished, and the wind dispersed, the rain ceased. The king rejoiced greatly, prostrated himself, and addressed the great man, saying: 'The king’s wisdom is shallow and has not beheld the countenance of heaven. Though he has served the heavenly demon, he has always longed for the Compassionate Venerable. Last night in a dream, someone expounded the *Treasury of the Single Vehicle* to the king. I do not yet understand: what is the meaning of the Single Vehicle? The king’s master, the heavenly demon, always says that the world is impermanent, that there is arising and ceasing. For this reason, kingdoms, cities, wives, children, elephants, horses, and chariots are all to be relinquished, in the hope of attaining constant bliss and escaping the suffering of impermanence.'

"At that time, the old man manifested a wondrous appearance, revealing his true form as a divine youth, adorned with the seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences. His radiance was outstanding. He addressed the great king, saying: 'I am foolish and dull, my understanding shallow. I have always heard that the *Ocean-Emptiness Treasury of the Single Vehicle* is without self or other, equal to empty space; that the Three Clarities and all sages are impermanent in every thought-moment. How then can worldly conduct be equated with arising and ceasing? The three realms are impermanent—why is this so? Whether there is constancy or impermanence, arising or non-arising, all such categories are simultaneously obliterated. How can there be constancy that receives the offering of impermanence? If one offers the impermanent in pursuit of constant bliss, then the constant and the impermanent are unequal. How can one speak of worldly conduct as impermanent?'

"Virtuous man, it is like boarding a boat where the captain, fearing the vessel will sink, concentrates his mind, praying: 'May we not encounter wind and waves.' Then two people address the captain, saying: 'Please ferry us to the other shore.' The captain reflects: 'The weather is calm; my boat can cross.' He then loads the two passengers and sets out for the opposite shore. Once on the water, the boat immediately capsizes.

"Virtuous man, the heavenly demon ferries the king in just this way. Though he receives the king’s offerings—kingdoms, cities, wives, children, elephants, horses, and chariots—he ultimately casts the king into the hell of the impermanent path.

"At that time, the heavenly demon, having heard these words, felt shame and remorse. Fixing his attention before the Dao, he listened to the flavor of the *Ocean-Emptiness Treasury of the Single Vehicle* and immediately exclaimed: 'Excellent! Excellent! This is my true father, my true life. How could I again offer kingdoms, cities, and the seven treasures, or perform various acts of generosity and great feasts, only to wholeheartedly receive and uphold the *Ocean-Emptiness Treasury*?'

"At that time, the four assemblies, having heard these words, rejoiced greatly. They prostrated themselves before the Dao, returned to their seats, and listened single-mindedly.

"Then the *Ocean-Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom* rose from his seat. With measured and graceful steps, fearless and composed like a lion, he entered the seven-jeweled grove, prostrated himself, and addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: 'Such a scripture, this wondrous treasury, possesses manifold virtues and manifold wisdoms. It is profoundly subtle and inconceivable. O Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, all beings today are burdened with heavy obstructions of affliction. They commit the three evil deeds, harbor disbelief, and slander this scripture. Yet all such beings possess the nature of the Dao. How then can it be said that they will fall into hell? If these beings possess the nature of the Dao, how can it be said that they suffer the afflictions of impermanence? When beings sever their roots of goodness, this is called the three evils. If the roots of goodness are severed, how can the nature of the Dao in all beings not also be severed? If the nature of the Dao is severed, how can it again be said to be constant, blissful, and sovereign? What is to be done with such cases?'"

"If it were determined, how could one attain the paths of humans, heavens, or even the lower immortals—true persons, Daoist adepts, or the Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Venerable? If the paths from human to heavenly realms down to the lower immortals were determined, then one should also not attain the unshakable treasury of the One Vehicle’s sea of emptiness, the secret and wondrous repository. If beings commit various evils, they are not determined to attain the paths of humans, heavens, or even the lower immortals to study the true Way as Daoist adepts. Being thus undetermined, the Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Venerable is also undetermined. If the Dao is undetermined, the *Sutra of the Sea of Emptiness’s Treasury of Wisdom* is also undetermined, and all dharmas are likewise undetermined. How is this undetermined, and how are the offenses of indeterminacy removed?

If one claims that indeterminacy removes the offenses of indeterminacy, then those who have already become true immortals and Daoist adepts should also be undetermined, and those who have entered the treasury of the One Vehicle’s sea of emptiness should also exit it, falling into the offenses of birth and death. If this were so, the nature of the Treasury of Wisdom would be undetermined. Because it is not determined, it should be known that there is no secret treasury of the One Vehicle’s sea of emptiness. How then can it be said that one enters the treasury of the One Vehicle’s sea of emptiness?"

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable, out of great compassion, replied to Sea of Emptiness, saying: "Excellent, excellent, good man, Sea of Emptiness, Treasury of Wisdom. You now serve as a bridge to benefit all beings, bringing them peace and joy. Out of pity and compassion for all in the world, you seek to cultivate the mind of the Great Vehicle and ask such questions on behalf of all true immortals. Good man, you have drawn near to the heavenly and human beings of the past, planting roots of goodness in all dharmas. Long have you perfected the virtue of equanimity, subdued the hordes of demons, and caused them to retreat. You have already taught immeasurable, boundless beings, all awakening to the truth. The true immortal youths have aroused the mind of equanimity. You have penetrated all dharmas, the profound, subtle, and secret treasury. In the past, you have enabled immeasurable, boundless heavenly and human beings to hear the profound and subtle meaning of the One Vehicle. You wish to enable beings who have not yet seen to see, to benefit all beings—whether human or non-human, good men or good women, great or small.

Good man, those who inquire into the flavor of this sutra’s meaning should now listen earnestly and attentively. I shall distinguish and expound it for you. Good man, even one who slanders is not determined. If it were determined, then one who slanders would never attain the paths of humans, heavens, or immortals. Precisely because it is not determined, one can attain them. As you have rightly observed, the nature of the Dao is not severed. How then can it be said that one who slanders severs the roots of goodness?

Good man, there are two kinds of roots: internal roots and external roots. Within the nature of the Dao, there is neither internal nor external. For this reason, the arising of the nature of the Dao is neither severed nor unsevered. There are also two kinds: the conditioned and the unconditioned. Within the nature of the Dao, there is neither conditioned nor unconditioned, and thus the nature of the Dao is not constant. There are also two kinds: the truly constant and the impermanent. Within the nature of the Dao, there is neither constancy nor impermanence. For this reason, the arising of the nature of the Dao is neither severed nor constant. If it were severed, it should be regained. If it is not regained, it is called unsevered. If it is severed and then regained, that is called slander, committing various evil offenses—this too is undetermined. If it were determined, one who commits various evil offenses would never attain the paths of humans, heavens, or immortals. One who slanders the *Sutra of the Treasury of Wisdom* is also undetermined. If it were determined, one who slanders the true Dharma would never attain the paths of humans, heavens, or immortals. Committing the three evils is also undetermined. If it were determined, one who commits the three evils would never attain the paths of humans, heavens, or immortals.

Form and the characteristics of form—both are undetermined. The characteristics of the eye, ear, and touch, up to the characteristics of ignorance—all dharmas are likewise undetermined. Good man, it is like a dancer who, in the midst of a great assembly, conjures cities and palaces, elephants, horses, and chariots, adorning the body with various ornaments, villages and towns, mountains, forests, and trees, springs, ponds, and rivers. Among that assembly, there are beings without wisdom who, upon seeing these, take them to be real. But those with wisdom know them to be illusory, deceiving the eyes through the power of illusion.

Good man, all ordinary beings, even the earth immortals of the lower realms who study the lesser vehicle, perceive all dharmas as having fixed characteristics—this is likewise so. The true immortal youths do not perceive any fixed characteristics in all dharmas. Good man, it is like a child who, in the sunlight, sees the shimmering heat and calls it water. A person of wisdom, seeing this sunlight, would never falsely perceive it as real water. It is merely an illusory mirage, deceiving the eyes—it is not truly water. All ordinary beings, even those of the lower realms who study the lesser vehicle, perceive all dharmas in this way. The true immortal youths do not perceive any fixed characteristics in all dharmas.

Good man, it is like an echo in an empty valley. Foolish people hear it and take it to be a real sound. Those with wisdom understand that it is not fixed or real—it is merely a sound deceiving the ear. Good man, all ordinary beings perceive characteristics in all dharmas in this way. The true immortal youths thoroughly understand all dharmas as having no fixed characteristics, perceiving the characteristics of impermanence, emptiness, quiescence, and non-arising and non-ceasing. For this reason, the true immortal youths perceive all dharmas as impermanent. Good man, there are also fixed characteristics. What is fixed? Quiescence, extinction, purity, constancy, bliss, and sovereignty—entering the Treasury of Wisdom of the sea of emptiness. Good man, the five penetrations of earth immortals are also undetermined."

Due to their lack of determinacy, they repeatedly pass through countless kalpas of *Yankang*, attaining the paths of humans and gods—yet even these remain undetermined. Due to their lack of determinacy, after another kalpa, they attain the Dao of Sea-Emptiness.

Good man, Sea-Emptiness now abides in the Jeweled City of the Eight *Qian* Grove, manifesting the wondrous seventy-two marks. He seeks to enter the secret treasury of the One Vehicle’s Sea-Emptiness Wisdom, enabling all future beings who have not yet attained the supreme One Vehicle’s true path to do so, and also causing the four assemblies—all disciples and good people—to generate great joy. He wishes for gods and humans to prepare pure offerings, establish grand feasts, and make offerings to all, so that both humans and non-humans universally receive benefit.

Good man, at that time, all in the assembly spoke among themselves, saying: "Sea-Emptiness dwells in the Treasury of the One Vehicle." Know that Sea-Emptiness, the supreme master, abides in the treasury. Why? Because Sea-Emptiness is constant bliss, unchanging, and thus dwells in the treasury. We, the four assemblies, all reflect: if the Treasury of Sea-Emptiness is undetermined, then know that Sea-Emptiness is also undetermined. For this reason, the Treasury of Sea-Emptiness is likewise undetermined.

Good man, know that Sea-Emptiness is also undetermined. Sea-Emptiness is neither emptiness nor non-emptiness; neither sea nor non-sea; neither emptiness nor non-emptiness, neither sea nor non-sea; neither god nor non-god, neither venerable nor non-venerable; neither human nor non-human, neither ghost nor non-ghost; neither hell nor animal, neither non-hell nor non-animal; neither sentient being nor non-sentient being; neither dharma nor non-dharma, neither form nor non-form, neither mind nor non-mind; neither existence nor non-existence, neither non-existence nor non-non-existence; neither impermanent nor non-impermanent, neither illusion nor non-illusion; neither name nor non-name, neither discourse nor non-discourse.

For these causes and conditions, good man, to understand that all dharmas are empty of all dharmas—by this principle, it is called Sea-Emptiness, called Treasury of Wisdom.

Good man, why is Sea-Emptiness not Sea-Emptiness? Those who speak of emptiness and speak of Sea-Emptiness are like the kings of the ten directions’ immeasurable lands, great kings and lesser kings, who in measureless kalpas have relinquished their thrones, wandering in mountains and forests, contemplating the Treasury of Sea-Emptiness of the One Vehicle. Thus they are neither kings nor non-kings. When Sea-Emptiness arises, it arises in non-arising, yet is not non-non-arising. Why? Ascending the summit of Jade Capital, it transforms and is born below—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-arising in heaven nor non-Pure Heaven. Why? It cannot be defiled by any worldly dharmas, like a lotus rising from muddy water yet unstained by mud or water. Thus Sea-Emptiness, though born among dharmas, is neither those dharmas nor the Treasury of Wisdom—this is called Sea-Emptiness, this is called Treasury of Wisdom.

Good man, for this reason, Sea-Emptiness is neither true person nor youth. This Sea-Emptiness is also neither non-emptiness nor non-treasury. Why? Sea-Emptiness has long been free from human existence in measureless kalpas—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-human nor non-ghost. Why? It also transforms beings through ghostly forms—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-ghost nor hell nor animal. Why? Sea-Emptiness has long departed from all evils—thus it is neither non-hell nor sentient being. Why? It has long abandoned the nature of sentient beings. Yet it expounds the subtle marks of sentient beings—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-sentient being nor dharma. Why? Each dharma has its distinct marks, but only Sea-Emptiness is complete with the One Mark. Thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-dharma nor form. Why? Its bodily form already possesses the seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences; the illusions of form are like mirages, like echoes. Thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-form nor mind. Why? Its thoughts are extinguished, equal to empty space—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-mind nor existence. Why? Sea-Emptiness is autonomous, pure, and subtly wondrous. Thus it is neither non-existence nor non-non-existence. Why? Sea-Emptiness—whether in coming or going, sitting or lying—also manifests as vajra. Thus it is neither non-non-existence nor impermanent. Why? Because it has parts—thus Sea-Emptiness is not impermanent. How is it not impermanent? Because it has knowledge. The eternal dharma is without knowledge, like the mark of empty space. Sea-Emptiness has knowledge—thus it is not eternal. Nor is it non-illusion. Why? Its vajra body is unshaken and unmoving; it divides this one body into measureless bodies, and those measureless bodies are again this one body. Sometimes it makes a great body, sometimes a small body, a male body, a female body, the bodies of youths—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-illusion nor non-name. Why? Without name or form, quiescent and eternally blissful—thus Sea-Emptiness is neither non-name nor non-discourse. Why? It speaks of the unspeakable, like a mirage, like lightning. Thus Sea-Emptiness is not non-discourse.

Then the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken these words, remained silent and unmoving. Again he answered Sea-Emptiness, saying: Good man, all ordinary beings do not see afflictions. All ordinary beings in the future will have doubts—do not see afflictions.

Then the Treasury of Sea-Emptiness and Wisdom addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, how is it that ordinary beings do not see afflictions? Within afflictions, do they have a body or not? In past lives, did the body originally exist or not? In the future and present, does this body exist or not? If there is a body, is it form or not form? Does the body belong to another or not? Is it neither belonging nor not belonging to another? Is there life without a body, or a body without life? Is there both body and life, or neither body nor life? Are body and life both eternal, both impermanent, eternal yet impermanent, or neither eternal nor impermanent?

Then the Heavenly Worthy, composed and smiling, answered Sea-Emptiness: Excellent, excellent, good man. All ordinary beings have a body or no body—an afflicted body. Why? The afflicted body is skin wrapped around pus and blood, obstructing the nature of the Dao. Thus beings do not see afflictions, yet possess the true nature of the Dao. The true nature of the Dao is not in the middle, nor is it existence or non-existence. Is it not past, not present, not future? Not form or mind, not self or other? Not having life, not lacking life? Not having a body, not lacking a body? Not eternal, not impermanent?

Then Sea-Emptiness bowed and made obeisance, addressing the Heavenly Worthy: As you have said, is it neither having a body nor lacking a body? How does the afflicted body that obstructs the nature of the Dao arise—from parents? From minute particles? From illusion? From spontaneity?

From emptiness? From transformation? From good? From evil? From beasts? From hell? From heaven? If the nature of the Dao arises from parents, how can parents be afflictions or not afflictions? If they are afflictions, how can they give rise to the true nature of the Dao? If they truly give rise to it, it should be eternal—how then can the true nature arise from afflictions? If it arises from afflictions, and afflictions are delusive obstructions that cast one into hell, then the arising of the nature of the Dao would also fall into hell. If it does not fall, how can the nature of the Dao arise from afflictions? If there are no afflictions, how can afflictions obstruct the nature of the Dao? For these reasons, I only pray that the Compassionate Venerable One will take pity and explain.”

At that moment, the assembly gazed intently, eager to hear. Then the Heavenly Worthy emitted a subtle and wondrous sound, answering Sea-Emptiness:

“Good man, the nature of the Dao is the nature of no-nature—neither the nature of existence nor the nature of non-existence. The arising of the nature of the Dao is both existent and non-existent. Good man, the nature of the Dao arises neither from a body nor from no-body, nor from neither existence nor non-existence; it arises both from a body and from no-body.

Good man, how do afflictions obstruct the nature of the Dao? The nature of the Dao arises from afflictions, yet not from afflictions; it is both affliction and not affliction. How then do afflictions obstruct the nature of the Dao? Good man, it is like dark clouds obscuring the sunlight. The light of the sun is neither born nor destroyed, neither comes nor goes, neither exists nor does not exist. The arising of the nature of the Dao is likewise.

Good man, the arising of the nature of the Dao is not born from parents, yet it is born from parents. Why? If it is born from parents, once born from parents, it is born from what is unborn—the arising of the unarisen. It is like flowers and fruit: flowers arise without fruit, and fruit arises without flowers. The arising of the Dao is likewise.

How then can the nature of the Dao arise from parents? Good man, how can the nature of the Dao arise from minute particles? The nature of the Dao arises from minute particles, yet not from minute particles; from illusion, yet not from illusion; from spontaneity, yet not from spontaneity; from emptiness, yet not from emptiness; from transformation, yet not from transformation; from good causes, yet not from good causes; from evil causes, yet not from evil causes; from beasts, yet not from beasts; from hell, yet not from hell; from heaven, yet not from heaven. For these reasons, the arising of the unarisen arises from arising, yet the arisen does not arise. If it is non-existent, the non-existent does not lack, neither lacks nor exists. Therefore, the arising of the nature of the Dao is the arising of arising, yet arising does not arise.

Good man, you earlier asked: If the nature of the Dao arises from parents, how can parents be afflictions? Good man, I shall now explain. The nature of the Dao arises from parents. Good man, it is like the lotus flower, which arises from the mud, yet the arising from mud is neither mud nor not mud. The arising of the nature of the Dao is likewise—both from parents and not from parents.

Good man, it is like a person in a house: the person dwells in the house, yet the house does not contain the person. The arising of the nature of the Dao is likewise. It is like life dwelling in wood, arising with the wood, yet not from the seed of wood. The arising of the nature of the Dao is likewise—arising from afflictions, yet not from the seed of afflictions. If it were afflictions, how could the nature of the Dao be like empty space, unattainable in form? From this, you should know that it is not the root of afflictions, nor of beings, nor of neither existence nor non-existence.

Good man, all beings, if born from the causes and conditions of parents, fail to recognize those causes and conditions. They recklessly commit all evils, generate discriminating thoughts, disbelieve the scriptures, do not cherish beings, and submit to the cycle of birth and death without end. For these reasons, they discriminate between good and evil, do not restrain the six senses, and give rise to all kinds of attachments. They slander the *One Vehicle Treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness*, hearing yet not hearing, listening yet not listening, and generate all manner of thoughts. Because of these causes and conditions, some contract leprosy, some become deaf or blind, some take the forms of beasts—oxen, horses, pigs, or dogs—some receive human form with incomplete faculties, possessing human shape yet lacking sentiment and wisdom.

Good man, when I previously expounded this sutra, the heavenly demon kings came together to the assembly, generating all manner of slander and disturbing the fourfold assembly. In an instant, those demon kings, each leading their retinues, returned to their own realms and lodged along the way. That night, they suddenly encountered a poisonous rain that fell for three days and three nights. Some contracted yellow toxins, some leprosy. Then, the demon hosts were afflicted with poisonous diseases; some developed leprosy, their suffering deep and grave, and they grew greatly distressed. Each thought to themselves: *Why have I fallen into such great suffering, with sores and pain on my head and face? Surely I must die.* From body to body, from birth to birth, they generated great generosity and great merit, vowing to relinquish their bodies to attain a true human form, to abandon perverse wisdom and attain right wisdom.

As those demon kings approached the end of their lives, they fell into the mud and mire, tormented by sorrow: *Alas! What transgression have I committed? What precept have I violated to suffer thus?* Then, out of my great compassion, I emitted a radiant light that illuminated the ten directions and boundless worlds, all beings, the three paths of hell, and all the ghosts therein. None were not illuminated, and all beheld the *One Vehicle Treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness* upon its jeweled terrace.”

They beheld the Ocean of Emptiness and heard the profound, true flavor of the One Vehicle’s meaning. Awakening to the evil causes of their past lives, they recalled the manifold thoughts by which they had slandered the scriptures and conceived disbelief. Thereupon they made confession, saying:

*“I now take refuge in the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness, the Most High Heavenly Worthy, the Heavenly Dharma Master, the Ocean of Emptiness Perfected One.”*
*“I now take refuge in the Most High Heavenly Worthy, the Heavenly Dharma Master, the Ocean of Emptiness Perfected One.”*
*“I now take refuge in the Most High Heavenly Worthy, the Heavenly Dharma Master, the Ocean of Emptiness Perfected One.”*

Having chanted this confession thrice, from the eastern direction a great jeweled city arose, floating in the void. At the sight of the jeweled city, the demon kings’ illnesses were instantly cured. They returned to their seats, listened to the Dharma, and settled their minds in unshakable stillness. Then they beheld the One Vehicle Treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness.

Having seen the Treasury, they faithfully received every line, every word, every verse of the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness scriptures. Day and night they contemplated them, their minds single and reverent. Thereupon the demon kings transformed their bodies into bodies of wisdom.

At that time, the hells were emptied, and none remained to suffer punishment. The great worthies of the land gathered and deliberated: *“Has our land attained the power of the Three Treasures, thereby establishing great blessings at this time?”* Before and behind the jeweled terrace’s halls, in all four directions, chambers and galleries rose in layered pavilions. Zithers, harps, and konghous blended their sounds in harmony—so exquisitely mournful and wondrous that none could hear them without being moved.

Then, whether man or woman in that land, all who heard the music gave rise to wholesome minds and extolled the One Vehicle Treasury of the Ocean of Emptiness. Within the terrace, a great Illuminator daily expounded the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness scriptures, universally delivering beings—whether human or nonhuman—perfecting their wisdom of all species and benefiting all.

When the Heavenly Worthy had finished speaking the scriptures in full, he sat in silent stillness. The assembly of worthies, the king, the elders, and all—great and small—each received benefit. Together they rose, bowed in reverence, and took their leave.

*The Fifth Scroll of the Most High One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom concludes.*

*The Sixth Scroll of the Most High One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom: The Chapter on Upholding the Precepts.*

At that time, the Ocean of Emptiness Treasury of Wisdom, together with the assembled gods and humans, perfected immortals and divine youths, earthbound immortals and Daoist adepts, rose to bow in reverence. Kneeling with hands clasped in devotion, they addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, we have now journeyed to the lower realms and witnessed the manifold beings—whether human or nonhuman—dwelling within the city of afflictions below. There, heavenly demons, wayward spirits, and malevolent ghosts torment and harm one another, leaving none at peace. Each is consumed by sorrow and distress, gripped by great fear, with nowhere to turn for refuge. How may the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness’ pure precepts broadly benefit gods and humans, the boundless multitude of beings, granting them peace and joy, enabling them to uphold and rely upon the wondrous, pure precepts? We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to take pity on us and expound in detail the pure and wondrous precepts, that all beings may abide in lasting peace."

Then the Heavenly Worthy replied to the Ocean of Emptiness, saying: "Excellent, excellent, good man, perfected ones and divine youths! You should all listen single-mindedly and uphold the One Vehicle’s unimpeded pure precepts, that future beings may receive benefit. Good men and good women, concentrate your thoughts on the five kinds of pure precepts. What are these five? Good man, the first is the Dao-precept, the second is the sagely precept, the third is the true precept, the fourth is the immortal precept, and the fifth is the precept of beings. Good man, perfected ones and divine youths should always cultivate these five practices."

Then the Ocean of Emptiness addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "As to the five precepts just described, how does the Dao-precept come to prevail?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied to the Ocean of Emptiness, saying: "Excellent, excellent, good man! The so-called Dao-precept is the secret treasury of the One Vehicle scriptures, giving rise to manifold forms. It is practiced as the one hundred and eighty precepts, the three hundred great precepts, the precept beyond precepts, neither existing as a precept nor lacking one; neither non-existent nor non-absent; neither eternal nor severed; neither severed nor eternal, nor neither severed nor eternal. Good man, just as the empty sky allows all wholesome dharmas to flourish, so too is the Dao-precept. All beings who hear and behold the secret treasury of the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness generate faith. They should contemplate the wondrous precepts of the true Dao, which are constant, blissful, self-existent, and pure, replete with merit, the supreme and correct Dharma."

Then the Ocean of Emptiness addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "How does the sagely precept serve as a bridge?"

The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Excellent, Ocean of Emptiness, good man! The so-called sagely precept is such that from the four classes of people in the world—immortals, Daoist adepts, kings, and elders—those who attain the correct Dharma and the subtle scriptures of the One Vehicle Treasury of Wisdom should all cherish and delight in it, avidly seeking the secret treasury of the Great Vehicle. They renounce what they love: their six kinds of kin, their dwellings, gold and silver treasures, exquisite ornaments, incense, flowers, lamps, candles, music, attendants, male and female servants, young and old, elephants, horses, carriages, oxen, sheep, chickens, dogs, pigs, and the like. They further reflect: 'Living at home is oppressive, like a prison. All afflictions arise from it, and all hunger arises from it. How, then, do we continue to bear this body of birth and death, this body of afflictions, this body of filth and worms, this body like a starving tiger, enduring manifold evils? How should we leave the household life to cultivate the supreme, correct, and wondrous Dao?'

When they resolve to leave the household life, deviant demons and heterodox ways generate great sorrow and suffering. These demonic paths then wage great war against them. They constantly think: 'How can we engage in conflict with others?' At that time, they arrive at the bodhimanda, where they behold the Heavenly Worthy and his disciples, their deportment complete, their faculties tranquil, their minds gentle, pure, and quiescent. We beings then approach them, seeking to leave the household life, entering the bodhimanda and donning the great Dharma robes. Having left the household life, they uphold the prohibitive precepts, their deportment flawless, their movements composed, without transgression. Even for minor offenses, they feel fear. Their resolve to protect the precepts is like vajra. They further hear the secret treasury of the One Vehicle Ocean of Emptiness.

Good man, it is like a person carrying a lacquered tray, wishing to cross the great sea. Then, a demonic thief in the sea begs the tray from this person. Having heard the request, the person reflects: 'If I give it, I will surely drown and die.' Thus, they reply: 'Demon, you may kill me, but you shall not have the tray.' The demonic thief says: 'If you cannot give it to me entirely, then grant me half as a kindness.' The person still refuses. The demonic thief says: 'If you cannot grant me half, then please give me a third.' The person replies: 'I would rather die together with you than give you the tray.' The demonic thief says: 'I beseech your great compassion to bestow upon me even a fragment of your treasure.' The person reflects: 'This treasure of mine shall never be yours.' The demonic thief says: 'If you still cannot give me the treasure, I am now impoverished and afflicted by manifold sufferings. I beg you to relieve me, even by a mote of dust.' The person replies: 'Today, I am about to cross the sea, yet I know not whether it lies east or west, near or far. How can I give you anything? If I do, how shall I traverse the peril of the great sea? I fear I may drown midway, and regret will be too late.'

Good man, perfected ones and divine youths who protect and uphold the prohibitive precepts are like that person guarding the lacquered tray, refusing to yield it to the demonic thief. Good man, perfected ones and divine youths who thus guard the wondrous and pure precepts do so in the same manner."

The demonic thief again says: "You should trust me, for I shall never deceive you. Simply relinquish the lacquered tray and guard the other trays. For this reason, you shall safely reach the far shore." At that moment, the person reflects: "I would rather drown in the great sea than destroy the tray." The demonic thief again says: "If you cannot destroy the lacquered tray, then you may destroy the true treasure in your hand. For this reason, you shall safely reach the far shore." The person again refuses to destroy it. The demonic thief further says: "If you cannot relinquish the treasure in your hand, then you may relinquish the luminous pearl upon your body. For this reason, you shall safely reach the far shore." At that time, the person again refuses to relinquish it. Then, the demonic thief ponders for a long while, turns away, and retreats.

Thereupon, the person sails across on the lacquered tray and reaches the far shore. Reflecting, he thinks: "Now, as I journeyed, the demonic thief came to assail me. I grasped the lacquered tray firmly and did not relinquish it, thus reaching this shore. It was because my mind was steadfast and unyielding. Just so, the lacquered tray, the treasure in my hand, the luminous pearl, and the golden anklets beneath my feet—I guarded them firmly, built a treasury, and placed them securely upon the jeweled tray."

Good man, the treasury of the empty sea—if there are beings who guard and uphold the wondrous and pure precepts of the empty sea, holding them firmly, they are like that person guarding the jeweled tray. Guarding the jeweled tray is just so.

At that time, Empty Sea addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "The true Dao and sacred precepts thus expounded possess wondrous merit, inconceivable in their efficacy. From such merit arise manifold thoughts and manifold practices. How do perfected immortals receive and uphold the precepts?"

Then, the Heavenly Worthy replied to Empty Sea, saying: "Excellent is this question. Good man, if there are beings who renounce worldly glory and profit, do not engage in trade, use false weights and measures, or deceive others; who do not seize others' wealth, fields, houses, or granaries by force; who do not keep elephants, horses, carriages, cattle, sheep, mules, donkeys, chickens, dogs, macaques, peacocks, parrots, young boys or girls, adult men or women, slaves, servants, gold, silver, lapis lazuli, giant clams, or other treasures—but instead disperse them all to seek and receive the pure precepts of perfected ones—good man, if there are beings who, regarding all grains—rice, wheat, beans, millet, sorghum, hemp, and prepared or raw foods—always take but one meal a day, never eating twice; who, when observing a fast, never eat twice; who, when fasting, eat only at midday, always knowing contentment, never accepting other invitations, nor partaking of mixed foods; who do not consume the five pungent roots or strong-smelling foods, so that their bodies and minds remain free from defilement—such beings are ever revered, honored, and praised by all gods and people, never forsaken. Whether man or woman, they draw near to hear the One Vehicle, the wondrous treasury of the empty sea."

"Good man, if there are beings who do not hoard treasures—whether gold, silver, seven-jeweled golden beds, or woven mats of various colors—and do not sit or lie upon them, maintaining a tranquil mind and refraining from gazing; who do not look upon elephants, horses, carriages, fine silks, or the colors of phoenixes, peacocks, or parrots; who do not listen to flutes, lutes, zithers, harps, or other musical performances; who do not practice physiognomy of hands, feet, or faces; who do not divine by casting lots; who do not serve as princes; who harbor no deceit or flattery, no jealousy or malice, but maintain equanimity, love, and peaceful conduct—good man, such perfected immortals, who firmly uphold the wondrous and pure precepts in their hearts, ward off all demonic influences, attain the true nature of the Dao, and perceive all things with perfect clarity, without distinction."

"Good man, if there are beings who receive and uphold the pure precepts and all such prohibitions, they should make this vow: 'I would rather cast this body into a blazing fire, a deep pit, or a long trench than violate these wondrous and pure precepts of the perfected ones.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have molten iron wrapped around my body than dare, with a body that has broken the precepts, to constantly receive the clothing of faithful benefactors.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather lie upon an iron bed than dare, with a body that has broken the precepts, to constantly receive the seats of faithful benefactors.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather endure a thousand poisoned needles piercing my body than dare, with a body that has broken the precepts, to constantly receive the sweet dew of medicine from faithful benefactors.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather cast this body into a cauldron of boiling water than dare, with a body that has broken the precepts, to constantly receive the houses and dwellings of faithful benefactors.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have this body ground to dust than dare, with a body that has broken the precepts, to constantly receive the reverence and homage of faithful benefactors.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have hot iron hooks pierce my eyes than allow my mind to be defiled by coveting another’s beauty.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have hot iron stuffed into my ears than allow my mind to be defiled by listening to another’s voice.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have a sharp blade sever my nose than allow my mind to be defiled by craving fragrant scents.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have a sharp blade tear out my tongue than allow my mind to be defiled by craving delicious flavors.' Good man, perfected youths further make this vow: 'I would rather have an axe chop my body than allow my mind to be defiled by craving tactile pleasures.' Why is this? For such reasons, beings fall into hells, animal realms, or the realm of hungry ghosts."

Good man, perfected youths safeguard and uphold these precepts, offering them in practice to all beings. For such reasons, they wish all beings to protect and maintain the prohibitive precepts, attaining pure precepts, subtle and complete, and accomplishing the precepts of the One Vehicle’s ocean of emptiness.

Good man, when perfected youths cultivate the pure precepts of the One Vehicle, they immediately attain rebirth in the Jade Pure Palace, unshaken and unmoved, neither retreating nor scattering. Good man, just as the Jade Capital remains unmoved regardless of the wind’s strength, so too do perfected youths who uphold pure precepts and dwell in the Jade Capital.

Good man, when perfected youths constantly single-mindedly cultivate the pure precepts of the One Vehicle, dwelling in the Jade Capital, they remain unshaken and unmoved, neither swayed by the inner demons of afflictions nor cast down by outer demons. Why is this? When perfected youths sit beneath the bodhi tree at the place of the Dao, even heavenly demons cannot shake them.

Good man, how can beings with pure precepts—whether the twenty precepts, the five precepts, or the three precepts—be called the treasury of oceanic emptiness and wisdom? Such precepts are the bridge of dharma that transcends birth and death, abandoning evil and preventing transgressions. Contemplating the emptiness of dharma-nature, it is both empty and not empty; because it is not empty yet empty, this body of mine exists.

Now I observe this body: head, feet, ears, eyes, skin, flesh, sinews, bones, spleen, kidneys, heart, lungs, liver, gallbladder, intestines, stomach, the five sense organs and their repositories, excrement and urine, nasal mucus, tears, fat, marrow, membranes, pus, and blood—all are impure. Contemplating thus, who possesses this "I"? To whom does this "I" belong? Where does it dwell? To whom does it belong? Is it an animal? A hungry ghost? A human or heavenly being? A plant? An insect or fish?

Further, I reflect: Are these bones me? Or is it what is apart from the bones? Again, I reflect: The bones have different colors—blue, yellow, white—but such appearances of bone are not me. Why? The form of this body of mine is neither blue, yellow, nor white. Now I contemplate: This form of mine is not my true form.

Again, I reflect: These bones arise from causes and conditions. The bones of the feet support the ankles; the bones of the ankles support the shanks; the bones of the shanks support the knees; the bones of the knees support the thighs; the bones of the thighs support the hips; the bones of the hips support the waist; the bones of the waist support the chest; the bones of the chest support the ribs; the bones of the ribs support the neck; the bones of the neck support the jaw; the bones of the jaw support the teeth; the bones of the teeth support the skull. Further, the bones of the neck support the shoulders; the bones of the shoulders support the arms; the bones of the arms support the wrists; the bones of the wrists support the palms; the bones of the palms support the fingers.

Good man, observing thus, I see the various causes and conditions, the various appearances of bones—these are my supports, my pillars. When I contemplate this body, all its bones are separate. Having attained this contemplation, I sever all desires.

Again, I reflect: The birth and death of this body are like flowing water, and it is not me. If consciousness is not me, then sometimes it is born, sometimes it dies—sometimes it is me, sometimes it is not. Again, I reflect: Am I a transformation? Or not a transformation? Am I composed of the four great elements? Or not composed of them? Among the four great elements, which is me, and which is not me?

Good man, it is like a *konghou* harp: as the wind passes, some strings produce sound, some do not. Good man, the four great elements compose me in the same way. Thus, this body of mine is a harmony of causes and conditions, like an illusion, arising with sound, taking on various forms and creations.

All you beings should single-mindedly receive and uphold the secret treasury precepts of the One Vehicle’s ocean of emptiness.

Then, Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom rose from his seat, bowed before the Dao, and addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "As you have spoken, if there are beings—good men and good women—who single-mindedly, with right mindfulness, reverently praise and uphold the pure precepts of the One Vehicle, constantly mindful and protective, then should outer demons come to disturb and confuse them, my disciples will sever their lives to cut off those outer demons. For such disciples, there is no possibility of falling into hell. Why? These disciples are my divine warriors, my mighty ones, who protect beings in upholding pure precepts. How could such a person fall into hell?"

Then, the Heavenly Worthy praised Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom, saying: "Excellent, excellent, good man, just as you have spoken."

In times past, I transformed and was born below as a great king named Dharma Radiance. Constantly, I received and recited the Mahāyāna sutras with a mind of reverent faith, free from coarse malice or envy. My speech was ever gentle and kind, and I distributed wealth to the poor, the orphaned, and the solitary. With courageous diligence, I never rested.

At that time, I heard that in the eastern quarter there existed the wondrous Mahāyāna sutra *Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom*. Overcome with sorrow, I wept uncontrollably, and throughout the kingdom, the queen, the crown prince, and all the ministers wept with me. Then, dragons, unicorns, lions, phoenixes, peacocks, parrots, and white cranes all gathered in flight.

Thereupon, a great minister, gazing upon the king’s countenance—now bright and composed—addressed the king, saying: "Why do we hear the sound of weeping?" The king replied: "I have heard that in the east there is the Mahāyāna sutra *Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom*. Yet I, the king, regret that I cannot go there myself. This is why I grieve."
