At that time, a great elder in the kingdom harbored evil thoughts, slandering in various ways and fostering disbelief. He addressed the king, saying: "I have heard that the *One Vehicle Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom* is but an illusion, a fabrication of the Daoists." In an instant, the elder’s body turned yellow and red, worms and foul odors flowed from him, his hair and fur fell out, his form became that of a hungry ghost, and his neck swelled like an ox’s. The king then severed his life. Through this cause, he did not fall into hell.

Good man, the majestic power and awe-inspiring dignity of upholding and cherishing the wondrous treasury of the One Vehicle sutra are thus—vast and unthinkable.

Good man, when beings abide in the world, they face the hardships of the Three Realms and the sufferings of illness. What are these sufferings? The suffering of birth, the suffering of sickness, the suffering of death, the suffering of enmity, the suffering of hatred, the suffering of separation, and the suffering of parting. Thus, beings are afflicted by the suffering of karmic hindrances. Wherever they are born, they are all consumed by desire, for they do not see old age, sickness, and death.

Good man, it is like a poisonous tiger whose mouth can kill a person, and whose paws and claws can do the same. Beings in the Three Realms, abiding in existence, are likewise.

Good man, it is like a land across the great sea where sweet dew abounds. Those who partake of it live for three thousand years, free from illness and suffering, at peace and joyful. Yet foolish people, craving its taste, prepare ships and set sail to obtain it, unaware that in the sea there are great scaled fish that can swallow ships whole. When those people set out, they do not know the great fish has already devoured their ship. Thus, the wise do not crave that taste and remain secure.

Good man, the true person, the youth, does not desire the taste of afflictions, and it is the same. Good man, the true person, the youth, abiding in the *Oceanic Treasury*, observes the suffering of afflictions just as the wise observe the fish and the ship, without delight.

Good man, people grow old and decline, yet they constantly seek joy in desire. It is like a lotus born in a pond, blooming fresh and splendid, delightful to behold. Yet when frost and hail come, all is destroyed.

Good man, the joy of human life, the desire for sensual pleasure, and the afflictions that assail the body—falling into the sufferings of the Three Wretched Realms—are likewise. It is like a broken axle, no longer of use. Old age is the same; one cannot return to youth.

It is like a land tortoise whose heart constantly longs for water. Good man, it is the same: though aged in appearance, one ever recalls the vigor of youth.

It is like the lotus in a pond in autumn, once the delight of all who saw it, suddenly withered and yellow, despised and discarded. Good man, the prime of youth and the beauty of strength are likewise—once the delight of all, yet suddenly aged and despised by all.

Good man, it is like sugarcane, once pressed, its dregs devoid of flavor. Good man, the vigor and prosperity of youth are likewise: once aged, desire is no more.

Good man, it is like polishing a mirror, which one holds daily, never parting from one’s heart. Good man, people are the same: in the prime of youth, their splendor is whole, but in old age, they become frail and emaciated, their spirit and form withered, ever longing for their youth, never parting from their heart.

Good man, the true person, the youth, cultivating the *Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom* of the One Vehicle, observes the suffering of illness with constant fear and unease. Good man, it is like an enemy, ever a source of sorrow. The true person, the youth, is likewise: observing afflictions, ever sorrowful.

It is like rice infested with borers, which die at the joints. Good man, people are the same: when illness strikes, it is difficult to cure, and in an instant, they die.

It is like a royal procession where the ministers go ahead and the king follows behind. When they near the enemy’s ranks, the king and his ministers pursue one another, unable to part. Good man, the true person, the youth, is likewise: following beings in their illness, unable to leave them, observing their suffering to bring them peace.

Good man, the true person, the youth, cultivating the treasury of the Mahāyāna sutras, observes the suffering of beings’ death and decay as a conflagration. It can consume all things, save only the jeweled terrace, beyond its reach. Good man, when a disastrous fire arises, it burns and destroys all things, yet the true person abiding in the *Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom* of the Great Vehicle remains untouched by the flames.

It is like a flood that submerges all, save only Penglai, beyond its power. Good man, the flood submerges the Three Realms, and all beings are swept away—save only the true person who abides in the great vessel of the One Vehicle, the *Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom*.

Furthermore, it is like the parrot, which can mimic sounds and speak, causing the phoenix and peacock to come and circle in dance. Good man, when the true person, the youth, upholds this sutra, all beings come to praise and extol him, just so.

Then the Heavenly Venerable, with eyes of compassion and kindness, gazed upon the beings in hell, the hungry ghosts, humans, and non-humans, each weeping and wailing: "Alas for us, born in hell! Shackles, fetters, and cangues bind and strike our bodies; day after day we die and are reborn, without respite." At that time, a hungry ghost, naked after ten thousand kalpas, reflected to himself: "How did I come to be born in this place of suffering? What did I do in the past—was it slander? Greed and attachment? Perverse views? Or wicked rebellion?" Then a hungry ghost in the form of a bare skull pondered: "Why now are my bones and flesh scattered, enduring manifold torments, dying and being reborn day after day, never knowing a moment’s peace? What did I do before—was it robbery and theft? Or abandoning others? In my suffering now, do I have parents who grieve for me alone? Where are my parents, siblings, and the hundred kin bound to me by love?" Having thought thus, each wept and wailed, beating their arms in grief.

Then the Heavenly Venerable transformed into a bull-headed being and addressed them: "Hungry ghosts, have you seen the immortals in the heavens above?" The hungry ghosts replied: "Truly, we have seen them." He asked again: "Have you seen the fragrant rice, the wondrous flavors, and the sweet dew medicine in heaven?" The hungry ghosts answered: "Truly, we have seen them." Then the bull-headed being said to the hungry ghosts: "Those immortals are your younger brothers. Once, in a royal household, you were the eldest brother, ever committing wickedness, killing without restraint, indulging in lust and desire, seizing the wives of others, relying on your strength to oppress the weak, and arrogantly asserting your own way. Your brother was ever compassionate, giving alms to the poor, delighting in mountains and rivers, and seeking the Dao and its virtue in seclusion. But you cut him off and would not walk the same path."

The younger brother attained flight as an immortal, and heaven bestowed upon him fragrant rice and wondrous sweet dew flavors. But you have become hungry ghosts, suffering unbearable hunger and thirst."

Then, upon hearing these words, the hungry ghosts wept together, their sobs rumbling like thunder. In that moment, all in hell—whether male or female, human or non-human—raised their hands, lifted their fists toward the sky, and cried out: "Alas! Alas!"

Thereupon, the torments of hell ceased entirely, and all within, whether male or female, sat in peace. Then, a celestial immortal in the sky addressed the hungry ghosts: "Now, I offer you sweet dew—will you partake?" He continued: "This sweet dew can free all beings from hunger and thirst, from birth and death, from suffering and joy."

The hungry ghosts replied: "In our desperate starvation, how could we refuse?"

The immortal then bestowed the sweet dew, and the hungry ghosts—one, two, ten, a hundred, a thousand, ten million—all were sated without exception. The immortal then said to the hungry ghosts: "I possess a wondrous medicine—will you take it? This medicine can sever all suffering and afflictions, allowing beings to dwell in bliss."

The hungry ghosts each answered: "We endure a thousandfold torment—we beg for deliverance."

The immortal then conferred the One Vehicle of the Ocean-Empty Pure Precepts. Upon receiving the precepts, the hungry ghosts instantly transformed, their forms reborn in beauty, and they gained clear understanding of the roots of good and evil across the three times.

Furthermore, good man, the Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury knows boundless expedient means, transforming and delivering beings, removing the city of suffering. Good man, it is like a fine medicine that eradicates all manner of illness in beings. Good man, it is like a wise person who comprehends all languages and serves as a great translator for all beings. Good man, it is like pure gold, which can be fashioned into any adornment according to one’s wishes. Good man, the Ocean-Empty is likewise: ever teaching the Dharma, discerning the varied dispositions of beings, expounding with expedient means, enabling all beings to perceive the absence of self. Because there is no self, all conditioned things are impermanent. Why? Through this cause and condition, all dharmas are without self. If there were a self, one would know it to be impermanent. Among all beings—including these hungry ghosts—there is not a single dharma that does not arise from conditions. Through this cause and condition, the wheel of birth and death turns.

Then, Ocean-Empty addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "How can all dharmas arise without self? If there is no self, there is also no enmity or kinship. If there is no enmity or kinship, why do the hungry ghosts weep together?"

The Heavenly Venerable replied: "Good man, I now expound the impermanence of all dharmas and the absence of self to enable beings to contemplate non-self and the absence of arising. Because there is no arising, what arises is already extinguished—like lightning, like a spark from stone, like a flame, like a dream, like an illusion, like a magical transformation. Good man, this body of mine arises from parents, and when the parents perish, this body of mine also perishes without arising. Therefore, know that all dharmas are without self. Through this cause and condition, all is impermanent. Good man, enmity and kinship among hungry ghosts arise from conditions. Why? It is like merchants carrying miscellaneous treasures to distant lands, seeking various gains, only to be suddenly harmed by bandits and lose their lives. Good man, it is like foolish attachment to kin and beauty, rushing east and west day and night, only to be suddenly poisoned—just so. Furthermore, it is like officials who rely on their power to oppress the people, acting lawlessly, only to be suddenly seized, shackled in cangues and fetters, their bodies bound and emaciated, as if afflicted by a century of illness. Good man, all beings who rely on the three poisons and indulge in the ten evils suddenly meet their end and transform into hungry ghosts or hell’s ox-headed tormentors, suffering ceaseless torture—just so."

Then, Ocean-Empty addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "Such teachings are difficult to fathom—subtle and supreme, the Dharma Wheel turns universally, discerning true nature with profound analogies. The Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury is replete with secret treasures of merit, benefiting beings and delivering all, like a benevolent ship crossing the sea of birth and death."

The Heavenly Venerable replied: "Excellent, excellent, good man! Why do you now conceive of manifold notions within the One Vehicle? Good man, the Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury is truly profound, its subtle merit unchanging and undifferentiated, serene and eternally abiding, like empty space. Good man, if any being regards the Ocean-Empty Treasury as their own body, then I am eternally abiding, indestructible and imperishable. I am the Ocean-Empty, and the Ocean-Empty is I; I am the Dao, and the Dao is I; I am the Heavenly Venerable, and the Heavenly Venerable is I. I am the One Vehicle of the Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury’s secret treasure, which expounds the wondrous Dharma, enabling all beings to listen, receive, and praise—this is my Dharma Wheel. If one claims, 'I am eternally abiding, without change,' how can it be said that the great Dharma Wheel turns? Therefore, you should declare that only the Heavenly Venerable and superior beings can turn the great Dharma Wheel. Good man, it is like the six senses: the eye depends on form, form depends on thought, and through their interdependent arising, eye-consciousness is born. Good man, the eye does not think, 'I can generate consciousness,' nor does thought say, 'I give rise to eye-consciousness.' Good man, all such dharmas arise through interdependent conditions—this is my Dharma Wheel. Good man, the Heavenly Venerable is likewise: through the six senses, he perceives all dharmas, and through the throat, tongue, teeth, lips, speech, and sound, he turns the great Dharma Wheel."

For this reason, one never thinks, "I turn the Dharma Wheel." Good man, it is like wood and fire: through the hand and the drill, fire is generated. Yet when fire arises, it never thinks, "This hand and drill have given birth to me," nor does it say, "I can generate myself." Good man, the Heavenly Venerable constantly turns the Dharma Wheel, yet never generates the thought, "I turn the Dharma Wheel." Good man, if no such thought arises, this is called turning the True Dharma Wheel. This turning of the Dharma Wheel is named the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Treasure Repository.

Furthermore, good man, long ago beneath the Kien-wood tree, I first turned the Dharma Wheel. Ninety thousand devas came together to observe and listen, all arousing faith and delighting in the Dharma, without rising from their seats. At that time, the devas immediately attained the supreme, subtle, and wondrous true fruit. Now, within this city of seven treasures, I first expound the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Treasure Repository, and again, eight million four hundred thousand devas abide in their seats, their faith unwavering. At that time, the devas immediately attained the four pure fruits of the heavenly paths.

Furthermore, good man, whenever the Heavenly Venerable expounds the Dharma, it is all called turning the Dharma Wheel. Why? It is like the precious wheel of a sagely king: this Wheel-Treasure enables beings to reach the secure city, revolving above and below without enemies or thieves. Good man, the Dharma is likewise: it transports beings to a place of peace, free from afflictions. Good man, you should now praise the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Wisdom-Treasure Repository as the True Dharma Wheel, whose meritorious virtues are subtle and inconceivable.

Then, Ocean-Empty addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "Heavenly Venerable, when you expound this Dharma, it is the great Dharma Wheel. It is not that you are unaware—my question was for the benefit of all beings, to broadly elucidate the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Wisdom-Treasure’s secret Dharma Wheel, which is not something that ordinary beings or lesser immortals and scholars can comprehend."

Then, the Heavenly Venerable replied to Ocean-Empty: "Excellent, Ocean-Empty, good man. You have already abided in the ground of the Great Vehicle, practicing the true practice and asking the true question. Good man, in the past, when I took the form of a being, I cultivated the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Dharma Wheel, fully penetrating all external demons, subduing their minds so they could not destroy it. I was able to uphold the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Wisdom Dharma Wheel and thought: 'The meritorious virtues of the secret treasure repository of the Single Vehicle’s Dharma Wheel are inconceivable. We beings should abandon this foul corpse and remove the defiled qi-body of external demons.'"

At that time, the demon kings among the assembly, having heard these words, immediately prepared a great feast, offering their wealth, treasures, beloved wives and children, houses and dwellings, elephants, horses, chariots, servants, and attendants—all scattered in offering. They adorned the place with pure incense and flowers, various ornaments, and came to the Dharma assembly to repent their past transgressions.

Then, the Heavenly Venerable, raising his hand to touch the table, replied to the demons: "Good man, all ordinary beings fail to properly restrain the six senses and commit evil, thereby generating afflictions. Drawn by evil, they reach unwholesome places. Good man, it is like a vicious horse, fierce and stubborn, which leads its rider to perilous places. Failing to restrain the six senses and committing evil is likewise, causing one to stray far from the Ocean-Empty’s good path and reach evil destinations. It is like a wild elephant whose mind is untamed: if someone rides it, it does not follow their will, leaving the city behind and entering the wilderness. Failing to restrain the six senses and committing evil is likewise, leading one far from the Ocean-Empty Treasure City into the wilderness of birth and death.

Good man, it is like a treacherous minister who teaches the king to do evil. The six senses, like treacherous ministers, constantly teach beings to commit boundless evils. Good man, it is like a wicked child who does not heed the teachings of teachers, parents, or elders, committing every kind of evil. Failing to tame the six senses is likewise, not following the good instructions of teachers and elders, committing every kind of evil. Good man, ordinary beings who do not restrain the six senses are constantly harmed by hell-beings, animals, and hungry ghosts, just as bandits harm good people.

Good man, ordinary beings who do not restrain the three poisons gallop through the five sense-objects, like a cowherd who fails to guard his cattle, allowing them to trample others’ crops. Ordinary beings who do not restrain the three poisons constantly dwell in existence, enduring much suffering. Good man, true persons and youths who cultivate the Great Vehicle sutras and practice the great sagely path constantly and skillfully regulate and restrain the three poisons, fearing greed, anger, ignorance, arrogance, and jealousy, for the sake of attaining all good dharmas.

Good man, if one properly guards these two roots of poison, one can restrain the mind; if one can restrain the mind, one can restrain the three poisons. Good man, it is like someone who protects their body and thereby protects the land; protecting the land is protecting the body. True persons and youths are likewise. If they hear and see the subtle sutras of the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty, they attain wisdom; attaining wisdom, they attain focused mindfulness. If the six senses scatter, mindfulness can halt them. Why? Because of the power of wisdom."

Good man, it is like a skillful cowherd: if the cattle wander east or west and eat others’ sprouts and crops, he immediately blocks and stops them, not allowing them to eat the sprouts. True persons and youths are likewise. Through the causes and conditions of focused mindfulness and wisdom, they guard and restrain the six senses, not allowing them to scatter and stray.

True persons and youths, with the mind of focused mindfulness and wisdom, do not perceive the mark of self, nor the mark of what is perceived, nor the mark of sentient beings, nor what is received and used. They see all dharmas as sharing the mark of dharma-nature, arising with the marks of lifeless stone, tiles, and rubble. It is like a house, which arises from various conditions yet has no fixed nature. Seeing all sentient beings as established by the four great elements and the five aggregates, they discern that there is no fixed nature; because there is no fixed nature, beings revolve in birth and death.

True persons and youths do not generate attachment in birth and death. Seeing sentient beings conceive notions of affliction within affliction, they therefore invoke the secret treasure-store of the Single Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty, desiring to enable beings to create various dharmas, to make various causes, to build great ships, and to construct great Dharma bridges.

Good man, it is like a painter who, with various mixed pigments, paints many images—whether of men or women, of cows or horses. The ignorant common person, seeing them, generates the marks of men, women, and so on. The painter, however, knows there are no men or women. True persons and youths are likewise. Observing the various marks of dharmas, they contemplate the one mark and ultimately do not generate the mark of sentient beings. Why? Because of the power of focused mindfulness and wisdom.

The True Person Youth, cultivating the *Great Vehicle Ocean-Empty Treasure Sutra*, at that time observes a woman of upright beauty yet does not generate a mind of attachment. Why? Because he contemplates her form. Good man, the True Person Youth knows that desire-thought holds no joy, cannot pause even briefly—like a dog gnawing bone; like one who meets fire yet walks against the wind; like a charcoal-poisoned pool, a dream’s ill-gotten gain, a medicine tree at the borderlands cast aside by many; like meat devoured while birds compete in pursuit; like bubbles on water, like traces drawn in water; like a woven warp exhausted, like a prisoner led to market, like a borrowed thing whose power cannot endure. Contemplating desire thus, he sees its many faults and evils.

Good man, the True Person Youth sees sentient beings attached to the touch of fragrance, flavor, and sound. From time immemorial through countless kalpas, they have constantly endured suffering and affliction. For each being, the bones accumulated in a single kalpa would form a mountain like Yujing; the milk they have drunk would equal the waters of the four seas. When parents, siblings, wives, children, and kin die, the tears shed in lamentation surpass the four great oceans. Even the stars in the void could not match their number, nor could parents and siblings ever exhaust them. Through measureless kalpas, some have fallen into hells, animal realms, or hungry ghost states, enduring boundless suffering in birth and death beyond reckoning.

Good man, the True Person Youth deeply observes thus: all sentient beings endure such afflictions, and therefore, with compassionate mindfulness, he does not generate suffering in the cycle of birth and death. Good man, it is like a great assembly in the world, spanning three thousand *li* in every direction. Then the great king commands a worthy minister to carry a jar of honey through their midst, forbidding even a single drop to spill. Should he lose one drop, his life would be forfeit. The king further dispatches a fierce warrior with drawn blade to follow behind, instilling terror. The minister, accepting the king’s decree, holds the jar with utmost care. Passing through the assembly, though he sees the five sense-desires of the multitude, his mind constantly reflects: *If I indulge my senses and cling to those desires, I will lose the king’s honey jar. If I lose the king’s jar, how can my life be preserved?* For this reason, he holds it firmly, not losing a single drop.

Good man, the True Person Youth is likewise. Passing through the afflictions and cycle of birth and death, he does not lose wisdom. Because he does not lose it, though he sees the five desires, his mind does not cling. If he sees pure form, he does not generate the perception of form but only observes its suffering aspect. Likewise with perceptions of consciousness. He does not conceive of arising, does not conceive of cessation, does not conceive of causation, does not conceive of harmonious union, but generates the perception of wisdom. The True Person Youth, abiding in this state, with the five faculties purified, thus upholds and maintains the precepts. All ordinary beings, with impure five faculties, cannot uphold the complete precepts nor properly preserve the merit of true nature. Therefore, the True Immortal Youth constantly severs [afflictions], thus attaining the fruit of the unconditioned, abiding in constant joy and freedom, extracting himself from the conditioned, forever cutting off afflictions, and perfecting merit.

Good man, there is also the departure from desire. The Youth constantly practices the unsurpassed treasury of the sweet-dew Dharma, thus departing from evil and afflictive karma. What is departure? Good man, if there are sentient beings who can well cultivate the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Subtle Secret Treasure Store*, transcribe, receive, uphold, recite, expound, and contemplate its meaning and flavor, they transcend the worldly cycle of birth, death, and affliction. For this reason, this is called departure from evil. Why? This sutra elucidates the Three Caverns and Seven Sections, the talismans and charts of the Dao, and scriptures such as the *Great Peace*. Good man, it is like a wise teacher guiding sentient beings. Among them, should there be one who can well contemplate, faithfully receive the teachings, and uphold the commands—whose mind does not create evil, whose mouth does not speak falsely, who departs from familial attachment and abandons the body of affliction—good man, the True Person Youth is likewise. Well contemplating the wise teacher’s command, the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Subtle Secret Treasure Store*, his mind does not create evil, his mouth does not speak falsely.

Good man, it is like a fine medicine in the world. If sentient beings take it with faith, for the duration of their lives, they will not be harmed by any evil poison. Further, one who proclaims this fine medicine, even until the end of life, will be free from all evil. Good man, the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty* is likewise—the finest medicine in the world. If one can well receive, uphold, recite, expound, and contemplate its meaning and flavor, for the duration of their life, they will not fall into evil destinies. Further, one who proclaims the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury* will attain rebirth among humans and gods, with exceptional form and marks. Good man, if there are sentient beings who can well transcribe it—with pure body and hands, arranging the characters in order like jade slips—they will surely attain the wisdom of a divine youth, standing in attendance upon the Heavenly Worthy, their form as majestic as that of a radiant king.

Good man, the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Subtle Secret Treasure Store* possesses such measureless merits, difficult to conceive. If there are sentient beings who expound it for others and contemplate its meaning and flavor, know that such a person is a true disciple of mine, one who well receives and upholds my teachings, one whom I protect and cherish. Such a person can comprehend my marks. Wherever they dwell—whether in mountains, forests, remote wilderness, dwellings, fields, mansions, pavilions, or palaces—I also abide there, constantly and immovably. In such places, I always receive offerings: sometimes as a Daoist, silently contemplating; sometimes as a worthy one, skillfully expounding the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty True Dao Treasury*.

Or as a poor scholar, approaching doors to beg for alms.
How then may such a person come to know that I, in such places, receive the offerings of others, constantly transforming my body and manifesting in accordance with the region?

Good man, such a person dwelling therein, in the depths of night, dreams of seeing divine beings upon jeweled thrones expounding the Dharma, with jade maidens and immortal youths standing in attendance; or sees heavenly beings, Daoist immortals in their true forms, kings and sagely rulers, princes and royal figures; or beholds great mountains and lesser peaks; or sees rivers and streams, the sun and moon; or oxen and sheep, elephants and horses, carriages and chariots; or parents, siblings, uncles and elders bearing the seven treasures—gold, silver, lapis lazuli, true pearls, and other precious things—approaching the Dharma site to make offerings with faith.
At that moment, know that it is the Heavenly Worthy who receives their offerings.
Upon awakening from such a dream, filled with joy, one soon obtains all manner of subtle and wondrous things.
Thereupon, one reflects thus, the mind free of evil thoughts, universally practicing loving-kindness and delighting in the cultivation of wholesome dharmas.

Good man, the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty* is likewise thus, able to accomplish such measureless merits, with devas and immortals receiving its boundless, inconceivable virtues.
Good man, you should now believe and accept my words.
If there are sentient beings—good men and good women—who desire the *Ocean-Empty*, who wish to perceive true reality, who seek to cultivate the secret treasury, who constantly delight in the Dao’s domain, who cast aside the four māras, who depart from the city of afflictions, who attain the joys of humans and devas, who uphold and practice the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Subtle Secret Treasure Store Sutra*, transcribing, reciting, and expounding it for others, contemplating its meaning and flavor—
you should draw near to them, rely upon them, seek their counsel, make offerings to them with reverence, honor and praise them, wash their hands and feet, prepare their seats, provide for all their needs, and ensure they lack nothing.
If they come from afar, you should go forth to meet them along the way, and for the sake of this sutra, present them with whatever you hold most precious.
Why? Because such sutras are difficult to encounter and rare to hear.
You should listen single-mindedly, receive, and uphold them.

Good man, I recall the immeasurable, boundless Heavenly Worthies of the past, future, and present, each assembling in great gatherings.
At that time, among the assembly, there was a Heavenly Worthy named *Formless*, who expounded for the great multitude this *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Subtle Secret Treasure Store*.
At that time, having heard it from a good friend, I grasped its meaning and flavor.
Now I shall expound for the assembly the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Treasure Store Sutra*.
When the great multitude heard this sutra, their hearts rejoiced greatly, and they established a grand feast.
Within the assembly, I transformed myself into a poor scholar, wandering about offering myself for sale, yet finding no buyer, and so prepared to return home.
Along the way, I encountered a man, and I said to him: "I wish to sell myself. Would you buy me?"
The man replied: "I am in need of a purchase, but I fear you may not comply."
I said: "What task would you have me do? Why doubt my sincerity?"
The man replied: "There is a grave illness in my household. The great physician prescribed medicine requiring human eyes. If you would provide them, I shall give you seven gold coins daily for their use."
Upon hearing this, my heart leapt with boundless joy. At that very moment, I offered my pair of wisdom eyes—luminous as moonlit pupils, their brilliance manifest in their orbs.
I said: "Give me the coins. I now offer you both eyes for your use."
Thereupon, the man gave me the gold.
Having received it, I returned to my original seat, established a grand feast, made offerings with reverence, and then listened to the sutra with a sincere heart.
At that time, though dull-witted, I was able to receive and uphold but a single phrase, a single character of the *Single Vehicle Treasure Store*.
Having received and upheld it, I immediately returned to the sick household.
Though I daily bestowed my luminous eyes upon them, I constantly contemplated the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Treasure Store*, my body free of pain, my daily practice unceasing, until the month’s end.
Through this cause and condition, the illness was cured, and my body restored, without wound or scar.
At that time, I beheld my body complete with perfect, subtle, and wondrous marks.
I then reflected: the power of a single phrase from the *Single Vehicle Ocean-Empty Subtle Secret Treasure Store* is already thus—how much more so for one who fully receives, upholds, expounds, recites, and contemplates its meaning and flavor?
Seeing this sutra’s power, I aroused the aspiration that in the future, all sentient beings might attain the immortal Dao, mastering the *Single Vehicle Subtle Secret Treasure Store Sutra* in its entirety.
Good man, by the power of this single phrase’s cause and condition, I am now able to expound the *Single Vehicle Treasure Store* for the devas and humans in this great assembly.

Good man, the *Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury* is inconceivable, benefiting all beings with boundless, immeasurable virtues.
Such is its profound, secret meaning.
Good man, if there are sentient beings who can well receive and uphold it, they will sever and depart from evil roots.
What is evil? Evil thoughts, evil intentions, evil illnesses, evil reflections—all such evils they will be able to distance themselves from, thereby growing and abiding in wholesome roots.
Wholesome roots, wholesome reflections; wisdom and skillful means—through such causes and conditions, this is called "departing from evil."

Good man, the true person, the youth dwelling in the city of afflictions, observes their own body as if it were a sickness, a wound, a poisoned arrow piercing the flesh.
Such a body is a great mass of suffering, the root of both good and evil.
For this reason, one regards the body not with attachment, for to nourish it is to sustain the body of a hungry ghost, the body of hell, the body of birth and death.
Good man, it is like a raging fire consuming withered wood, or a plantain tree struck by frost and hail, like lightning’s flash, like a flame, like an illusion.
Good man, the true person, the youth dwelling in the city of afflictions, observes the body’s marks—it is likewise thus.

If one can depart from the body of birth and death and abide in the treasure repository of the single vehicle of sea and emptiness, one will then attain the body adorned with seventy-two marks and eighty-one subtle excellences, accomplishing merit and virtue, becoming a Dharma-wheel king who forever guards the body.

Why is this so? If the body is not guarded, life is not preserved; if life is not preserved, one cannot transcribe this sutra, receive, uphold, recite, or expound its meaning and flavor. Therefore, one should guard and preserve body and life. For this reason, the true person, the youth dwelling in the city of afflictions, departs from all evil and protects body and life.

Good man, it is like beings who wish to cross the sea: they carefully guard their vessel to reach the other shore. The true person, the youth, is likewise thus.

At that time, Sea-Emptiness and the assembled devas, celestial immortals, and youths, having heard these words, rejoiced greatly in their hearts. They received and upheld the teaching, listened attentively, grasped its meaning and flavor, then all rose to pay homage. Each returned to their own realm, taking leave and departing.

*Thus concludes Fascicle Six of the* Supreme Single Vehicle Treasure Repository of Sea-Emptiness Wisdom. *Variant: Dunhuang manuscript reads "good marks" instead of "good roots."*

**Fascicle Seven: The Chapter on Equality**

At that time, Sea-Emptiness Wisdom Repository addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: "Today, I have but a shallow understanding. When true persons and boundless youths practice the mind of the Dao, cultivating kindness, compassion, joy, and equanimity, they attain the true Dharma ground. When they cultivate the mind of equanimity, when they cultivate wisdom, what Dharma do they gain after accumulating such merits for measureless kalpas? What benefits do true persons and youths obtain by knowing these merits thus?"

"The Heavenly Venerable now speaks these secret and essential words. If one does not grasp at them, one does not know the Dharma; yet if one grasps at them, that is grasping. If one does not grasp at them, then one knows nothing—how then does the Heavenly Venerable speak of the Dharma as not to be grasped? Among this assembly, I do not recognize the fundamental principle, do not comprehend the mark of emptiness, do not understand all things. I only pray that the Heavenly Venerable will descend and graciously expound."

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable replied to Sea-Emptiness Wisdom Repository, saying: "Good man, you know the right time and perceive that I am about to speak, so you inquire thus. When true persons and youths cultivate the mind of equanimity and cultivate wisdom, they attain the unconditioned, abide in constant peace and bliss, and dwell in the true, empty, and equal Dharma ground—the inconceivable, subtle, and wondrous realm. Like the supreme Dao, it is difficult to compare, like the great sea, like the vast emptiness."

"Good man, when true persons and youths abide in the empty and equal ground, which is difficult to surpass, they do not see father, mother, brothers, relatives, acquaintances, sisters, children, or those who are hateful and resentful. Just as emptiness has no father, mother, or brothers, nor even any sentient beings or lifespans, all dharmas are likewise thus. Their minds are equal, benefiting many, like emptiness itself. Why is this? Because by practicing merits, they skillfully cultivate all the Dharmas of emptiness. This inner Dharma is empty, yet it is constant, blissful, self, and pure, attaining fearlessness. Within this inner Dharma, though there is the nature of the Dao, this nature is neither external nor internal, neither non-existent nor existent, equal and without duality. Why is this? Because the true nature is eternally abiding and unchanging. This is called a true person, a youth, contemplating inner emptiness. Because the inner Dharma is empty, they contemplate all dharmas as originally empty in nature, without permanence, suffering, or joy, without purity or impurity—this is called the emptiness of Dharma. Because of the emptiness of Dharma, it is called empty emptiness."

"Good man, true persons and youths of the ten directions constantly penetrate a fraction of this, like a speck of dust—how much more so others? Good man, when true persons and youths contemplate this gate of emptiness, which is empty yet not empty, they attain dwelling in the Dharma ground of emptiness. Good man, when I now speak of these meanings of emptiness to the great assembly, hundreds of thousands of true persons and youths immediately attain dwelling in the Dharma ground of emptiness. Good man, once true persons and youths abide in this ground, they are without obstruction, bondage, or attachment in all dharmas; their minds are free from confusion, constantly attaining self-mastery, purity, and liberation. For these reasons, it is called the pure Dharma ground of emptiness."

"Good man, Sea-Emptiness Wisdom Repository, it is like emptiness: it does not generate greed for lovable forms, nor does it generate anger toward unloved forms. True persons and youths abiding in this ground are likewise thus. In all dharmas, they demonstrate knowledge and practice, whether causes and conditions, effects and non-conditions, causes and effects, root natures, refined contemplation, the Great Vehicle, good-knowing advisors, pure precepts, or abundant giving. In all such dharmas, they know and see the supreme liberation, the profound practices, and the foremost wisdom. They see sentient beings practicing unwholesome dharmas, inevitably falling into hells, enduring measureless suffering and affliction. Like sentient beings emerging from hells and being born among humans, if they practice giving and fulfill all such acts of generosity, they will certainly enter right liberation. This is called knowing Sea-Emptiness Wisdom Repository, true persons, and youths. There are also those who see and know in other ways."

"What is seeing? Seeing the constant and the impermanent, seeing purity and impurity, seeing self and no-self. Knowing that the divine venerables are definitely not ultimately subject to birth and death, knowing that the bodies of divine venerables are indestructible like vajra, not bodies constituted by afflictions, nor bodies of foul decay. They also know that all sentient beings possess the nature of the Dao. Good man, knowing that the minds of these sentient beings are accomplished in faith, knowing that these sentient beings seek the Great Vehicle—such a person is from the stream, yet not of the stream; such a person abides rightly, knowing that at the time of birth, they have already reached the other shore, abiding in the Great Vehicle, attaining the profound flavor of the Dharma, the fundamental principle of the Dharma, and right liberation. Cultivating the mind of pure conduct, with the pure divine eye, they see sentient beings creating unwholesome bodily, verbal, and mental actions—sexual misconduct, theft, and the three unwholesome karmas—falling into hells, animal realms, and hungry ghost realms, enduring unbearable suffering, tormented by wind and blades."

"They see sentient beings cultivating wholesome actions, diligent and vigorous, who in their next lives will be born in heavenly or human realms. They see sentient beings moving from darkness to darkness, benighted and confused; some moving from darkness to light, with clear understanding and knowledge; some moving from light to darkness, abandoning truth for falsehood; and some moving from light to light. Good man, if unwholesome karma is accomplished through greed, anger, or delusion, such karma will inevitably result in hellish retribution. Such persons, by merely upholding precepts and practicing these deeds, do not fall into hells. By repenting and revealing all their evils, having repented, they dare not commit them again, accomplishing shame and remorse. Thus, with a single mind, they make offerings to the Three Treasures. For these reasons, they do not fall into hells."

Those whose offenses intersect with retribution suffer headaches, abdominal pains, eye pains, back pains, untimely calamities and deaths, rebukes and insults, whippings and beatings, confinement and strikes, hunger and hardship, unfulfilled desires, thwarted endeavors, and manifold sorrows and afflictions—these are not merely isolated cases. Enduring such boundless sufferings, they experience present-life retribution.

The Perfected Youth, the Golden Radiance Youth, and those who witness such persons, unaware of the causes and conditions, fail to repent. They do not reflect upon themselves, do not reproach themselves, do not generate shame or remorse, and harbor no fear. Thus, their offenses grow, and they receive hellish retribution. When will they attain liberation? They wander in endless darkness, cycling through bitter toil.

They see that all sentient beings possess the nature of the Dao, yet it is obscured by afflictions, preventing them from perceiving it—like a dark night where nothing is clearly seen. What they perceive are merely worldly words and speech: men and women, carriages and vessels, houses and cities, clothing and food, mountains and seas, forests and trees, the lifespans of sentient beings—these are called "what is seen."

The subtle teachings of the sages transcend male and female, extending even to forests and trees. They know what to bestow and how to offer equally, understand diligence, recognize recipients, and comprehend the law of cause and effect.

The Perfected Youth knows the eightfold assembly of the Dharma’s origin, and his merit is none other than the five virtues of the Heavenly Worthy. What he knows is as luminous as form itself.

Good man, good woman, the Perfected Youth attains the four unimpeded eloquences and can follow the names established for all dharmas. The Perfected Youth, in all his teachings, encounters no obstruction, cannot be swayed, fears nothing, and is indomitable.

Good man, this is called the Perfected One. Within a single dharma, he expounds myriad names, and even after countless kalpas, his speech will not be exhausted.

Good man, all ordinary beings cling to form, and even to consciousness. Because of clinging to form, greed arises, and thus they are bound by form, even bound by consciousness. Therefore, they cannot escape birth, aging, sickness, death, sorrow, lamentation, suffering, and all afflictions.

Good man, for this reason, in teaching my disciples, I call those who strike and cling "demonic ghosts," who coil around the body and cannot be shaken off for an entire lifetime. If one does not cling, one is freed from demonic ghosts. It is like a criminal in the world who is shackled by officials, while the innocent are not. The Perfected Youth is likewise: those who cling are encoiled by demons, while those who do not are far from demonic ghosts and abide in constant freedom. The Perfected Youth is without attachment.

At that time, Haikong Zhizang addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Your servant is like fine silk, repeatedly refined to yield manifold flavors. I, too, having heard the Dao many times, have obtained the flavor of the Dharma. This Dharma-flavor is the taste of detachment from desires, the taste of tranquility, the taste of the true Dao."

Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, like true gold, repeatedly forged, melted, and tempered, becomes ever more radiant, pure, malleable, and lustrous, its value immeasurable. Only then is it treasured by humans and devas. The Heavenly Worthy is likewise: through earnest inquiry, one hears and sees the profound treasury of the Dharma, enabling those of deep faith to receive, uphold, and cultivate it. Countless beings awaken the mind for supreme enlightenment, and only then are they revered and honored by humans and devas."

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy praised Zhizang, saying: "Excellent, excellent! Perfected Youth of supreme, unconditioned wisdom, for the sake of benefiting all sentient beings, you have inquired into the profound meaning of the supreme Dao. Good man, for this reason, I expound the Great Vehicle in accordance with your intent, the treasury of profound, secret wisdom. It is cherished as dearly as an only child."

Then the Heavenly Worthy again addressed Haikong Zhizang: "You have deeply savored the Dharma-flavor, the foremost sublime practice, of boundless merit. Such a disciple is rare indeed." And he spoke in verse:

"Haikong Zhizang, all is indeterminate.
Provisionally gathering sentient beings—how could this not be emptiness?
The true nature of the five dusts—from where could they arise?
Since they cannot but be empty,
such matters are neither false nor deluded, neither existent nor inverted.
To speak of affliction and bondage is to give rise to perverse views.
If one does not believe in emptiness,
from where do all the leaks and dusts arise?
One then falls into the error of eternalism.
If they exist now, how could they be born?
Are they produced by conditions?
Do they dwell parasitically?
Do they arise without cause?
Or do they arise collectively?
Since they are equally unborn,
it is known that they are not real—
beyond thought and contemplation.

You have now become
the King of Virtue without limit,
without present or past,
without going or coming,
without thought or conception,
without hatred or love,
without birth or extinction.
Subduing toil and enmity,
manifesting the correct to dispel the perverse,
crushing all external paths,
eradicating all views—
profound in name and essence,
not to be sought in fixed form,
divine function beyond thought,
without any determinate appearance.

Understanding the emptiness of all dharmas,
Haikong Zhizang,
you who cultivate this Way—
your spirit shines deeply and far.
Knowing my profound mystery,
truly unshaken,
you gain the power of fearlessness,
the inconceivable,
able to know the ancient beginning—
this is called the principle of the Dao.

Previously unenlightened, now enlightened—
the seed of the Dao.
Why is this so?
The Heavenly Worthy’s wisdom
is boundless and immeasurable;
the meaning of the subtle and wondrous
is profound and far-reaching, difficult to fathom.
Forcibly describing its form,
its benevolent practice is beyond thought.

How can one attain
the manifestation of all dharmas?
All sentient beings
are deeply attached to the four perversities,
confused by manifold appearances,
not understanding, not recognizing,
indulging in greed and lust,
not practicing the four immeasurables.
Discriminating emptiness,
they can never attain it.
Returning to the root, restoring the mandate,
abiding in the Haikong Dao,
they pacify their minds—
Haikong Zhizang.

You should know
that tranquility has two kinds:
The first is tranquil with existence,
with thoughts, reflections, and contemplations,
constantly mindful of pure practice—
the One Vehicle of Haikong.
The second is empty tranquility,
thoughts vast as the sea,
constantly mindful of pure practice—
thus preserving oneness.
Next, entering emptiness,
one attains the gateway of the empty Dao,
only then reaching the profound origin,
fully realizing ultimate tranquility.
Tranquilizing all distinctions,
all existence returns to emptiness;
emptying tranquility itself,
tranquilizing all dharmas.
Thus expounding,
the principle of emptiness is true emptiness.

Why is this so?
Because all sentient beings
were originally self-purified,
but deludedly arose discriminations,
leading to wandering and transmigration,
sinking into the paths of suffering.
Whether male or female,
if one does not give rise
to manifold perverse views,
understanding that forms are empty,
one returns to restore the mandate,
becoming a child of the Dao,
pacifying the mind,
entering the Haikong Treasury,
contemplating the emptiness of all dharmas.

Haikong Zhizang,
you and the present assembly,
being unable to comprehend,
must have this expounded.
Now speaking these words
is for the sake of future ages,
that those who benefit from the Dharma,
returning to the source in emptiness and tranquility,
may become my disciples—
tranquil and constant,
attaining the Dao, eternally abiding,
unshaken and immovable.

Haikong Zhizang,
do you now understand?
What is the subtle body of the supreme Dao?
It does not long abide in the world,
fundamentally without arising or movement,
nor going or coming.
For the sake of sentient beings,
it manifests birth and extinction.
The great compassion of the true Dao
never abandons or forsakes—
why then does it manifest birth and extinction?
Because sentient beings
cannot abide constantly,
it deeply pities and sympathizes,
inconceivably.
Its mind cherishes sentient beings
as a mother loves her child.
Because sentient beings undergo birth and death,
it manifests birth and death.

The supreme Dao has no partiality,
only favoring the good.
It exhorts and awakens sentient beings,
offering them comfort.
With gentle words,
it enables them to understand and be subdued,
to seek the root of the Dao,
not to give rise to perverse views,
not to entertain evil thoughts,
to extinguish all manifold afflictions,
to practice with a constantly pure mind,
to be mindful and not retreat from the Dao.

Knowing these matters,
I now establish the precepts—
they should not go unspoken.
If one can be mindful and practice,
attaining the supreme Dao,
the virtues of manifesting dharmas
and the power of transformation and extinction are thus revealed.

You should know
that the mind’s actions become the body’s,
and four accomplishments are attained.
Whether male or female,
if one clings to perverse actions,
engaging in contention, killing, harming, and licentiousness,
giving rise to manifold evils,
like a venomous serpent,
losing the true principle—
those who seek the true, whether male or female,
must not give rise to such things.
Having attained this,
they awaken to that true source.

Those who deviate from the Dharma, whether male or female,
sink into this cycle of birth and death,
not drawing near to the ground of the Dao,
their blessed conditions receding day by day,
their evil conditions approaching.
Practicing right mindfulness,
they will surely attain
pure liberation,
unconditioned and free.

Good sons and good daughters,
when practicing these matters,
cultivate a magnanimous mind,
abandoning the four evils,
hastening to remove sorrow and affliction;
do not give rise to boasting and contention,
or to doubts and deluded thoughts.
Practice great merit,
acting with an unimpeded mind,
giving rise to the mind for all things.

Whether male or female,
if one takes this wondrous root as their source,
practicing this mindfulness,
thought after thought without retreat—
they are my true child.
Those who possess the Dao
constantly practice the supreme practice,
not dwelling in the four evils,
not engaging in perverse desires,
not entertaining any manifold perverse views;
not seeing what exists,
not seeing what does not exist;
mindful of the Dao, seeking the Dharma,
giving rise to great vows,
performing great merit.

Now this great assembly,
you should also enable them
to attain a lofty and wondrous body,
a true and upright youth,
attaining the inconceivable.
The supreme Dao pervades all knowing,
profoundly mindful, vastly universal.
Mindful of sentient beings to come,
when practicing, they will attain
the great and wondrous root,
with wisdom complete,
possessing thought and non-thought,
the greatest wisdom,
truly constant and unchanging.

You, the present assembly,
will not give rise to evil illnesses.
When practicing this Dao,
as children of supreme virtue,
possessing all marks,
understanding emptiness and existence—
when comprehending this mindfulness,
they will surely be mindful of the Dao,
attaining wondrous practice,
free and at ease as they wish.
Expounding for others
the One Vehicle of Haikong,
the secret treasury.

Haikong Zhizang,
know that these dharmas
have no bottom or limit.
Contemplating and expounding them,
their profound meanings are five:
First, good practice—
thinking of all
dark and hidden places,
all attain illumination,
the wondrous marks of the unconditioned."

Second, skillful exposition—
the mind and intent grow gentle,
without self or other.

Third, constant aspiration—
exhorting others to arouse the mind,
to seek superior power,
to distance themselves from evil paths,
to practice fearless action.

Fourth, utmost sincerity—
cutting through all delusions,
free from the net of doubt,
ever abiding in wondrous matters,
gaining the profound flavor of the Dharma,
inexhaustible throughout the day,
all beings
receive deliverance.

Fifth, right intention—
forming all manner of vows,
whether as man or woman,
those who have not seen or heard
all come to hear and know,
and shall attain the Dao.

When practicing these,
one enters the ocean of merit,
the unconditioned assembly of the Dao.
With wholehearted aspiration,
boundless causes and conditions,
the unconditioned fruit—
the name of Dao-achievement,
unobstructed liberation,
this is called "guiding things."

Three practices, three virtues,
three return to one.
Practice and understanding as one condition—
abandon the mind of conditioned doing,
arouse the mind of unconditioned being.
Empty and yielding as dust,
not opposing the honored virtue.
Contemplate the Three Treasures,
never for a moment forsaking them.
Never wavering in resolve,
obscurely aided by the child.
With the mind’s practice perfected,
fully attaining the Dao,
no longer stained or hindered.

You should know:
this great scripture,
circulating in the world,
if seen or heard,
brings boundless causes and conditions.
Good men and good women,
practicing according to its teachings,
cultivating the four equal practices,
their minds filled with joy.
Those who practice thus
rightly enter the unconditioned,
foremost children,
unretreatable causes and conditions.

All beings,
flawed by conditioned existence,
afflicted by vexations,
accumulate them all day long.
Yet once attained,
they do not endure for long.
The affliction of vexations
emptily wastes body and life,
and what is gained?
What is not gained?
What is truly not gained?

Wisdom Treasury, know this:
its meaning further unfolds in seven aspects.
First, the virtue of wisdom—
thought after thought, this mind
enters non-retreat,
its practice ever still.

Second, practice and understanding—
contemplating the Dao, leaving the household,
ever tasting the flavor of the Dharma,
diligent and steadfast.

Third, manifest benefit—
receiving and guiding beings,
enabling them to leave suffering,
ever hearing the Dao and its teachings.

Fourth, beneficial application—
contemplating the sages,
with many skillful means,
bringing benefit to all.

Fifth, wisdom—
true persons and youths
attain great spiritual power,
all achieving Dao through it.

Sixth, attainment of power—
all beings,
emerging from the world through the Dao,
gain fearlessness.

Seventh, virtue fulfilled—
spiritual penetrations, self-mastery,
coming and going, returning,
nothing firm or obstructive.

Thus this wondrousness
serves as the power of the Dharma,
delivering and saving future lives.
If good men
can attain liberation,
truly expounding the real,
recognizing the fundamental source of the Dharma,
entering the causes and conditions of the Dao,
this is where my contemplation dwells.

Why is this so?
The supreme Dao has no bottom,
profound and difficult to fathom,
neither abiding nor perishing,
neither ending nor beginning,
eternally enduring without end.
The practice that employs it
draws all things to itself,
the world entire turns toward it.
Its application is deep and far-reaching,
the tranquil abode of the Dao,
beyond contemplation—
its meanings number in the hundreds and thousands,
its mystery most profound,
a bottomless treasury without limit.

Virtuous deeds transform beings,
responses truly efficacious,
boundless and unlimited,
manifesting skillful means,
delivering from birth and death.

The practice of the Great Vehicle,
the use of lesser wisdom;
neither false nor real,
neither non-existent nor existent,
neither unconditioned nor conditioned.

Such supreme merit
has four inexhaustible applications.
Now expounded thus,
boundless causes and conditions.
The Dao cannot be said to exist,
nor can it be said not to exist—
the power of Dao-wisdom
equalizes all things.

If there are beings
who can dispel the net of doubt,
cutting the roots of vexation,
they are my disciples,
true to the Dao from beginning to end,
turning the Wheel of Dharma,
form and spirit as one,
truly wondrous bodies.
Like stone flowers
transforming into gold and jade,
once truly achieved,
only wondrous marks remain,
no coarse substance seen,
abandoning the body of beings,
attaining a separate Dharma-body.
The coarse departs, the wondrous arrives,
and the true Dao is accomplished.
First abandoning the old and decayed,
then gaining the new and enduring.
Without cause, without effect,
all arises from vows.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy having spoken this verse,
all in the assembly attained the inconceivable:
true and supreme practice,
next discerning truth from falsehood,
foremost in what is practiced,
mysterious and boundless.

At that moment,
hundreds of thousands of myriads of millions
of true immortals and Daoist adepts
were present in the assembly,
upholding the correct Dharma,
having already attained the immeasurable,
fully possessing the six penetrations,
turning toward the wondrous and true,
the unconditioned realm,
inconceivable,
supreme and perfectly true,
beyond comparison.

The true ones of supreme virtue
manifest throughout the ten directions;
innumerable forms
pervade all lands,
receiving and guiding beings,
never slackening.

If good men and good women
should know the practices of seeking the Dao and the secular,
arousing all manner of minds,
they shall attain the Dao,
supreme and perfectly true,
pervading knowledge of all dharmas.
The three realms have no support—
only the Dao can be relied upon.
Though without form or appearance,
its appearance is most true,
its name does not depart—
this is true immovability.

Within the Great Clarity,
lies my source.

As these words were spoken,
good men,
all beings without exception understood.
When true persons and youths
practice the supreme Dao,
they constantly observe beings,
never harboring resentful thoughts,
pushing straightness onto others,
drawing crookedness toward themselves,
without contention,
gaining long life.

Why is this so?
Because they skillfully know the causes and conditions of all means,
desiring to enable beings to plant all manner of good roots.

At that time,
seventy-three lesser immortals and Daoist adepts
came from the west,
all arriving at the seat.
Their names were:
Virtuous Mind Daoist,
Vast Offering Daoist,
Renouncing Love Daoist,
Skillful Exposition Daoist,
Universal Contemplation Daoist,
Faithful Practice Daoist,
Constant Protection Daoist,
Radiant Wisdom Daoist,
Supreme Mark Daoist—
such assemblies
could not all be recorded.
As retinue they came,
to hear the exposition,
all seated together.
Some aroused virtuous practice,
burning incense and lighting lamps.

Some left parents behind, journeying far into mountains and forests;
some made offerings to others, or abandoned wives and children,
devoting themselves to ascetic practice,
surrendering body, wisdom, and wealth,
harmonizing their voices to chant and praise the sacred virtue,
proclaiming the emptiness of the One Vehicle’s oceanic vastness,
extolling and expounding the subtle and wondrous scriptures.
Whatever practices they undertook,
all were performed with utmost devotion,
as offerings to the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy.
At that very moment, they all entered the One Vehicle,
attaining unimpeded liberation and inconceivable realization;
constantly abiding in the Dharma-wheel,
entering the stage of non-retreat;
constantly abiding in the Dharma-realm,
firm and unshaken in bliss.
They beheld the city of oceanic emptiness,
contemplating all dharmas with the mind,
comprehending suffering and emptiness,
impermanence, non-self,
eternal bliss, self, and purity.
Having heard the Dharma, each led their retinue back to their native lands.

Among this assembly,
there were those who had awakened to the wondrous principle,
attaining the fundamental essence of the thirty-six divisions of true scriptures.
They discerned the three marks,
understanding and proclaiming the teachings,
achieving the Dao and its fruits,
grasping causes and conditions,
gaining boundless wondrous penetrations,
turning the spirit to enter samādhi,
realizing the wisdom of the untainted,
mastering skillful means.
They were called the Great Compassion,
entering the samādhi of emptiness and quiescence,
inconceivable.

Suddenly, among this assembly,
one arose and expounded the essential teachings,
profound in meaning.
The great multitude,
each and all, roused courage,
overflowing with joy.
One among them declared:
“Today, I have been able,
in the presence of the Venerable One,
to listen, receive, and awaken to understanding—
awakening to what was unknown and unseen before.
At this moment,
a throne adorned with a hundred treasures,
vast and magnificent, appeared.
In my heart, I sighed in awe,
feeling shame and reverence.
The essential teachings I received
could never be fully expressed.
Yet, by the grace of this great assembly,
I am called to expound the teachings—
how could I remain silent?
If I did not proclaim what I have received,
it would be as if concealing the Dharma,
failing to honor the supreme teaching.”
At that time, he began to lecture and recite the sacred Dharma,
relating the wondrous deeds he had practiced.
Just as with us,
those in the assembly who had not heard or understood before
all gained thorough comprehension,
receiving boundless benefit.
From this resolve,
they together attained the true and radiant Golden Abode,
with immortal youths as attendants,
a hundred thousand musicians,
and manifold transformations guiding all beings,
enabling them to abide perpetually in the fruit of non-action.

“You, this assembly,
and those of future ages,
must wholly abandon evil conduct and practice right contemplation,
turning away from evil and drawing near to goodness,
beginning by renouncing attachment,
forsaking pleasure to seek the Dao—
this is the seed of my teaching,
the foremost and supreme practice,
inconceivable.
Those whose bodies are impure
shall be transformed to purity;
those who, through my Dharma, know the body as ever impure
shall come to understand and purify it.
If you contemplate this truth,
it is a true and reliable assurance,
not false or deceptive—
a profound path of practice,
transcending the understanding of conditioned dharmas.
Thought after thought, they change and shift,
turning the coarse into the wondrous,
shedding one body to receive another,
becoming true companions of immortals.
The six roots and seven limbs
are likewise transformed.
Attaining the true and realizing the Dao
follows this same principle.

Beings deluded by the four perversities
are disturbed by māra,
their spirits departing, their forms dying,
their souls cast into dark prisons.
They suffer myriad torments,
the five agonies and bitter poisons—
when will they find liberation?
In the endless long night,
how can they escape?
Such matters are truly terrifying.
Contemplate the Dao and leave the household life,
distance yourself from the four perversities.
Those who can both speak thus
and put it into practice
shall live in joy.
Do not cling to what was originally possessed;
simply illuminate the truth for beings:
let them renounce the five flavors,
the five colors,
and the allure of delicate, seductive women,
so that their hearts do not become attached.
Constantly hold fast to the wondrous scriptures,
never setting them aside for even a moment,
ever as if starving and thirsty,
craving food and drink.
Cherish the treasure of the scriptures
as you would your own body,
and you shall gain further awakening,
attaining supreme power,
abiding unshaken,
limitless and unsurpassed,
perfecting the wheel of transformation.
This is the guide for cultivating the Dao and practicing immortality.

When the Great Immortal speaks,
none fail to bow their heads in reverence;
when the Perfected One manifests,
none fail to bow their heads in reverence;
when the Youth manifests,
none fail to bow their heads in reverence;
when the Heavenly Worthy manifests,
the eight realms pay homage,
none fail to bow their heads in reverence;
when the Sages of the ten directions each manifest,
none fail to bow their heads in reverence;
when the Immortal Ministers and Youths manifest here,
none fail to bow their heads in reverence.

All empty space,
the provisional three realms,
the five aggregates are without substance,
the three paths are all suffering.
Thought after thought arises and ceases,
all dharmas do not abide,
neither regressing nor turning.
The Prince of Victorious Causes
is called bliss,
ever practicing purity,
attaining unimpeded liberation.
The Oceanic Treasury of Wisdom and Emptiness.

Furthermore,
the merits accumulated by those who study the true Dao
are inconceivable.
True Dharma companions,
now hidden, now revealed,
transforming empty space,
appearing and disappearing as circumstances require.
Sometimes born in the Dharma-realm,
in the palace of the Wheel-Turning King,
possessing great wisdom and power,
attaining the unborn,
realizing the name of the Dao,
entering the stage of non-retreat,
practicing purity.
For five hundred kalpas,
they expound the scriptures and teach the Dharma,
lecturing day and night,
discoursing on their meaning,
yet never exhausting it.
You should know that from this point onward,
for hundreds of thousands of kalpas,
those who cultivate thus
shall reach the realm of non-action,
without thought, without reflection,
entering emptiness and wisdom,
free from all conceptions.
From the highest to the lowest,
they bow at the feet of the Dao,
perceiving the seventy-two marks,
fully grasping the intent of the Dao,
their spiritual wisdom boundless,
like empty space,
unfathomable.

Furthermore,
the prince abandoned his body to seek the Dao.
His parents, filled with pity,
feared he would flee,
so they adorned terraces and ponds,
fortifying every place.
They secured a great gate,
called the Hundredfold Gate of Luminous Dharma.
When the prince departed,
the great king would know—
secrecy was impossible.
Once the prince had gone,
they searched everywhere,
their minds bewildered and distressed,
rushing about in all directions.
What method could they devise to find him?
On the road, they encountered five mighty ghost-spirits of the five paths.
At that very moment,
they questioned them, saying:
“Venerable ones,
I wish to seek the Dao.
I have heard that the adornments of the various paths are wondrous indeed.”

I now ask this with such intent: which Way may I follow?

At that moment, the five mighty ghost-spirits of the five paths suddenly replied: “In times past, I too once left the household life. Yet entangled in the net of doubt, the four Māras assailed me, and I lost the root of the Way, becoming what I am now—not human.

Now I have come to know and reveal all good and evil. As for your seeking the Way, I have heard of it: the supreme, correct, and true One—though only its name is heard—possesses boundless virtue. Though without form or appearance, its mark is serene and unobstructed, the supreme Dharma. Its true nature is unshaken, its majesty vast, subduing toil and enmity. Its responsive transformations are boundless, inconceivable—such is the wondrous power of the Way.”

Then the prince spoke no further and departed. With true heart and right mindfulness, he naturally understood the Dharma, entered the source and flow of the Way, and ever abided in its singular flavor. The ocean of emptiness, the Dharma-earth, stood firm and unshaken. He understood the Dharma as neither empty nor not empty.

“Good man, the treasury of wisdom in the ocean of emptiness—all suffering is inconceivable. I observe the gods as they wander everywhere and see the people: men and women whose mouths and faces fester with pus and flowing foul blood, whose necks are like twisted cloth, whose bellies swell like hanging drums. They bear iron staves, hold fire in their mouths, drag one another through mud and ashes, no longer human in form. Their feet tread upon blades, their bodies bear iron staves—pain too heavy to endure, poison too cruel to bear. How sorrowful!

Again I see men and women with ox-heads and beast-bodies, their tongues pulled out and pierced with iron awls. Mighty celestial enforcers beat them ceaselessly with iron staves, their forms no longer human. Their feet stand upon knife-mountains—pain beyond endurance.

Again I see men and women naked and unclothed, swallowing fire and eating coals, burned by flames. Their heads and faces are scorched, their bodies rotting. They wear iron cauldrons on their heads and tread upon mountains of fire.

Again I see men and women, young and old, plunged into cauldrons of boiling water, their bodies stewed in a hundred poisons poured over them. Their heads and feet are shackled, their bodies tormented. Imprisoned in dark dungeons, they see no sun, moon, or stars. Their forms are shorn and severed, bound in iron chains. They bear mountains and carry stones, walking back and forth upon beds of iron needles, unable to rest day or night. They embrace copper pillars while beasts of Mount Tai devour their flesh.”

Then the Way spoke: “What crimes did these beings commit? What unwholesome deeds led to such retribution?”

At that time, the flying devas of the three realms replied: “Such are the various sinners. In former lives, they committed every evil: red-tongued strife, unceasing conflict, slander of morality, attacks upon teachers and masters, mutual defamation. Some killed without principle, thought nothing of sentient beings, practiced cruelty and tyranny, harbored dark malice, envied those superior to themselves, suppressed the worthy and wise. They committed every kind of offense—too many to recount. Thus they now face these sufferings, enduring them for ten thousand kalpas, destined to be reborn among non-humans. Such is the consequence.”

The Way said: “Let these suffering men and women open their hearts and eyes, repent their good and evil, and attain tranquility. With gentle words, comfort them. Remind them of their past deeds and urge them to think of goodness, to enter the wheel of Dharma. Exhort them again with warnings, that they may be reborn among humans. Through the merit of understanding and practice, cultivate this Way to resolve past enmities, the boundless source of transgressions. Contemplate and practice the conduct of the Way, widely open the gate of Dharma, and establish great merit. When all practices are perfected, enter the gate of blessings, behold the great causes and conditions, the fruit of non-action. Attain extinction and liberation, and reach the truth of the Way.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy spoke again in verse:

The eye of conditions sees all—
beings human and non-human,
creating external forms,
each taking them as kin.

The mind delights in this,
thinking of sentient beings,
uttering false and ornate speech,
evil scolding, two-tongued words,
greed, anger, and deluded minds,
clinging to perverse views,
stealing, killing, and lust—
heavenly spirits do not honor them,
defiling the light of sun and moon.

All evils are like this,
various unwholesome deeds—
ghosts destroy their forms.

Arrogant toward all Dharma,
the heart does not believe in the true Way,
harming those who have left the household,
even good men seeking food and clothing without limit.

Perpetrating lawless acts,
acting against Dharma,
ghosts swiftly assail them,
good spirits do not protect.
All enmities gather,
vying to destroy their bodies.

They cannot grow old,
like barren grain.
Sounds, forms, and the five flavors—
the mind clings to them.

Believing in perverse people,
never thinking of the Way,
only practicing unwholesome deeds—
truly inconceivable.

You good men,
in the ten directions of the great earth,
where blessings and virtue abound,
there are no obstructions.
Where blessings and virtue abound,
all thoughts, great and small, are equal.

Liberating boundless suffering,
like frost meeting scorching heat.
Such is the power of wisdom—
nothing to cling to or attach to.

Attachment makes gods and humans,
eight in pursuit, one in return.
Entering and exiting neither being nor non-being,
transformations without bound.

Without a discriminating mind,
possessing all-embracing wisdom,
liberating sentient beings,
equalizing right and wrong.

Those who do not believe in causes and conditions
see success and failure through endless kalpas.
Bound by the six senses,
they know not the conditions of liberation.

Among thousands and ten thousands,
rarely is there one
who, if they cultivate mindfulness,
is truly a seed of the Way.

One should arouse various minds,
wishing to comprehend past events,
the great causes and conditions of the future.

Countless good and evil beings,
understanding past principles,
principles in the Dharma of skillful means,
boundless and infinite multitudes.

Within the realm of the great Way,
able to discern unobstructed matters,
able to accomplish all Dharma.”

Grasping the meaning of the Three Powers,
penetrating the marks of all dharmas,
without any place of obstruction,
the mind delights in practicing the Way,
and hears the supreme matters.

When all sages expound the Dharma,
one should attain eloquent speech.
With the six practices, the mind can advance;
one should aspire to attain purity.

Able to relinquish all forms,
with equal and compassionate mind,
for all suffering beings,
I am one who is destitute.
And within the five paths,
enduring all matters with forbearance,
diligent in unstained dharmas,
contemplating concentration without retrogression,
not giving rise to the four perverse intentions.

Thought after thought is the Dharma-wheel,
able to endure unrighteousness,
I harbor no resentment,
guarding virtue in the world.
Not desiring the desires of others,
with reasoned forbearance and no contention;
far removed from worldly afflictions,
concealing oneself in secluded places;
not violating the harmony of mind and mouth,
conduct not transgressing sutras and precepts.

Day and night one should practice the Way,
amidst the five foods, always with vegetables,
mixed food without relishing taste.
Delighting in the heart of pine and cypress groves,
only thinking of consuming myriad medicines,
the mind not gazing upon perverse sights.

The various boundless sufferings
of this afflicted world—
in future lives, good daughters and sons,
born into the world committing various evils,
shall fall into the great hells,
dying and transmigrating within the five paths,
exhausting their lives in retribution,
their bodies embracing bronze pillars,
hands and feet treading upon knife mountains,
forever circling amidst sword trees,
then again entering cauldrons of boiling water,
when hungry, swallowing fire,
faces and heads all scorched.

In the heavenly and human realms,
there will be no more causes and conditions.
In hells and among hungry ghosts,
boundless afflictions,
forever abiding in suffering.

In future lives, men and women
who do not awaken to the conditions of deliverance,
diligent in seeking superior power,
sacrificing the body as the Dao-ground—
as spoken in this sutra,
the profound practices,
without any falsehood.

In past kalpas and the present kalpa,
there has never been such discourse.
You all should revere with devotion,
witnessing these rare matters.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken the gāthā, again addressed Haikong Zhizang, saying: “Good son, you and the present assembly, regarding such matters—boundless afflictions, the eight difficulties interwoven, various poisons, most terrifying—all sentient beings do not arouse the mind of the Way, do not generate the intention for the Way, do not practice the four immeasurables, are perverse and contrary, forever losing causes and conditions, not encountering the Three Treasures, not hearing the essential Dharma, not hearing the Dharma-drum, not hearing the secret treasury of Haikong Zhizang. When you attain these matters, in future worlds widely propagate them; those who have not seen or heard, all should be made to understand and awaken. Having understood and awakened, they shall enter non-retrogression, the Great Vehicle of non-action, arriving at the Palace of Longevity, the foremost and supreme cause, difficult to compare even with a wall’s inscription.”

Haikong Zhizang rose from his seat, approached before the Dao, prostrated with five limbs touching the ground, his heart joyful and delighted, his mind filled with emptiness: “Today, I have heard words and gāthās that in ten million kalpas have never been uttered. Within these few words, I have now heard and received, gaining much understanding and awakening. In an instant, Haikong Zhizang attained the inconceivable.”

Then, there were boundless and infinite true and good light-forms; the Great Wisdom Youths descended from the sky to the seat, all desiring to augment Zhizang’s merit and virtue, foremost in wisdom.
