Their names were: Universal King Superior Practice Youth, Three Heavens Perfected Superior Practice Youth, Great One Superior Practice Youth, Four Immeasurables Wondrous Light Superior Practice Youth, Universal Practice Equal King Superior Practice Youth, Five Eyes Penetrating Immortal Superior Practice Youth, Solemn Pure Moon Virtue Superior Practice Youth, Six Virtues Universal Light Superior Practice Youth, Sunlight Treasure Accumulation Superior Practice Youth, Flower Light Good Karma Superior Practice Youth, Heavenly King Wondrous Fragrance Superior Practice Youth—such assemblies as these, boundless great beings, arrived at the seat, rejoicing and praising, bowing at the honored one’s feet.

At that time, there were devas from the Formless Realm descending from below, their names being: Bright Court Rosy Transcendence Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Profound Penetration Primordial Cavern Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Flourishing Honor Wondrous Achievement Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Elegant Joy Forbidden Above Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son—these four directional heavenly sons, hearing this wondrous sound, each led their realm’s men and women, good and faithful, to listen to the One Vehicle’s Haikong Secret Treasury. Though there were men and women, there was no intercourse; coming and going, they were free and at ease, without desire, arriving at my place. Their bodies were tall and large, desiring to hear these rare discourses, the profound Dharma, attaining the turning of the Dharma-ground, the unobstructed place, liberation and purity, coming and going, uniting with the true Dao.

At that time, there were also devas from the Form Realm descending from below, their names being: Empty Transcendence Balance Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Supreme Ultimate Veiled Darkness Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Vermilion Bright Harmonious Yang Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Mysterious Bright Reverent Splendor Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Radiant Bright Ancestral Whirl Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Bamboo Grove August Reed Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Empty Bright Hall Illumination Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Observing Bright Upright Tranquility Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Mysterious Bright Reverent Celebration Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Supreme Flaming Ultimate Jade Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Primordial Carriage Cavity Ascent Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Supreme Peace August Cliff Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Manifest Concentration Ultimate Wind Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Beginning Yellow Filial Awn Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Supreme August Grandfather Heavy Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, No-Thought River Origin Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Upper Gambling Joy Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son, Boundless Cloud Vow Realm Heavenly Emperor’s Son—such realm’s people and their ministers arrived at my place, expounding the true power of supreme wisdom in due time. This realm reveres and practices the unobstructed Dharma, erects the great Dharma-banner, inconceivable. Hearing these wondrous matters, they scattered incense and formed bonds, forever severing perverse desires, without afflictions, not entering the thousand poisons of birth and death.

At that time, there were also devas from the Desire Realm, who likewise all came.

Their names were Heavenly Son of August Layered Heaven, Heavenly Son of Jade Perfection, Heavenly Son of Youthful Harmony, Heavenly Son of Level Nurturance, Heavenly Son of Primordial Luminance, and Heavenly Son of Serene Radiance. The people of their realms were largely incomplete, beset by boundless suffering and afflictions, sinking into the cycles of birth and death, torn by love and hatred, partings and enmities, malicious slayings—matters beyond conception. Yet if any turned wholeheartedly to hear the Dao, distance mattered not.

Now I expound for them the One Vehicle’s Ocean-Empty Secret Treasury, delivering all realm-dwellers according to their capacities, guiding them step by step to awakening, ensuring none regress, all attaining peace. Ministers, officials, and common folk alike gain unobstructed freedom, abiding in the joyous Dao-ground. Now proclaiming these Dharmas, ever of one taste, I enable all worlds to cultivate gradually, each attaining the Dao-fruit.

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable further spoke in verse:

The Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury,
The Dao’s greatness—beyond compare.
Heaven and earth, the four seas,
Insufficient as metaphor.

Without end, without beginning,
True One’s wondrous principle,
Neither increasing nor decreasing,
Without cause, without learning,
Without present, without past.

The Great Dao is non-doing,
Its depths unfathomable.
For sentient beings,
There is constant coming and going;
Though there is coming and going,
Yet no coming or going—
Inconceivable,
Its profound origin, its subtlety.

You, my retinue,
With tranquil, unified minds,
Contemplate the Dao,
The supreme, correct, and true.
Harmonious in suffering and joy,
Emptiness and non-emptiness.

The Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury,
Supreme immortal,
Forever severs the net of doubt,
Like extracting a poisoned arrow,
Attaining fearlessness.

The Heavenly Venerable now expounds,
Distinguishing for the assembly.
All present bow in reverence,
Unfailing.

Future beings,
Let not the four perversities arise.
Whether man or woman,
Abandoning the body to seek the Dao,
No longer clinging to bodily existence,
Ceasing all desires,
Rectifying the mind in the Dao-ground,
Extinguishing conditioned thoughts,
Without origin.

Those who practice the profound Dharma
Shall know no affliction.
They shall attain wisdom,
Adamantine virtue.

All in the great assembly,
Universally practicing the Dao’s work,
Attain the Lion of Kings,
Great compassion’s parable.
The numinous treasure’s insight,
Mindful deliverance without measure,
Augmenting adornment.

Having cultivated mindfulness,
They shatter evil, fear, and demons,
Subduing weariness and resentment,
Abiding in constant joy, self, purity,
Gaining fearless power.

Good men and good women,
In such matters,
Not conditioned by form’s arising,
Recognizing this as “name,”
Not perceiving form,
The five aggregates purified,
Thus ever unstained,
Pure and liberated.

All Dharmas
Arise from causes and conditions,
Yet possess no dual nature.

Contemplate the boundless,
The limitless divine wisdom,
Honoring it as supreme.

Those who leave home in understanding and practice
Attain true liberation.
The so-called practitioner
Is like earth, like mountains,
Like eyes, like clouds,
Like father, like mother.
All Dharmas are likewise.

Unshaken,
This is called understanding and practice.

Perfected beings and youths
Expound in manifold ways,
Yet never sated.
Joyous speech is unobstructed,
Boundless, measureless.
For countless kalpas,
Expounding words and meanings,
Never exhausted.

Sons and daughters of men,
For a thousand kalpas,
Cultivating worldly Dharmas,
Through such cultivation,
Unobstructed in Dharma,
Further, for boundless
Hundreds of thousands of kalpas,
Accumulating discourses,
Thus attaining joyous speech.

Perfected beings and youths,
To deliver sentient beings,
Cultivate thus the four unobstructed Dharmas,
The wisdom of unobstruction.

Middle-grade practitioners
Cultivate the Dharma of quiescence,
Delighting in solitude.
When transforming beings,
They manifest only spiritual powers,
Remaining silent all day,
Expounding nothing.

Ultimately pure,
The Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury,
Foremost in wisdom.
Immortal ministers and youths,
Foremost in spiritual powers.

Such matters are unequal:
Originally present, now absent;
Originally absent, now present.
Ancient and modern Dharmas
Are thus declared.

Now I shall again expound for you,
Broadly distinguishing and explaining.

Good men and women,
Now possessing
The bonds of afflictions,
Originally born of parents’ union.

Thus, in the present,
There is no adamantine,
Subtle Dharma-body.

Formerly, I possessed
Impermanence, no-self,
No-joy, no-purity.
Because of impermanence,
No-self, no-joy, no-purity,
What is present now is absent.

The supreme Dao-mind,
Because of non-perception,
Lacks impermanence, joy, purity.

If there are Daoists
Who speak or do not speak,
Whether men or women,
Who claim:
“The Heavenly Venerable’s supreme Dao,
Free in coming and going,
Impermanent wondrous joy,
Is my purity”—
This is impossible.

For this reason,
The present cannot
Destroy the four demons;
The present is ultimately empty,
Defiled in all Dharmas.

If my disciples,
Dull-rooted,
Cannot expound
The One Vehicle’s Dharma,
Originally lacking sharp roots,
Kings of men among elephants,
Perfected beings of wondrous practice,
Equal in no-self roots—
According to circumstances,
They reveal the Three Vehicles.

All learners
Who claim:
“The supreme Dao,
In past, present, or future,
Ultimately expounds
Non-doing”—
This is impossible.
They speak according to time and circumstance.

If beings
Cannot attain this,
The primary condition:
The divine, wondrous Dao
Ultimately has no expounding,
Nothing to be gained.

At that time, Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury,
Having received this wondrous matter,
Opened his mind and understood,
All becoming perfectly clear.
His body grew vast,
Adorned with seventy-two marks,
Eighty-one excellences,
Without root or foundation.
The profound, subtle, non-doing,
Supreme power of Wisdom Treasury
Filled him with boundless joy,
And he spoke in verse:

Great compassion pities sentient beings,
Thus now I take refuge.
Skillfully extracting the poisoned arrow,
Hence called the Great Physician King.
Worldly physicians’ treatments,
Though healed, relapse.
The Heavenly Venerable’s cure
Is ultimately never reborn.

The Heavenly Venerable’s sweet-dew medicine
Is bestowed upon sentient beings.
Once beings have partaken,
They neither live nor die.

The Heavenly Venerable now for me
Expounds the great wisdom.
Beings who hear this secret treasury
Attain the unborn and undying,
Body and mind both at peace,
Clearly beholding the City of Ocean-Empty.

Having spoken this verse, Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury again addressed the Dao, saying: “Heavenly Venerable, what has now been expounded—all in the world neither know nor perceive it, yet those who see the True Person can know, see, and perceive it. If the True Person were of the world, one could not say the world does not know, does not know or perceive. Yet if not of the world, what distinguishing marks does the True Person possess?”

“Moreover, good son, the True Person is both of the world and not of the world. What do you mean when you say the True Person has distinctions? Reflect carefully. I shall explain further for you—wait but a moment, and I will expound its meaning separately. This is not the day to exhaustively speak all that can be said or fully express its intent. I will now tell you, one by one, the profound roots of the Dao. You should comprehend and awaken to the singular condition.”

Thereupon, Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury and the entire assembly each bowed once, took their leave, and withdrew.

*End of Scroll Seven of the Supreme One Vehicle Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury Sutra*

*Scroll Eight of the Supreme One Vehicle Ocean-Empty Wisdom Treasury Sutra*

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy dwelt in the Great Jeweled City, expounding the essentials of the Dharma for all sentient beings. There was an elder who resided in the western part of the city, devout in faith and offerings, named Good-Seed Great King. Together with thirty-three of his kind, they served as great bridges and beams for the world, relinquishing their bodies and forsaking their wealth. Rising from their seats, they bowed in reverence, prostrated with their heads to the ground, and knelt to gaze up at the Heavenly Worthy, tears of sorrow streaming down. They addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “We only pray that the Heavenly Worthy and all Daoist masters will compassionately accept our humble offerings of the poor, so as to deliver the immeasurable hosts of heavenly beings. Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, we now have no lord, no kin, no savior, no protector, no refuge, no destination—poor, hungry, and destitute. We seek from the Heavenly Worthy the food of the future. We only pray that you will compassionately accept our meager offerings, so that all beings—whether human or non-human—who receive our offerings may attain peace and happiness. Thereafter, the Heavenly Worthy will return to the realm of non-action, to the quiescent and unmoving ground of stillness and extinction. Our offerings now are like those in all lands who, through diligent farming, obtain great oxen and level fields free of mounds, wastelands, brambles, thorns, and poisonous grasses. Such good fields await only the rain from heaven. Greatly Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, our bodies are just the same—we await only the sweet dew of the One Vehicle’s Dharma-rain to nourish the fields of our bodies. We, poor and destitute, beseech the Heavenly Worthy, our father of great compassion, to take pity and remove our poverty, distress, and suffering, and to rescue the immeasurable multitudes of beings from their afflictions. We now make these offerings, praying that the Great Compassion will equally bestow sufficiency upon all—whether human or non-human—and that all heavenly immortals and the great assembly may gain great benefit and abide in constant peace and joy.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy, with a heart of great compassion and wisdom of many kinds, addressed Good-Seed, saying: “Excellent, excellent, good son, Great King and Elder! I shall now remove for you the notions of poverty, hunger, thirst, and exhaustion. The rain of the Great Compassion’s Dharma shall nourish the fields of your bodies, and the sprouts of the Dharma shall grow. If you seek from me longevity, peace of body and mind, and boundless eloquence, I shall grant you longevity and peace, all without obstruction. Why is this? Good-Seed Elder, your offerings are pure and equal toward all. Such giving yields a karmic reward without distinction. What does it mean to be equal, without distinction? First, upon receiving, one abides in the treasury of the One Vehicle. Second, upon receiving, one returns to the quiescent ground of the spirit’s stillness and extinction. I now accept your earnest offerings and bestow upon you the complete treasury of the secret and wondrous One Vehicle Ocean-Empty.”

Thereupon, Good-Seed Great King and Elder advanced, knelt, and prostrated, addressing the Heavenly Worthy: “As the Venerable One has said, the karmic reward of equality is without distinction—this is what we ourselves have reflected upon. Yet this principle is not so. Why is this?”

"If there are beings who first receive offerings—while their afflictions remain unexhausted, their omniscience not yet perfected, and they have not yet enabled all beings to fully attain the treasury of the One Vehicle—then those who subsequently receive offerings have extinguished all afflictions, already realized the secret and wondrous Ocean-Empty treasury of the One Vehicle, and can universally enable all beings to fully attain the equal One Vehicle, the constant bliss of purity. The former recipients partake of impure food; their bodies, bound by afflictions, are bodies of birth-and-death, impermanent bodies, hungry ghost bodies. The latter recipients are bodies of wisdom, adamantine bodies, true bodies, Dharma bodies, bodies of constant bliss. Given such distinctions, how can you speak of the One Vehicle as equal, its karmic reward without difference?

Now, when the Venerable One receives offerings first, having partaken, they enter the belly and are digested, sustaining life, enhancing complexion, and bringing constant, enduring bliss, with boundless eloquence. Yet those who receive offerings later partake of impure, mixed food, devoid of superior fruits. How then can you say their karmic reward is without difference?"

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy addressed Good-Seed: "Elder, Great King, good son, as for those like me who partake—since limitless, boundless kalpas ago, we have had no body of food, no body of birth-and-death, no body of afflictions, no body of poisonous craving. My body is the constant body; your body is the constant body; the adamantine body. Among all beings who will receive offerings later, they have not yet seen my body—it is a body of afflictions, a body mixed with craving, a body of birth-and-death, a hungry ghost body. Yet for these four assemblies, whether human or non-human, I partake equally with them. Once the food is consumed equally, upon its digestion, they immediately perceive my form abiding in the treasury of the One Vehicle. Therefore, I say the karmic reward is without difference.

If beings shatter worldly dharmas, universally eradicate the four Māras, and enter the Ocean-Empty treasury of the One Vehicle, for this reason, I say the karmic reward is without distinction. If there are good people who, though not broadly expounding all scriptures, have already fully realized the secret and wondrous Ocean-Empty treasury of the One Vehicle and extensively explain it to beings for their discernment, their merit is boundless. Therefore, I say the karmic reward is without difference.

Good son, beings like me—since limitless, boundless kalpas ago—have not partaken of the mixed food, mixed forms, or mixed appearances of the world. For the sake of beings, I speak of receiving offerings, just as those highest perfected ones receive garlands and only afterward return to the quiescent ground. I now do likewise: receiving your offerings, I shall then return to the secret and wondrous Dharma ground of the Ocean-Empty One Vehicle. I now receive offerings, yet truly do not receive offerings; I now receive a body, yet truly do not receive a body; I now praise, yet truly do not praise; I now expound, yet truly do not expound. For the sake of this great assembly, I thus receive your equal offerings—yet truly do not receive them."

Thereupon, the four assemblies, having heard the Heavenly Worthy speak thus, understood that he compassionately accepted the offerings of the impoverished Elder Good-Seed Great King on their behalf. Then the four assemblies prostrated, touching their heads to the ground, rejoicing and exclaiming in unison: "Excellent! Excellent! The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, out of pity for us, has accepted these offerings—how rare! How rare! Excellent! Excellent! The name you bear is not in vain. To be called 'Good-Seed' is to embody wondrous meaning. You now establish such wholesome dharmas, sowing seeds that flow through the three realms. Thus, in truth, your name is derived from goodness—you are Good-Seed. Great King, you now gain great benefit in this present life, your merit and vows fulfilled, your depth fully realized. Good-Seed Great King, your birth among humans and gods is most rare! Excellent, Good-Seed—beyond conception!

In this present life, to follow the Great Compassionate Worthy as he traverses other realms is also most difficult to encounter, as is the faith in the Dharma that inspires such offerings. This wholesome cause and condition, this offering born of faith, can yield sweet fruit—this too is rare."

Then the great assembly, with one mind, prostrated, knelt, and addressed Good-Seed: "Your wisdom now shines like the full moon, free of clouds. All beings in your realm gaze upon you without exception. Just so, you are the one upon whom we four assemblies gaze. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy has accepted your offerings, and now you have fully attained great merit, the secret and wondrous Ocean-Empty treasury of the One Vehicle. Therefore, we say your light is like the full moon, and all beings in your realm—whether great or small, old or young—gaze upon you without exception. Though you bear a body, it is an adamantine body, an adamantine mind. Good-Seed Great King, you are the seed of the Three Jewels’ wisdom, the protector who upholds the flow of the Dharma."

Thereupon, the four assemblies rejoiced and exclaimed in verse:
*"Excellent, Good-Seed King,
Compassionate father of the world,
Though born in the human realm,
You transcend the three realms’ existence.
We and all beings now bow our heads in reverence.
Great Compassionate Worthy of the three realms,
Now return to your original abode.
May you pity us,
And swiftly consent to remain,
Lingering long in the world,
Benefiting all beings,
Expounding the city of wisdom’s treasury,
Universally showering the rain of sweet dew."*

Thereupon, Elder Good-Seed Great King, having heard these words, rejoiced: "Excellent! Excellent! What I have heard is like one whose parents, thought dead, suddenly revive, restored to their former state. My joy now is likewise. What I have heard is like a poor man encountering a golden vase. My joy now is likewise. It is like one weakened by loss, wandering in a foreign land, parted from parents and homeland, long separated by love and affection—then suddenly reunited, seeing their homeland again, parents and siblings, filled with great joy. My joy now is likewise."

Then Good-Seed rose from his seat and spoke in verse:

"Excellent! I have gained great benefit,
Universally benefiting all beings,
Severing the afflictions of the Three Poisons,
Forever departing the Three Wretched Realms.

Encountering the great benefit of the Dharma,
All protect this vajra-body.
Meeting the Primordial Honored One,
I fear not falling into the beastly realm.

Like the jeweled city in the empty sea,
Rare to see, rare to hear.
Having seen it, I plant the roots of goodness,
Forever departing the hungry ghost realm.

Attaining entry among the Four Peoples,
Together receiving the light of compassion.
Rare indeed, most rare—
The Great Compassionate Honored One who appears in the world,
Whose body and mind are perfect in wisdom,
Delivering humans and non-humans alike.

Rare indeed, most rare—
The Great Honored One who appears in this age of decline,
Whose body emerges like the lotus,
Adorned with subtle and wondrous marks of virtue.
Severing the ailments of the conditioned,
Forever transcending the day of death.

To be born in this world is difficult,
To encounter a teacher is even more so.
Like the waters of the great sea,
Once cast adrift, return is harder still.

I now offer this devotion,
Wishing to attain the supreme fruit,
Shattering all knots of affliction,
Leaving none unbroken.
In this realm, I seek not
The Heaven of Heavens.
Through skillful means, I gain great benefit,
My heart harboring no regret.

May the Compassionate Honored One accept my offering,
My joy boundless and eternal.
Like the great lion
Emerging from the celestial jeweled forest,
My body is as the lion’s—
The Honored One of Decline accepts my offering,
Emerging from the celestial jeweled forest.
Thus, I rejoice.

My heart is like the lotus within the lotus,
A pure and subtle flower.
All the heavenly youths
Come together to serve and attend me.
The people of this world and land
Are all beset by great suffering.
Having known the Great Compassionate Honored One,
You shall soon return to your original abode—
The realm of neither death nor birth,
The compassionate father beyond the world.

With resonant voices, all chant in unison:
‘In this world, there is no compassionate father.
From birth, none can be relied upon,
Alone and exposed, without refuge.’
Wiping their tears, they bow and plead for you to stay.

We only beseech the Great Compassionate Honored One
To remain long in the world,
Universally expounding the supreme path
For all Daoists.
Like that city of seven treasures,
Abiding steadfast in the sea,
With wisdom, you skillfully sever,
And we, enlightened, dwell in light without darkness.

Like the great radiant light
Shining upon the vaidūrya gem,
With this wondrous and excellent light,
Universally dispel all afflictions,
Forever melting them away.

O Great Compassionate and Great Merciful Honored One,
How can you return to your original place?
We, all sentient beings,
Are overcome with longing and sorrow,
Gazing upon you with tears of grief,
Flowing like rivers.
We only beseech the Great Compassionate Honored One
To remain long, strengthening our faith,
Severing the delusions of affliction,
Skillfully expounding the bridge of Dharma."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Honored One, having heard these verses, addressed Good-Seed Elder Great King: "Excellent! Excellent! Good son, it is just as you have said. My appearance in this world is most difficult, most difficult. Why is this so? The Jeweled City in the Empty Sea is hard to see, hard to enter; even to encounter it and generate faith is most difficult. I shall now return to the realm of non-action. That you can serve as a bridge, offering sustenance to beings, and perfect the subtle and wondrous marks of virtue—this, too, is most difficult. Good-Seed, do not grieve so deeply. Be at peace and rejoice, deeply celebrating the great benefit of the Dharma you have attained. Your offering today has accomplished merit, perfecting the single vehicle of the Jeweled Treasury of the Empty Sea. You should not beseech me to remain long in the world. You must understand: the Three Clarities’ realm is momentary and impermanent. The nature and characteristics of all dharmas are likewise—like shadows following form, now present, now gone. How can you ask me to remain in the world?

I observe myself—even I am empty;
Because I am empty, others are also empty;
Because others are empty, this is called ‘emptiness of emptiness.’"

Then the Heavenly Honored One, moved by great compassion, spoke in verse:

"All dharmas born in the world,
Those born must return to transformation.
Lifespan is like empty space,
It must come to an end.
Prosperity and decline have their time,
Union and parting are inevitable.
Youth and strength do not abide,
Each moment swiftly passes.
Life is the cause of death,
Four Māras, four illnesses afflict.
The constant and inconstant—do they endure?
Loved ones and strangers alike depart.
Suffering turns without end,
Flowing ceaselessly.
The Three Realms are all impermanent,
All conditioned things are without abode.
Even the Dao is empty and nonexistent,
All is utterly empty.
How can one cling to the turning of the Dharma,
Ever beset by sorrow and affliction?
Fearful of sins and evils,
Aging, sickness, death, and decline.
Amidst these afflictions,
One is also assailed by enmity.
Bound by afflictions,
Like a silkworm in its cocoon—
What wise being
Could delight in such a state?
This body is an assemblage of suffering,
All dharmas are impure.
All desires are impermanent,
Thus, I do not cling to them.
Departing desire, contemplating wisely,
One clarifies the Jeweled Treasury of the Empty Sea.
Ultimately bright and pure,
Forever free from calamity.
I ride the ship of the Empty Sea,
Surely reaching the other shore."

Thereupon, Elder Good-Seed Great King, having heard these verses, rose and bowed, addressing the Heavenly Honored One: "So it is, just as you have said. I am foolish and dull-witted, my wisdom shallow, like a blind moth—how could I fathom the profound meaning of the single-vehicle Jeweled Treasury? Now, together with the heavenly sages, perfected immortals, divine youths, dragon kings, and all my retinue, I have departed afflictions and attained ordination. Though I have not yet perfected the precepts of the single-vehicle emptiness, I have already fallen into the rank of immortals. Likewise, though I lack great wisdom, I have entered the royal station. By the majestic power of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One, I am unimpeded in understanding—this is the mark of a great sage. Therefore, I now beseech the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One to remain long in the world, not to return your spirit to the realm of non-action. We are like thirsty ones who, having tasted the sweet dew, could never reject its flavor. We only pray that the Heavenly Honored One will abide and expound, just as before—remaining in the world, pouring forth the sweet dew and the flavor of the single-vehicle Dharma, enabling us to hear what we have never heard, see what we have never seen, and accomplish the secret Jeweled Treasury of the Empty Sea."

At that time, among the assembly there was a perfected one named Dharma Joy, who addressed Good Seed, saying: "Excellent, Good Seed, elder and great king, you ought not utter such words, beseeching the Heavenly Honored One to remain forever in the world. Why is this? You should know that all conditioned things are impermanent, empty of self-nature, empty of abiding marks, with nature and marks both void. Contemplate the three realms—past, present, and future are all empty. You should understand that to seek abiding in the world is to study this truth."

Thereupon, Good Seed, smiling, asked in reply: "Dharma Joy, wise one, you say the Compassionate Honored One’s conditioned things are impermanent, empty of self-nature, with nature and marks both void, and that contemplating the three realms reveals all three times as empty. Yet you should know: how is it that the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is the most revered and supreme in the heavens and the world? Is not such a mark one of true existence? If it is existent, is it subject to arising and ceasing, or not? If it is subject to arising and ceasing, like bubbles or lightning—swiftly appearing, swiftly vanishing—coming and going in flux, like a turning wheel, then all conditioned things are likewise. Yet I have heard that the Heavenly Honored One’s lifespan is vast and distant, at ease and free, eternally abiding in purity, the Heaven among heavens, the Immortal among immortals. How then can you say the Great Compassionate One’s lifespan is brief, not even a hundred years? Like a radiant king who attains sovereign power—by virtue of that sovereignty, he can restrain others."

The wealthy man shall later become poor and lowly, despised and discarded by others, made to serve as another’s drudge. Why is this? Because he has lost his power and strength. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is likewise. If he were the same as all conditioned things, he could not be called the Heaven among heavens, the Immortal among immortals. Why? Because all conditioned things are subject to arising and ceasing, bound to birth and death. Those of dharma-joy and wisdom, do not observe the Compassionate Honored One as identical to all conditioned existence and claim he is impermanent.

Furthermore, I ask: O you of dharma-joy and wisdom, do you know the Heavenly Honored One and thus speak these words? Or do you not know the Heavenly Honored One and yet utter such speech? If the Great Compassionate One were the same as all conditioned things, then being conditioned, he would not be imperishable—how then could he be divine? If the Heavenly Honored One were the same as all conditioned things, he could not be called the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One, the Heaven among heavens, the Immortal among immortals. It is like the Dharma King of the three realms below, who possesses a great warrior capable of defeating enemies and foreign adversaries. When battle is joined, among the ranks of soldiers there suddenly appears one man whose strength equals a thousand. Thus, all foreign enemies submit without exception. For this reason, this great king is said to have the strength of a thousand. Such a warrior is cherished by the king, who bestows upon him treasures and emoluments, grants him rank and recompense, and provides him with natural sustenance—a realm of constant joy, peace, and fearlessness. For this reason, he is called one who equals a thousand. Yet this man does not necessarily possess the strength to overcome a thousand; rather, through various skillful means and expedient methods, he is able to surpass the strength of a thousand, and so is called one who equals a thousand.

The Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is likewise. He is skilled in extinguishing all afflictions, the demon of defilements, and the demon of birth and death for all beings. For this reason, the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is the Heaven among heavens, the Honored One of the three realms, like that warrior who equals a thousand. Through these causes and conditions, he perfects and fulfills immeasurable, true virtues—the treasury of the One Vehicle, the ocean of emptiness, the secret storehouse.

O you of dharma-joy and wisdom, you should not conceive or discriminate, thinking the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One to be the same as all conditioned things. It is like a wealthy king or elder who begets a son. At that time, skilled physiognomists come to examine him and find the mark of short lifespan. Upon hearing this, the parents know he is unfit to inherit the family line and no longer cherish him, regarding him as worthless as straw. If one knows that the lifespan is short, he will no longer be revered by all beings throughout the ten directions and all lands. If the Heavenly Honored One were the same as all conditioned things, he likewise would not be venerated by all beings of the three realms in the world. The Dharma he teaches would not be unchanging, unaltered, true, subtle, and ultimate.

O you of dharma-joy and wisdom, if there are beings who single-mindedly receive and uphold this Dharma, guarding and protecting it, never allowing it to depart from their hearts, day and night dwelling upon it—it is like a destitute woman without parents, whose original dwelling place and protectors are gone. Suddenly afflicted by illness, tormented by hunger and thirst, she wanders begging for food. At another’s house, she gives birth to a child, but the master of the house drives her away. Then, the destitute woman carries her son, intending to go to another land. On the road, she encounters a fierce storm with wind and rain, enduring bitter cold. Carrying her child, she crosses a deep pool with swift currents, yet she does not let go. Thus, mother and child both drown together. Yet by the power of this woman’s compassion, she is reborn in the blissful realm above.

O you of dharma-joy and wisdom, if there is a man or woman who receives and upholds the treasury of the One Vehicle, the ocean of emptiness, guarding it carefully, you should not say whether it is the same as or different from conditioned things. You should only reproach yourself: “I am now foolish and lack the wisdom eye to perceive the inconceivable One Vehicle true Dharma of the Compassionate Honored One. Therefore, I should not propagate or expound it.”

Is the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One truly conditioned or unconditioned? If one attains the mind of right view, one should say: The Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is definitely the true fruit, constant and blissful, unconditioned. Why? Because he gives rise to wholesome Dharma for beings and engenders love and cherishing. It is like the woman in the fierce storm who, out of love for her child, sacrifices her life and drowns with him. We, too, should be thus: we would rather sacrifice our lives than say the Compassionate Honored One is the same as the conditioned. We should constantly contemplate the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One as unconditioned, attaining the treasury of the One Vehicle, the ocean of emptiness. Like that woman who was reborn in the blissful realm above, why? Because of her love for her child.

Now, my love for the Dharma is likewise thus. What is this love for the Dharma? It is to declare that the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is identical with the unconditioned—seeking neither bliss, nor liberation, nor permanence, nor the return of spirit, yet bliss, liberation, and permanence arise of themselves, freely and spontaneously. Just as that woman sought not the blissful realm above, yet heaven came to her of its own accord, so too is my reverence for the Honored One.

Dharma-joyous true ones, it is like a traveler on a distant journey, weary and exhausted along the way, who takes shelter in another’s dwelling. As he lies asleep, suddenly a great fire erupts in the house, flames rising on all sides. Startled awake, he immediately reflects: “Now I shall surely die without doubt.” Stirred by shame and remorse, he wraps himself in his robe, and thus his life ends. Reborn in the realm above, he dwells there for eighty years, then becomes a celestial king for a hundred thousand years, and later descends into the human realm, transforming into a wheel-turning monarch. Never again does he fall into the three evil destinies; the wheel of his rebirth turns ever in blissful realms. For this reason, those who possess shame and remorse should not regard the Great Compassionate Honored One as identical with conditioned phenomena.

Dharma-joyous true ones, the teachers of the lesser vehicle and external paths, those of perverse views, declare that the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One is of the world, conditioned and afflicted by defilements. Now, true adepts should not be thus—they should not conceive of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One with thoughts of defilement. If any external teachers or those of perverse views utter falsehoods and various evil words, know that such persons, upon death, will enter hell, suffering in dark confinement for ten thousand kalpas, long submerged in the three paths and five torments.

Dharma-joyous true ones, know that the Honored One is the true reality. He should not today abandon his body and return his spirit, leaving behind his many disciples. Therefore, we gaze upon him with tears, entreating him to remain and expound for us the secret treasury of wisdom of the One Vehicle’s ocean of emptiness, that we may all forsake ignorance and seek the true and right fruit.

Then, the Dharma-joyous ones spoke in unison, praising: “Excellent, good seed! You have now attained a blissful realm, for you rightly know the Compassionate Honored One as eternal and blissful, unchanging and unaltered, having realized the unconditioned Dharma. Moreover, you are able to offer him pure sustenance, inviting him to teach the conditioned Dharma of the world, manifesting the marks of the conditioned. Like the man engulfed in fire who, stirred by shame, wraps himself in his robe and perishes in the flames, by the power of his virtuous mind, he is reborn in the blissful realm above, in a pure land, and later descends to be born as a wheel-turning sage-king, forever removed from evil destinies, dwelling in the city of the ocean of emptiness. You, too, are thus—well guarding the Compassionate Honored One, inviting him to remain and receive offerings. We, the lesser immortals below, shall reap profound benefits, and before long, we shall attain the treasury of the One Vehicle.”

Then, the Heavenly Honored One again addressed the Elder Good Seed and the Great King: “Good son, you are now well able to distinguish the marks of the Dharma, no different from myself. You may swiftly prepare and offer pure sustenance at any time. Among my assembly, there may be flying immortals, devas, noble sages, true ones, youths, earthbound immortals, and Daoists—both men and women—who follow me as I traverse the lands, their divine minds weary and exhausted. Whatever they require, you should provide with pure offerings at the proper time. Such giving is the perfect fulfillment of the city of equality of the One Vehicle’s ocean of emptiness.”

Again, he addressed the Elder Good Seed and the Great King: “If one offers with a mind of perfect equality, whether noble or base, whether much or little, whether sufficient or insufficient, it should be given in due time. Now, I shall return my spirit to the principle of the unconditioned, abiding in the unmoving, quiescent ground of extinction.”

When Good Seed and the assembly heard these words, each clasped their hands, raised their heads, and let out long cries, wailing and lamenting, snapping their fingers so that the sound resounded through the ten directions. Then, all the devas and earth-bound spirits, every forest and tree, mountain and river, valley and hill—whether human or non-human, bird or beast—all joined in mournful cries, weeping and shedding tears without cease.

Then, from among the assembly, an immortal rose from his seat, bowed his head in reverence, wiped his tears, and again prostrated himself, addressing the Heavenly Honored One: “How can you suddenly abandon your original vow, leaving the world bereft and without refuge? And now, as the great king Good Seed makes offerings, how can you return your spirit to the unconditioned? In the past, Heavenly Honored One, you toiled for countless years, enduring the turning of kalpas, dying and being reborn, succeeding and failing, yet you still sustained the taste of wondrous delicacies, offering them equally. Whether human or non-human, all were sated at once. How much more so now, when Good Seed makes his offering, do you speak of returning your spirit? Moreover, you tell Good Seed: ‘You now truly believe that the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One receives this offering.’ Is this truly receiving or not receiving? Is this truly a body or not a body? As I reflect, if the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One receives this food, it is certainly not receiving food; if he receives this body, it is certainly not receiving a body. Such a body is a body yet not a body; such food is food yet not food. Why then do you all weep and lament without end?”

Then, the Heavenly Honored One addressed the immortal: “So it is, so it is, just as you have said. This body is not a body; this food is not food. Cease your sorrow. Now, I shall return, yet in truth, there is nothing to return. You have already well understood the subtle and wondrous treasury of the One Vehicle’s ocean of emptiness—there is no ‘is’ or ‘is not,’ no thought of love or attachment. Constantly, with the mind of great compassion and equality, one contemplates beings as a mother cherishes her child. Wherever there is a place, one should uphold the One Vehicle’s ocean of emptiness, and one will clearly perceive that my body is not a body, that there is no body at all. It is like the great ocean, whose watery nature is luminous, reflecting the depths so that fish, turtles, dragons, and aquatic creatures are all made visible.”

Just as the great ocean, though its watery nature is without fish, reveals fish through its water, so too am I now without body, yet reveal a body through myself—precisely thus. Then, out of great compassion, the Heavenly Worthy emitted radiance, sending forth from his mouth manifold lights. Their brilliance leapt forth, illuminating all within the fourfold assembly. Once this light had passed, they understood the matter.

The virtuous seed then spoke: “The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion, in his mercy, has manifested this auspicious sign—these manifold lights, rare and wondrous indeed! Such an event surely portends that soon he will return to the unconditioned Dao.”

“Should you make offerings, reverently serving all beings, whether human or non-human, know this: the Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion has emitted his great radiance, illuminating the three realms and the beings of hell. Wherever the light reaches, once it has fully opened, all are overcome with sorrow, falling silent in grief, prostrating and bowing their heads.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy again addressed the elder Virtuous Seed and the great king: “Good son, the offerings you have brought for me and the four assemblies—whether human or non-human—are most fitting for this moment. Now I shall indeed return to the unconditioned principle of the Dao. The bodily form of the past is not something you have seen, nor something you may seek.”

When the elder Virtuous Seed and the great king heard this, they raised their voices in wailing, choked with sorrow and lament: “Alas! Alas! Now we are orphaned, the three realms all empty!” Then, addressing the assembly, they said: “Our children, the Heavenly Worthy’s past bodily form is about to depart the world. Let us all together entreat the Heavenly Worthy.” Thereupon, all the children rose, prostrating themselves fully, and with one voice pleaded: “We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to take pity on us, to remain in the world, and not to speak of departing.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed Virtuous Seed: “Good sons, do not weep so bitterly, scattering your minds. You should know that when you observe this body, it is like a body of great fire, like a body of great wind, like an echo in a valley, like a reflection in water—never at rest for even a moment, like a thread once spun, with no way to trace or continue it. You should contemplate all conditioned things as poisoned food, full of many faults and afflictions.”

Thereupon, Virtuous Seed thought to himself: “The Heavenly Worthy of Great Compassion does not wish to remain in the world. He urges us to cease our weeping. His parables and words leave no room for doubt. How then can I not weep? Alas! Alas! The world is empty and void! I beseech the Heavenly Worthy to take pity on his children, to remain long in the world, and not to return to the Dao.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy again addressed the elder Virtuous Seed and the great king: “Good son, you should not speak thus, entreating me to remain long to expound for you the ocean of emptiness of the One Vehicle. Good son, it is out of great compassion that I take pity on you and linger until now to expound the subtle treasury of the One Vehicle’s emptiness. I am always without self. How could there be a self? Why? All dharmas are suffering, empty, without self, and even ‘without self’ is not a self. Because there is no self, it is called ‘my return.’ Virtuous Seed, you and all should contemplate all conditioned dharmas as impure, without self, impermanent, not abiding in this body, full of many faults and afflictions—like bubbles on water, like mirages, like transformations. For this reason, you and the four assemblies should not weep. Instead, calm your minds in due order, and do not be alarmed or doubtful about me or the great assembly.”

Then the elder Virtuous Seed and the great king bowed their heads and said: “So it is, just as you have taught. All existence is impermanent, without self, without body, yet through skillful means, a body is manifested where no body exists. But we, unable to comprehend, cannot help but grieve. When I reflect on this sorrow, I realize there is no true sorrow, and joy arises instead. Though I weep now, there is no true weeping, and gladness arises.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy, pleased, praised him: “Excellent, excellent, good son! You have understood that I, through the power of skillful means, appear as one among beings, yet there is no arising where arising seems, no self where self appears. Now you rejoice, and sorrow has no hold on you. You have grasped the marks of dharma. It is like climbing a tower in spring to gaze in all directions—all who come to gather look up from afar at the tower. I am now like one who has ascended to those clouds, like one upon a tower, seeing all beings and enabling their awakening.”

He further praised Virtuous Seed: “Now you are also able to contemplate the marks of dharma as illusory, as transformations, and through the power of skillful means, remain unstained. Why? The nature of dharma is pure. Because it is pure, there is no self, no sorrow. Good son, I now accept your offerings of equality, wishing that you and all beings may escape the perils of birth and death, that all afflictions may come to rest in the unshakable ground of the One Vehicle, and that you may constantly abide in bliss, subtle and complete, becoming good fields for the world.”

Then the elder Virtuous Seed and the great king, having heard this teaching, bowed and said: “Excellent, Compassionate Worthy! If I am capable of abiding and serving as a field of blessing, then I shall be able to understand all dharmas. But now, we and the four assemblies are like mantises, truly unable to fathom the constant principle. How then can we be considered fields of blessing for the world? We, with our retinues, grieve and weep, encircling you with incense, wholeheartedly reverent, humbly presenting great offerings and provisions for your sustenance. We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to show mercy to us all.”

Thereupon, the four assemblies spoke in verse:

We bow our heads to the unsurpassed master,
The four assemblies, with four conditions, together entreat.
All the highest perfected ones and divine youths,
Forever cut off from existence and non-existence, ever our refuge.

Having seen the great jeweled city of the One Vehicle,
We children are drowning in suffering.
Our hearts are heavy with longing and sorrow,
Like calves who have lost their loving mother.

Poor, without dharma, without refuge,
Like sick children, like those with afflicted minds.
Without physician, without medicine, tormented by the heart’s afflictions,
All that we seek, all that we eat, is fulfilled.

Though we have taken the lesser physicians of the worldly Small Vehicle,
None of their views, none of their doubts, could ever be resolved.
We beseech the Great Compassionate and Great Merciful Worthy,
For our sake and for the sake of conditions, to expound horizontally.

Now we are like a kingdom without a lord, a land without a ruler,
All beings in the four realms suffer from hunger and famine.
We four assemblies are likewise:
The Heavenly Worthy entrusts us, then returns to his divine form.
Serene and eternally abiding, beyond birth and death,
We are left orphaned, like grieving children.
Having lost the Dharma, lost the Worthy, like withered vines,
We weep and wail, certain of our death.

We only pray that you do not forsake your great compassion,
But universally expound the City of the Treasury of Wisdom of the One Vehicle.

At that time, Haikong, having heard the verse, rose and said:
“Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, your words are like a parable—
Just as a king raises his many children,
Their forms upright, their hearts vast with love and care,
Teaching them the classics until all are thoroughly versed,
Then the great king entrusts them to govern separate lands and guide their people.

I am now likewise, like a prince,
Having received the complete teachings of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy,
I shall return to my divine form.
We bow our heads to the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy,
Only praying that you do not abandon the beings of the Two Vehicles.
If the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy remains long in the world,
Expounding the Treasury of Sweet Dew, filling all things,
Then beings will not conceive thoughts of fear or fall into hell.

It is like a man who first studies the arts,
Only to be seized by officials and imprisoned.
His fellow prisoners ask: ‘For what crime have you come to this prison?’
The man replies: ‘I am deeply afflicted.
If I could but escape, I would surely find peace and attain great dharmic power.’

Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, you are likewise:
For the sake of all beings, dwelling in the city of suffering,
Revealing that suffering is not yet exhausted,
Manifesting in accordance with the inclinations of beings.
The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy teaches and shows the good seed,
Like a physician who thoroughly understands the properties of medicine,
And again administers wondrous medicine to his child.
All other external students who receive instruction
Cannot perceive it.
Now our Heavenly Worthy is likewise:
Alone, he teaches the profound and subtle treasury of the precious Dharma to the good seed.
How can we not be seen and pitied?
The wondrous Dharma of equality should not be kept secret or hoarded.
Like that physician who teaches only his child and not external students,
One might think the great master’s affection has preferences,
That the Dharma treasure is kept secret,
But the heart of great compassion ultimately has no preferences.
Why is this?
We four assemblies do not see your teachings.
We only pray that you remain long in the world and expound for us.

It is like beings whose bodies suffer illness,
Who abandon the distant, level path and take the perilous road,
Where dangers and hardships abound, and they endure manifold sufferings.
If there were no other person to take pity on them and teach them,
They would be shown the level path.
We four assemblies are likewise:
The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, for the sake of great compassion,
Points out to us the treasury of the One Vehicle.
For this reason, we come to understand the equal marks of emptiness and existence.”

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed Haikong, saying:
“Do not let your minds be like those of ordinary people, speaking of preferences.
You should each put aside your sorrow and no longer grieve.
Be diligent and vigorous, maintaining right mindfulness.
If you have any doubts, freely ask and I shall resolve them.
Whether I am empty or not empty, constant or not constant,
Suffering or not suffering, dependent or not dependent,
Abiding or not abiding, departing or not departing, returning or not returning;
Whether suddenly existent or suddenly non-existent, neither constant nor inconstant,
Neither blissful nor non-blissful, neither annihilated nor non-annihilated,
Neither real nor non-real, neither extinguished nor non-extinguished—
Such and other countless aspects within the Dharma,
Whatever you ask, whatever you doubt,
I shall explain for you accordingly,
And I shall also expound for you the flavor of equality.

After I pass away, it will be exceedingly difficult to encounter my manifested form in the world,
Difficult to encounter the body of wisdom, difficult to trust in your own body.
Such difficulties—hard to see, hard to hear.
You have long since perfected the great precepts,
Fulfilled all virtues, and your practice is without flaw,
Thus you have been able to see my form—rare indeed, inconceivable!

Good son, Haikong Treasury of Wisdom,
You have long since departed from the eight difficulties of birth and death,
Attained the vajra body,
And thus encountered me—this should not be in vain.
Good son, in the past, during former kalpas,
I underwent manifold hardships,
And now have attained this unsurpassed fruition of the Dao.
For your sake, I provisionally manifest the abandonment of this body,
And shall return to the divine form of the non-action One Vehicle,
The Dharma city of Haikong, replete with all manner of virtuous treasures,
Which you may take as you will.
Therefore, you shall adorn the true Dharma,
And comprehend the meaning of emptiness.
You shall be of one mind, accumulating manifold virtues,
Encompassing them like the sea, fulfilling the treasury of the heart of wisdom and virtue.
For this reason, you are now named ‘Haikong Treasury of Wisdom of the One Vehicle.’

Good son, it is like merchants who encounter a treasure city,
Personally gather its riches, and return home to become greatly wealthy.
You are likewise:
Having encountered my form and attained the One Vehicle,
Deeply comprehending the treasury of the Dharma,
You accomplish the Dharma body—just so.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy addressed all the earth immortals:
“Do not let your minds be complacent and conceive thoughts of satisfaction.
Though you students have now left the household life in this Great Vehicle,
Do not covet the ranks of the earth immortals and the like.
Though you four assemblies have donned the robes of great compassion—
Yellow-brown garments and dark headcloths—
Your hearts have not yet been imbued with the treasury of the One Vehicle Dharma.
Though the four assemblies of earth immortals practice gentleness and weakness,
Wandering through famous mountains,
Their hearts have never sought the treasury of the One Vehicle Dharma.
Though they have left the household life, they have not attained the true Dharma;
Though they wear the five flowers, their fetters are not yet severed.

Now, out of great compassion, for the sake of Haikong Treasury,
I expound the true teaching of the One Vehicle.
You four assemblies, while I am still present,
In the midst of the great assembly, I harmoniously resolve
The Dharma-nature of the One Vehicle, true and unshakable.
For this reason, you four assemblies should gather your minds,
Be courageous and vigorous, shatter all fetters and afflictions,
And attain the clarity and purity of the Dharma.”

At that time, the earth immortals, hearing the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy expound these profound teachings, were filled with shame and remorse. Overcome with deep sorrow, their body hairs stood on end, tears streaming down their faces. They bowed their heads to the ground, prostrating at the Worthy’s feet, and knelt to address him, saying: “Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, swiftly proclaim the supreme teaching of emptiness and the absence of self, to assuage the sorrows of the Haikong Treasury. Just as among all beasts, the elephant king is supreme, so too is the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy foremost among all the heavens across the ten directions. If there are beings who arouse great diligence, they can eradicate the three fetters of affliction and the ignorance of the three realms—just as a farmer, in the autumn month, diligently plows the deep earth to remove noxious weeds. If even one among us four assemblies arouses such great diligence, it is likewise. Though the sufferings of the three realms—whether constant or inconstant—are difficult to endure, for this reason, Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, though the constant and inconstant abide, the reversal of spirit is supreme. Just as a king, knowing his life is nearing its end, mercifully pardons all under heaven, releasing prisoners from their bonds and shackles, allowing them to go free before he departs this life, so too does the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy teach us and all beings, enabling us to awaken to the One Vehicle of the Haikong Treasury. Thus, the four assemblies, having received the benefit of the Dharma, aroused great diligence. Together, they rose, paid homage, and took their leave.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy wandered to the south of the city, where he gathered with an innumerable assembly of heavenly perfected ones, youths, and divine youths upon a seven-jeweled mystic terrace. Then, from the ten directions, supreme sages, boundless divine kings, and the thirty-two great and lesser heavenly kings, each accompanied by five hundred fifty-five thousand five hundred fifty followers, assembled at the Dharma site. As one, they paid homage, gazing upon the Heavenly Worthy, and took their seats in due order.

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, seated upon a seven-jeweled mystic throne within the city, expounded the One Vehicle of the Haikong Treasury. Within the city, the heavenly musicians played zithers, zhu, and konghou, their melodies plaintive and exquisite, their sounds rare and refined. Together, they scattered flowers and burned incense, their fragrance wafting and flowing, perfuming the boundless expanse, both within and without, naturally evoking the Daoist intent. Then, the Heavenly Worthy, in deep contemplation, his body and mind unmoving, emitted a great radiance that pervaded the ten directions and the boundless worlds. Even in the hells and among the hungry ghosts, none failed to behold it. Thus, the four assemblies—whether human or non-human—and all beings, though seated together, each received benefit. All whose faculties were stained by attachment to the light’s appearance awakened in their hearts, aroused great diligence, and single-mindedly listened with reverence.

At that time, Haikong Treasury of Wisdom rose from his seat, adjusted his robes, stepped forward, and bowed to the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “Virtuous One, I have attended upon you for countless kalpas, yet never before has there been a day like this. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy has emitted a great radiance that pervades the ten directions without exception, universally encompassing all—heaven above and heaven below, all beings, whether human or non-human, each receiving benefit. I wonder, Heavenly Worthy, what extraordinary sign this is, benefiting all beings in such a manner.”

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, moved by great compassion, replied to Haikong Treasury of Wisdom: “Excellent, excellent, good son. Return each to your seat, and I shall explain this for you. Good son, in the past, I expounded the One Vehicle of the secret treasury with great compassion, broadly unfolding the Dharma teachings for gods and humans, universally delivering all to receive the true Dao. Reverently observing the three grades, they traversed the ten directions and the five billion heavens. I opened the great kalpas, transforming and delivering beings, in past kalpas and future kalpas, adapting to each realm. Contemplating emptiness and the emptiness of appearances, utterly unattached, they received the samādhi of emptiness, yet without any fixed appearance. For this reason, I shall now return to the realm of formlessness, naturally united in root.

Haikong Treasury of Wisdom, you should now request the essential teachings in a timely manner. I observe that beings dwell in the city of afflictions, deeply attached to evil appearances, each tormented by their own sorrows. Thus, out of compassion, I manifest a responsive form—not a body of afflictions, nor a body of the five turbidities. You should know that the One Vehicle of the Haikong Treasury observes beings and teaches the Dharma accordingly.”

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, wishing to proclaim this meaning, spoke in verse:

The Haikong Treasury is inconceivable,
Formless, naturally responsive.
All beings arise from the wisp of smoke,
Never losing the causes and conditions of birth.
Causes and conditions each have their counterparts,
Enduring kalpas of suffering, unceasing,
Difficult to escape, difficult to avoid.
Attachment to appearances makes liberation hard,
Following the kalpas like a turning wheel.
In the jeweled city, I abide,
Contemplating and expounding the One Vehicle.
Because beings differ,
My compassionate heart arouses pity.
The Haikong city is hard to enter,
Thus I repeatedly expound these wondrous words.
Those who see the Daoists
Naturally attain the true Dao.
Gathering to see the Daoists,
Diligently study and enter the city of emptiness.
Daoists cultivate the immortal Dao,
In one lifetime, no rebirth.
The immortal Dao gathers and endures,
Unobstructed and without interval.
The distant great immortal king
Roams and delights in the Great Mystery.
I shall now depart,
My body of quiescence and unobstructedness.
All sufferings have their causes,
Only the wise know the truth.

Then, the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken these verses, addressed Haikong Treasury, saying: “Good son, Haikong Treasury of Wisdom, you have long since planted the roots of virtue in past lives, ascending the supreme Dao. Your fame is equal and impartial, like the great sea that receives all streams. You are likewise—responding to the lower realms, establishing the great treasury for all beings, inconceivable in its vastness. I observe your heart, possessing skillful methods, desiring to heal the illnesses of beings. Good son, in the future, beings will be constantly afflicted by great bodily diseases—ailments of the mind, the abdomen, the head, the hands—treat them as you see fit. I shall now return my spirit to the realm of non-action and immutability.”

At that time, Haikong, having heard these words, grew sorrowful in his heart. Prostrating himself with his head to the ground, he wept and bowed, then addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: “How can you suddenly depart from the world and return to the realm of stillness and extinction? I only beseech the Heavenly Worthy to stir the great wind of compassion, universally revealing all—whether human or non-human—so that all may know nurturance and sustenance, delivering beings from the city of afflictions and securing them in the treasury of peace. May all beings, upon seeing the sick, be instantly released. With the great rain of the Dharma, shower all afflicted beings, guiding and illuminating all existence—this I shall never refuse.”

Then, the Heavenly Worthy smiled and replied to Haikong: “Excellent, good son! You are able to establish the great vessel spanning the Three Realms, serving as the great bridge for all gods, humans, and beings in the boundless worlds—those suffering in distress and all moving creatures—ferrying them into the City of Plum Void, comforting those in the realm of death and form. Furthermore, I instruct you, Haikong: contemplate the secret treasury of the One Vehicle, the *Haikong*, and expound it for others, traveling to the boundless worlds in the ten directions. Such lands are beyond conception. With diligence and joy, Haikong Treasury of Wisdom, all beings—dull-rooted and slow to awaken—do not comprehend that all, whether human or non-human, return to emptiness. Emptiness is without the mark of self; yet through the absence of self, false distinctions arise.”

Thereupon, Haikong rose and again addressed the Heavenly Worthy: “Greatly compassionate Heavenly Worthy, how is it that all these beings shall be utterly empty? If all is empty, how then can there be sin and merit, suffering and joy?”

The Heavenly Worthy replied to Haikong: “Good son, you should know that all beings shall return to emptiness. Precisely because they return to emptiness, they falsely create manifold sins. Where sin is not empty, this is called the suffering of sin; where merit is not empty, this is called the joy of merit. The mind, stained by sin and merit, knows suffering and joy, hatred and love. Through these causes and conditions, sin and merit arise. If one observes one’s own body—since the body is empty, all dharmas are also empty—where then is the form of sin, and in what place does it reside? If it resides in affliction, the mark of affliction is empty; if it resides in merit, the mark of merit is also empty. Thus, know that sin is empty and merit is empty; since sin and merit are empty, this is called ‘emptiness of emptiness.’ Good son, you are able to skillfully transform, adapting to the responsive forms of beings—hence the name *Haikong*. Cause all beings to diligently contemplate and recite the *One Vehicle Treasury of Haikong*, word by word, line by line, verse by verse, with single-minded devotion. Know that such a person is the Heaven among Heavens, ever abiding in the meaning of the One Vehicle’s emptiness, ever dwelling in the City of Emptiness of the One Vehicle. Good son, if there are beings who know my formless nature, naturally sharing the same root, know that such a person comes ‘from the heavens above,’ having fulfilled the immortal Dao. All people of every land will together take refuge and praise them with kind words, calling it the Land of Eternal Joy and Immovability.”

Again, the Heavenly Worthy addressed Haikong Treasury, saying: “Good son, if there are beings born in the lower realms, dwelling in the city of afflictions, who recognize the body as suffering and awaken their minds to tell the people: ‘We beings all dwell together in the fiery city of afflictions, poisoned by the three toxins—how can we escape and leave the city of birth and death? How can we enter the Dharma-city of the One Vehicle, the Land of Eternal Joy, a place without afflictions, a realm of peace?’”

At that time, the beings, having heard these words, were each filled with dread and thought to themselves: “How is it that we were born in the lower lands, within the city of afflictions, tormented by the fire of the three poisons? How can we be reborn and reach that land? That land of great peace is separated by vast seas. How can we cross and arrive there?”

Then, one among the assembly said: “I have seen three ships in that sea: the great ship can carry countless beings, the medium ship can carry hundreds of thousands, and the small ship can carry tens of thousands. These three ships possess great spiritual power, unafraid of wind and waves, with oars and rudders all newly sturdy. If we ourselves board these ships and sail across the waters, we shall reach the other shore with great joy.”

Thereupon, the four assemblies, having heard these words, rejoiced greatly and each prepared themselves. One million two hundred forty thousand people, with one mind, desired to depart for the other shore. Yet there were fifty million who chose not to go, each bidding farewell at the seashore. After parting, fifty thousand among the assembly boarded the great ship, ninety thousand boarded the medium ship, and one hundred thousand boarded the small ship, each according to their preference, finally embarking. Raising the sails, the wind was favorable, and in an instant, they traveled a thousand miles.

Then, those who remained on the shore laughed and sighed, saying: “How foolish are these people! Why seek death by entering the great sea, hoping to reach the other shore? How could they possibly arrive, even at the cost of their lives?”

At that time, those aboard the ships sailed forth, gliding upon the waters. Now, within this sea were great islands, and upon these islands were lands. The three ships arrived together at one such land—a vast and abundant country with natural food and drink. The people of this land were all of good heart, and their cities and dwellings were made of gold, silver, and the seven treasures.

Then, those on the small ship said to one another: “The ship we ride is weak in strength and cannot sail further. We have already traveled a hundred thousand miles from our homeland, and this land’s abundance is sufficient for us. We wish to remain here.” Thus, the small ship stayed in this land. The medium and great ships raised their sails and continued onward.

They passed another land, level and just, filled with the seven treasures, with natural clothing and food. None died prematurely, and all lived out their years.

Then, as their lives ended, their souls ascended to heaven, and their bodies did not turn to ash.

Those on the medium ship said to one another: “The ship we ride is weak in strength and cannot advance further. Let us remain in this land, where the rewards of our merit are sufficient for us.” Thus, they begged to stay in this land, and so they remained. Those on the great ship raised their sails and departed, arriving at the farther shore—the Land of Utmost Bliss. In this land, the people’s ground was of gold, their steps of jade, and rows of seven-jeweled trees bore sweet fruit. Their palaces were of the seven treasures, their lifespans long, and their virtue in harmony with the Dao. There, they were reborn and attained the Dao by nature.

Then, the Heavenly Venerable addressed Haikong, saying: “Good son, as for the three ships and their travelers of whom I spoke—some near, some far—what do you think?”

Thereupon, Haikong replied: “I do not understand, Heavenly Venerable, the meaning of your earlier words. Do the three ships truly differ in their carrying capacity? And yet, when sailing upon the waters, do they also differ in strength? How can it be that some travel near and some far? How is it that the three ships, raising their sails at the same time, arrive at different distances? What is the Heavenly Venerable’s intent?”

Then, the Heavenly Venerable answered Haikong, saying: “Good son, what do you make of my words about the three ships’ journey? Good son, the path may be strong or weak, high or low, far or near, great or small. Why is this so?”

The lands vary in distance, in rank, in poverty, in wealth. Why is this so? Those born in near lands dwell in the most wretched of realms, for the lower-bound beings who take birth there sink into the five sufferings, never again to plant the seeds of humanity. Their souls drift and wander, cut off from the root of human rebirth. Thus do all the sages, moved by great compassion, divide the One into Three, guiding beings along separate paths, that they may escape suffering and gradually enter the Great Vehicle. Hence the distinction of great lands, middle lands, and small lands—some near, some far. By this cause and condition, the Way manifests in refinement or coarseness, each matched to its corresponding affinity, naturally received as such.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable, his heart suffused with boundless compassion, spoke in verse:

With the eye of Dao I behold,
All good and evil in the world—
Originally one with the great mixed qi,
Defilement and attachment make them so.
Turning, they fall upon the paths of the Three Wretched Realms,
Once gone, they cannot return.
I plant the wisdom of the One Vehicle,
With compassionate heart I urge and pity,
Dividing it to teach the Three,
Guiding each by affinity to return.
Passing through the city of Haikong,
What worry is there not to ascend as immortals?
The small ship escapes the Three Wretched Realms,
The middle ship avoids the Eight Difficulties,
The great ship ascends the cloud-bound path.
The three ships follow my grace,
Riding the Great Vehicle to Jade Capital,
Bodies ascending the Seven Jeweled Mountain.
This body is of great wisdom,
Anxious for all roots.
If all roots are not delivered,
I shall not realize true fruition.
My heart holds the overflowing virtue of the Dao,
Through kalpas I rescue from calamity’s causes.
The middle ship plays amidst the clouds’ net,
Its mind at ease, universally embracing.
The Small Vehicle feasts in Crimson Numinance,
Yet may attain self-benefit through care.
Small and middle lack wisdom and awakening,
Cut off from hope of the Seven Jeweled City.

At that time, among the assembly there was an immortal named Miao Si, who rose from his seat, bowed his head to the ground in reverence, and addressed the Heavenly Venerable, saying: "Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, why do meritorious virtues and practices vary in weight, some great and some small, with corresponding differences in karmic reward? What is the meaning of this? Can one awaken to the causes and conditions behind it?"

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable replied to Miao Si, saying: "Good son, as for meritorious virtue, it arises from wisdom in practice, opening the gates of all dharmas and revealing the Dao to all beings—whether human or non-human. Contemplating the single-vehicle treasury of the sea of emptiness, one attains decisive insight, emptily comprehending all dharmas across the boundless lands and worlds of the ten directions, seeing them as clearly as the palm of one’s hand, with nothing left unseen.

Good son, if there are beings who single-mindedly perform prostrations, meditating on the wisdom-treasury of the single-vehicle sea of emptiness, forgetting sleep and food, fasting past noon, and upholding the precepts without fail—

Good son, it is like a filial son whose parents have died: embracing the coffin, he wails in grief, beating his breast and crying out to heaven, moving all within the kingdom, human and non-human alike, to weep with him. Thereupon, his parents immediately revive. Then, all the children rejoice together, leaping with boundless joy. My joy is likewise thus.

If there are beings who contemplate the wisdom-treasury of the single-vehicle sea of emptiness and expound it to others, forgetting to eat, I will guard and protect them, never abandoning my original vow, and my joy will be boundless. It is also like the filial son who does not lose his parents—so too is it thus.

Good son, if there are beings whose hearts abide in gentle yielding, whose bodies and minds endure humiliation, whose speech avoids evil, whose six senses are pure, and who do not join with humans, devas, or any beings to create an ‘evil city’ or accumulate wicked karma—it is like a compassionate mother who nurtures her beloved child, holding him close and never parting from her lap, always guarding and protecting him, never allowing him to quarrel with others. So too do I guard and protect their body, mind, speech, and intention.

Good son, if there are beings who practice great generosity, giving away their household wealth, kingdoms, wives, children, beloved kin, the seven treasures, and all precious things, bestowing them upon others and scattering blessings to all beings of the ten directions, human and non-human alike—it is like sweet rain that moistens all, so that every plant and tree receives its benefit. My compassionate giving is likewise thus."

At that time, Miao Si and the fourfold assembly, having heard these words, gained great dharma benefit. They each resolved to cultivate diligently, rose together, and approached the Heavenly Venerable. With single-minded devotion, they bowed in reverence, took their leave, and departed.

Thus concludes *Scroll Eight of the Heavenly Venerable’s Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*.
*Scroll Nine of the Heavenly Venerable’s Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom* begins.

**The Chapter on Abandoning and Receiving**

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable addressed King Good-Seed: "Good man, great king and elder, you have relinquished your wisdom and wealth, come from afar, and entreated me to expound the *Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*, abiding in the jeweled city within your kingdom upon the seat of the true adept.

"Good man, great king, having heard the true adept of the *Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom* inquire after illness, how does it appear to you?"

Thereupon, King Good-Seed and the elders, having heard the Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable speak these words, rose from their seats, prostrated at the Venerable’s feet, and addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "That true adept from afar possesses profound wisdom, making repayment difficult. He fully comprehends the marks of dharma and is unhindered in eloquence. All the immortals and adepts have resolved the *Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*, and none fail to enter the gate of wisdom. Moreover, he subdues the hosts of external paths and demonic forces, manifesting divine powers and skillful means—all have attained liberation. His wisdom is unfathomable, wondrous and subtle, rare indeed, rare indeed!

"The Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, for the sake of all beings, instructs the true adept to dwell in the jeweled city and expound the *Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*. At that time, all the disciples, the people of the world, the great kings, and the elders together aroused wholesome minds, relinquishing their bodies, wisdom, and wealth—houses, mansions, servants, and attendants—all were scattered in offering. Now, as that true adept expounds the Dharma, among those seated in faith are over eight thousand true adepts, seven hundred immortals, three hundred great kings, and hundreds of millions of devas and humans—both men and women—all following in attendance. Hearing the essential teachings of the *Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*, they become great bridges and Dharma stairways.

"Then, the true adept and his disciples employed their spiritual power, and within the jeweled city, all the palaces to the left and right became utterly empty. At that time, the true adept sat in the empty city, having removed all possessions, resting only upon a jeweled couch due to illness. All his disciples—both human and non-human—gathered around, gazing upon him with tears streaming down in a hundred rivulets, sighing in unison: 'The Great Compassionate True Adept abandons us, leaving us exposed and desolate! Alas, the true adept forsakes us, resting due to illness. Now we reflect: from whence does the great master’s illness arise? Can it be cured?
