If it may be healed, we, his disciples, would rather relinquish our bodies and lives to restore the great master, that he may accomplish for us the *Single-Vehicle Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom*, comforting us and abiding in the great jeweled city, where we may hear his teachings.'

"At that time, the *Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness and Wisdom* proclaimed: 'My illness arises for the sake of all beings. It is not the mark of illness, yet it is called illness; it is not the mark of seeing, yet it is called seeing; it is not the mark of emptiness, yet it is called emptiness; it is not the mark of speech, yet it is called speech. Our minds remain doubtful and unclear—how is this so? We only pray that the Great Compassionate One, for our sake, will distinguish and explain it.'

"Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable, with great compassion, replied to King Good-Seed: 'Good man, great king and elder, as you have said, the true adept of the *Sea of Emptiness* fully comprehends this mark of illness—there is no dharma of illness beyond it; he fully comprehends this mark of abiding—there is no dharma of abiding beyond it; he fully comprehends this mark of emptiness—there is no dharma of emptiness beyond it.'"

"He fully comprehends this mark of speech—there is no dharma of speech beyond it; he fully comprehends this mark of tranquility—there is no dharma of tranquility beyond it; he fully comprehends this mark of departure—there is no dharma of departure beyond it. Why is this so? Illness arises from nowhere; abiding finds no resting place; emptiness has no attachment. If there were a dharma, it would be unseen upon inspection; if it were an empty dharma, it would exist upon following it. For this reason, that which abides has nowhere to be placed, and that which departs has nowhere to arrive. Now, what is called illness has nothing to be ill; what is called abiding has nothing to abide; what is called emptiness has nothing to be empty; what is placed has nothing to be placed. Great kings, hold these words with a virtuous mind, and you shall attain understanding."

Thereupon, the great King Good-Seed among the assembly, having heard these words, rejoiced greatly in his heart. He bowed at the Venerable One’s feet and addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "If this is so, can the illness of the *Sea of Emptiness* be treated? Would healing it cause harm, or would it not worsen the affliction?"

The Heavenly Venerable of Great Compassion, amidst the boundless assembly of true immortals, divine youths, and earthbound Daoists, was earnestly questioned: "What is the cause of the illness of the *Sea of Emptiness* adept? How may it be extinguished, and its causes exhausted? May this bring joy to the assembly, that all may arouse a virtuous mind and delight in hearing the treasury of the single vehicle of *Sea of Emptiness* wisdom."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable replied to King Good-Seed: "Good man, you ask from whence the illness of the *Sea of Emptiness* arises. Good man, the illness of the *Sea of Emptiness* arises from the convergence of conditions, and thus there is affliction. If all beings were free from illness, the adept of the *Sea of Emptiness* would likewise be free from illness. Why is this so? The treasury of *Sea of Emptiness* wisdom enters the body of birth and death for the sake of beings. With the body of birth and death, there is the cause of illness. If all beings were free from illness, then the *Sea of Emptiness* would no longer suffer affliction. Good man, it is like a compassionate mother with but one child: if the child falls ill, the parents also fall ill; if the child recovers, the parents also recover. The adept of the *Sea of Emptiness* is likewise. Now, the *Sea of Emptiness* loves all beings as a child. For this reason, when beings are ill, the *Sea of Emptiness* is also ill. Good man, you ask from whence the illness of the *Sea of Emptiness* arises. Great kings, I now reflect: the illness of the *Sea of Emptiness* arises from great compassion."

Thereupon, King Good-Seed in the assembly, having heard these words, addressed the Heavenly Venerable: "Heavenly Venerable of Great Compassion, how is it that the adept of the *Sea of Emptiness* treasury of wisdom dwells in the jeweled city, yet the city is empty, without even a seat or throne? I now reflect upon this with great trepidation."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable replied to King Good-Seed: "Excellent, excellent, good man! You speak of the city’s emptiness—the Three Clarities’ Jade Capital and the Land of Eternal Bliss are likewise empty and void. King Good-Seed again addressed him: "If this is what is said, by what is it empty, that it is called empty and void?" The Heavenly Venerable replied: "It is empty of emptiness." He further asked: "By what is emptiness empty?" The Heavenly Venerable replied: "Emptiness has no distinctions. Why is this so? Distinctions are also empty, and thus it is called emptiness of emptiness." Good-Seed again asked: "Does emptiness distinguish or not?" The Heavenly Venerable replied: "Distinctions are also empty." He further asked: "If emptiness has no distinctions, of what dharma is it empty?" He replied: "It is empty of dharma-marks, empty of the six dusts. Since the six dusts are empty, dharma-marks are also empty." Good-Seed again asked: "What are dharma-marks?" He replied: "Dharma-marks are precisely liberation, and liberation is precisely dharma-marks. For this reason, since dharma-marks are empty, liberation is also empty." He further asked: "What is liberation?" He replied: "Afflictions are precisely liberation, and liberation is precisely afflictions. Since liberation is empty, afflictions are also empty." Good-Seed again asked: "If afflictions are illness, are they not illness? If they are illness, from whence does illness come? Does it come from the body, or not from the body? If it comes from the body, since the body-dharma has afflictions, how can it be called empty?" The Heavenly Venerable replied: "What I call illness is precisely afflictions; since afflictions are empty, the dharma of illness is also empty. Since the dharma of illness is empty, the dharma of the body is also empty. Why is this so? The afflicted body is like an illusion, like a dream. For this reason, it is empty of emptiness." Good-Seed again asked: "Among the four great elements—earth, water, fire, and wind—which great element is the body?" He replied: "The afflicted body is not born from the earth great, yet it does not depart from the earth great. It is likewise with the water, fire, and wind greats. The afflicted bodies of all beings arise from the four greats, and this is called illness. Thus, the true adept follows and is ill with them."

Thereupon, Good-Seed, having heard these words, rose and bowed, praising the single vehicle of the *Sea of Emptiness* treasury of wisdom: "This is my great teacher, who speaks to us of illness, that all conditioned things are impermanent, that the body-dharma is without self, and does not speak of the *Sea of Emptiness* as weary of the body; who speaks of the body’s suffering, and does not speak of the eternal bliss of the Jade Capital of the Mysterious Metropolis; who instructs the three vehicles and acts as a great bridge for all beings, ferrying them across the sea of birth and death. Dwelling in the empty city, he takes on illness in his body, pitying those beings, that they may recognize the suffering of countless kalpas in past lives. He urges the cultivation of vast merit, that all beings may be benefited, and that none may be caused distress. He exhorts and aids all beings to diligently practice vigor. As the great king of physicians, he treats the roots of all illness in beings, comforting and consoling them, lying ill in their stead."

Thereupon, the treasury of *Sea of Emptiness* wisdom addressed King Good-Seed: "Do not doubt that my body is ill, yet there is no illness. The illness I now have arises from past-life causes—deluded thoughts, inverted views, and the arising of afflictions. There is no substantial dharma in it, yet it is called illness."

"Why is this so? The four great elements combine to form what is provisionally called a 'body'; the four great elements have no master, and the body likewise has no attachment. The illness I now have arises entirely from attachment to the body—thus one should not generate attachment to the body. King Good-Seed, having understood the root of illness, should eliminate the notion of 'I' and the notion of afflictions, and extinguish the notion of dharmas.

You great kings should contemplate thus: this body is merely composed of various dharmas; this body of mine arises only from dharmas and perishes only through dharmas. This dharma-body does not know one another—when arising, it does not say, 'I arise, you perish'; when perishing, it does not say, 'I perish, you arise.' My thoughts of beings are likewise thus.

King Good-Seed, you should know and contemplate thus: this dharma-body is also inverted. This body of mine is the great affliction. You should be weary of and turn away from this body. How then can one be free from 'what is mine'? To be free from 'what is mine' is to be free from the two dharmas; to be free from the two dharmas is to be without thoughts of inner or outer, and all dharmas are equal.

How are they equal? We are eternally blissful, eternally blissful and pure; there is no self within or without, and I too am pure. These two equalities are all utterly empty. What is emptiness? It is merely names—emptiness arises from names. These two dharmas have no fixed nature in sequence. Attaining this equality, there is no other illness, only the illness of emptiness. The illness of emptiness is also empty; having understood the illness of emptiness, this is my having illness.

Now my illness is without reception yet received; I speak of the body as impermanent, yet the marks of dharmas do not perish. To establish faith and conviction, I provisionally posit a body, universally contemplating beings, arousing great compassion, and expounding the treasury of the One Vehicle. Taming this body of mine, I shall also tame all beings, removing manifold illnesses.

Now I speak of illness to sever the roots of clinging in beings. Having severed the roots of illness, there is nothing to be obtained. If there is nothing to be obtained, then clinging is severed. When all faculties are exhausted, this is my being without illness."

King Good-Seed, having heard this discourse, bowed his head in reverence, knelt, and praised: "Excellent! Excellent! Great compassionate one, for the sake of severing my attachments, you have spoken thus, taming this body of mine, and shall also tame all beings' suffering of old age, illness, and death. If not for this, we beings would live without benefit, bound by afflictions. The true one of the Sea of Emptiness has spoken to me—like one victorious in dharma, who may be called brave, and who can also remove the suffering of old age, illness, and death, abiding in the city, I have heard your discourse.

The true one of the Sea of Emptiness is likewise thus: for my having illness, you speak of having illness. My body's illness is neither real nor existent. The Treasury of Sea of Emptiness Wisdom is likewise neither real nor existent. If there are beings who contemplate this illness and do not generate attachment or views, such a person is the Treasury of the Sea of Emptiness, long since freed from the ailing body of birth and death.

Why is this so? The Treasury of Sea of Emptiness Wisdom has long since severed the afflictions subtle as dust, yet arouses great compassion. For those who love and grieve, it is weariness of mind in birth and death that causes one to lie ill. If there are beings who can generate weariness and turning away, following whatever they love, such persons, wherever they are born, are not covered by attachment or views.

Having understood the marks of dharmas, wherever they are born, they are not struck; moreover, with wisdom, they expound the dharma to beings, untying bonds—just as the Sea of Emptiness expounds the One Vehicle. All bonds are untied; having freed the body from bonds, they can free others from bonds. The bonds of self and others are all purified.

If there are beings who greedily cling to the flavors of goodness, the Sea of Emptiness strikes the notion of being bound. Afflictions have no master, and the body likewise has no self. Contemplating thus is the arising of skillful means—this is the Sea of Emptiness' liberation."

King Good-Seed, having spoken thus, gazed up at the honored countenance, bowed, and withdrew. Thereupon, the Sea of Emptiness, hearing Good-Seed's words, rejoiced greatly and addressed King Good-Seed: "Excellent! Excellent! Good man, you noble ones are my true children, with profound wisdom and unobstructed eloquence, able to understand the marks of dharmas. You are my great teacher—your wisdom is unfathomable, surpassing even my discourse.

I now reflect: King Good-Seed, your name is not in vain. You are truly able to establish the seeds that remain in the three realms—thus you are called Good-Seed. Good man, you should listen carefully as I distinguish and expound for you.

Good man, what is the bond of skillful means? It is the mind attached to views, the lesser vehicle and lesser views, adorning the Three Jewels. The seven-jeweled palace adorns the body, and one tames oneself, transforming beings, practicing dharmas of existence together, adorning the dharma within emptiness and formlessness with manifold embellishments. Such a person is bound by skillful means.

What is liberation through skillful means? Without attachment or views, one does not cling to the body as beloved, adorning it with subtlety and wonder, perfecting beings together, having understood the One Vehicle Treasury of Sea of Emptiness Wisdom, abiding unmoved, realizing emptiness as non-emptiness, speaking of existence as non-existence. With the power of skillful means, within emptiness and formlessness, one transforms the dharma, also guiding beings to tame themselves, weary of the body, not receiving any attachments. Such a person is liberated through skillful means.

Good-Seed King, if there is one lying ill, you should contemplate thus: all dharmas are without self; my body is impermanent, suffering, empty, and not-self. Though the body is ill, within birth and death, one transforms and liberates all without weariness—this is skillful means.

You should also contemplate this body of mine: the body does not leave illness, and illness does not leave the body. This illness and this body are neither new nor old—this is the skillful means of wisdom. If the body is ill yet tranquil, this is the skillful means of wisdom."

Good-Seed King, if there are beings who, though ill, entertain thoughts of unrestrained minds, not wearying of the body, and craving love and attachment—such persons follow the way of fools. Know that these beings do not depart from the suffering of birth-and-death and the torments of hell.

If there is one lying ill, contemplating all dharmas as suffering, empty, and without self—this illness of mine is within birth-and-death, yet not of birth-and-death. Since there is no birth-and-death, birth-and-death is without self. I, within birth-and-death, bear no defiled conduct, abiding in constant bliss, yet not in constant bliss, for it is not tranquil—this is the practice of oceanic emptiness.

Such a person forever departs from the city of birth-and-death and afflictions. Though possessing this body, they do not rely on body or mind; though within the three realms, they do not grasp at dharma-nature; though practicing emptiness, they hold no notion of emptiness.

Then the Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One addressed Good-Seed Elder-King: Though my body is ill, lying for the sake of all beings who suffer; though practicing formlessness, for those beings I ferry all across; though practicing non-action, for those beings I manifest a received body; though practicing non-movement, for those beings I display movement.

Through various expositions, though practicing the single vehicle of the oceanic emptiness treasury of wisdom, for those beings I manifest bodies throughout—even bodies as minute as motes of dust. Though practicing wisdom and turning the great Dharma-wheel, for beings in the dark chamber of ignorance, I reveal the great jewel-light, illuminating their afflictions, all arousing wholesome minds and practicing the single-vehicle practice.

Having spoken thus, Good-Seed King and his eight thousand ministers all aroused wholesome minds, joyfully paid homage, took their leave, and returned to their seats, awaiting further discourse.

At that time, among the assembly was a youth named Marvelous Thought. Rising from his seat, he held a lotus flower, faced the Heavenly Honored One with dignified steps, approached, and bowed, saying: "Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One, how does Oceanic Emptiness abide in the empty city, lying ill upon a seven-jeweled bed? In such a city, all is empty and nothing exists. We, along with the heavenly kings and the people of the world, have come together to hear the single-vehicle treasury of oceanic emptiness. Where does such a one constantly sit?"

Then the Heavenly Honored One replied to Marvelous Thought: "Excellent, excellent, good son! Noble and virtuous one, what is your intention in asking this? Have you come among this assembly for the Dharma or for a seat? Good son, in the past, in the great Floating-Ri Kingdom, I sat within a jewel no larger than a millet grain, expounding the essential Dharma for all beings. At that time, the fourfold assembly—both human and non-human—all entered the jewel, without obstruction or number. The beds and seats within the jewel were neither cramped nor narrow. How then do you say the city is empty and without a seat?"

Then Marvelous Thought, having heard this teaching, knelt and replied: "Great Compassionate Heavenly Honored One, I came here to hear of the single-vehicle treasury spoken of in this city. I did not expect Oceanic Emptiness to lie ill in an empty city without a seat."

Thereupon, the Heavenly Honored One replied to Marvelous Thought: "Good son, those who seek the Dharma spare neither body nor life, do not cling to notions of existence, do not perceive any form, and are free from sensual desire. Now, your teacher lies without illness, sits without a bed—neither non-existent nor existent. The city is empty and without treasure; only Oceanic Emptiness remains. Not seeking, yet seeking—the mind seeks the Dharma. Not seeing the body as seeking, not seeing form as seeking, not seeing speech as seeking; not seeing seeking as existent, not seeing seeking as non-existent, not seeing seeking as both existent and non-existent, not seeing seeking as neither existent nor non-existent, not seeing seeking as neither neither-existent-nor-non-existent, not seeing seeking as neither not-neither-existent-nor-non-existent.

Those who seek the Dharma do not see suffering as seeking, do not see bliss as seeking, do not see the cessation of accumulation as seeking, do not see the cultivation of the path as seeking. Why is this? The Dharma is free from idle discourse; to speak of it is to posit existence. Therefore, the great teacher seeks the Dharma in accordance with various seekings, in accordance with various existences. If one says that the true man Oceanic Emptiness lies ill, such a person engages in idle discourse and does not seek the Dharma.

Marvelous Thought, good son, you should know that the Dharma is called oceanic emptiness, yet oceanic emptiness is not the Dharma. If beings practice oceanic emptiness with their bodies, such persons seek oceanic emptiness, not the Dharma. Good son, the Dharma is called the single vehicle, yet the single vehicle is not the Dharma. If beings practice the single vehicle with their bodies, such persons seek the single vehicle, not the Dharma. Good son, the Dharma is without attachment, yet attachment is not the Dharma. If beings practice attachment with their bodies, such persons seek attachment, not the Dharma. Good son, the Dharma is called formless, yet formlessness is not the Dharma. If beings recognize by following forms and seek forms accordingly, they do not seek the Dharma. Good son, the Dharma is without abode, yet abode is not the Dharma. If beings abide within the Dharma, know that such persons practice abiding in the Dharma, not the Dharma itself."

At that time, the fourfold assembly, seventy heavenly kings, and eight thousand koṭis of beings—both human and non-human—received the benefit of the Dharma. In all dharmas, they became clear and pure, understanding suffering, emptiness, non-self, the impermanence of all conditioned things, and the absence of self in arising and ceasing. In the Dharma, all was purified for them.

Then Oceanic Emptiness, having heard these words, sat up in full, emitting subtle and wondrous light. Each hair on his body radiated light, each with various rare and supreme virtues. From his lion throne, light shone upon the thirty-six kingdoms of the eastern direction, where it transformed into great kings and sons of elders. It also illuminated the southern, western, and northern directions. Wherever the light reached, all beheld the body of Oceanic Emptiness—sixteen feet in height, seated upon a lion throne, adorned with supreme and wondrous majesty.

What the people of these lands had never seen before, they now beheld; what they had never heard, they now heard; what they had never understood, they now understood. This city’s jeweled dais, vast and all-embracing, held thirty-two thousand lion thrones, yet the thirty-six kingdoms remained unobstructed, and all who came found ample space to sit at ease. The youth Miao Si then addressed the Heavenly Venerable: “How is it that the adornments within this city are so rare and wondrous? Is this Oceanic Emptiness, or is it not? The city’s treasures are all extraordinary, its lion thrones beyond count, its great and lesser kings all dignified and majestic, seated together upon lion thrones. The assembly is filled with doubt—never has such a thing been seen. This city’s halls contain boundless lion thrones, yet nothing is hindered. What is your explanation? We wish to hear your discourse and resolve our questions.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable replied to Miao Si: “Excellent, excellent, good man! This city is emptiness—it is not nothingness, yet it is not something. For this reason, there is the true being Oceanic Emptiness, who is called liberation, beyond all thought. These kings, great and small, are also liberation, beyond all thought. Good man, it is like the devas entering a jewel: nothing is added or diminished. The celestial beings remain at ease as before, unaware that they have entered, yet those who are to be delivered see it clearly—they behold the devas entering the jewel, beyond all thought. The lion thrones entering the city of Oceanic Emptiness are likewise.

Good man, it is like the ocean entering a single mote of dust: the dragons, fish, and sea creatures within remain at ease as before, unconstrained, their watery nature unchanged, as it was originally. Oceanic Emptiness’s body, transforming into these kings—great and small—is also thus.

He further told Miao Si: “All beings who make offerings to Oceanic Emptiness of the One Vehicle Treasury cause the Threefold Heavenly Venerables of the past, present, and future to appear within a single mote of dust. Moreover, within a single subtle mote, they behold all the suns, moons, and stars of the ten directions. If a great wind arises, uprooting grasses and trees, all is shattered and broken—yet by recalling Oceanic Emptiness’s skillful power, one draws it into the mouth, and the body remains unharmed, at peace as before. If a fierce fire burns the kalpa to its end, by contemplating Oceanic Emptiness, the fire enters the belly, yet one remains at ease as before, untouched by heat, the fire unchanged, causing no harm.

He further told Miao Si: “I dwell within the city of Oceanic Emptiness, manifesting boundless skillful means beyond thought. At times, by divine power, I appear as Oceanic Emptiness’s subtle and wondrous body; at times as my true form, at times as an aged figure, at times as a king’s body, at times as a Dharma King’s body, at times as a body of poverty and sickness, at times as a golden body, at times as an ordinary body, at times as an animal’s body—innumerable transformations. I expound the Dharma in countless ways, teaching impermanence, suffering, emptiness, and non-self. All beings who hear these teachings come to understanding, together arousing the mind of goodness, relinquishing body, wisdom, and wealth to seek the supreme fruit. Though these bones may turn to dust, within a single mote of dust, great virtue arises again, beholding Oceanic Emptiness preaching within the city. They hear my discourse, and I listen to theirs, perfecting the profound wisdom of the One Vehicle. They reflect: ‘From whence did this body come? How can the evil roots of birth and death be severed, so as to enter the mysterious gate?’ The path of liberation is beyond all thought.

Some beings, upon hearing this inconceivable One Vehicle Dharma gate of Oceanic Emptiness’s skillful means, weep aloud. Their cries shake the ten directions and the boundless worlds of all lands, moving great and lesser kings, ministers, elders, men and women—each according to their kind—to arouse faith and receive this great Dharma, reciting it day and night without cease. Such people together attain the equal wisdom gate of Oceanic Emptiness.”

As he spoke these words, among the boundless assembly, a great king named Square City rose from his seat, raised his fists, and wept, making this great vow: “I wish to relinquish this body, offering it to all who beg. Let them take as they will—my hands, feet, head, eyes, ears, nose, marrow, brain, flesh, skin, bones—I give it all in offering. I offer my dwellings, palaces, beds, curtains, wives, children, servants, elephants, horses, chariots, gold, silver, lapis lazuli, mother-of-pearl, agate, coral, amber, pearls, and other treasures; clothing, food, and drink—I scatter them all. May this body, by relinquishing and receiving form, come to dwell in the wisdom gate of Oceanic Emptiness, the ground of liberation, to hear together the subtle sutra of the One Vehicle.”

Having spoken these words, they heard his discourse, and I listened, never growing weary.

Then the Heavenly Venerable, having heard King Square City’s words, rejoiced greatly and said to him: “Excellent, excellent, good man! Because of your compassion, you have aroused this great vow, becoming a bridge and ladder of the Dharma for all beings. King Square City, now your body is the ship of Oceanic Emptiness, ferrying all beings from the city of afflictions. Now your eyes are the lamp of Oceanic Emptiness, illuminating the paths of affliction for all beings. Now your hands are the strength of Oceanic Emptiness, severing the city of afflictions for all beings. Now your feet are the chariot of Oceanic Emptiness, transporting all beings across the three realms. Now your mind is the treasury of Oceanic Emptiness, expounding the sutras of wisdom and the treasury of teachings for all beings. Now your ears are the voice of Oceanic Emptiness, so that they hear my discourse, and I listen to theirs. Now your nose is the wind of Oceanic Emptiness, fanning the Dharma teachings so that all beings come to understand the One Vehicle Dharma gate of Oceanic Emptiness.”

Then the Heavenly Venerable further addressed King Great Citadel: "Elder, you have now entered the One Vehicle Dharma gate, abiding in the inconceivable realm, observing beings dwelling in the city of afflictions—like the flash of flint and stone, suddenly appearing, suddenly vanishing. For this reason, you are able to offer your body, hands, eyes, head, elephants, horses, chariots, gold, silver, and all treasures, scattering them all without reserve—what is hard to give, you give; what is hard to relinquish, you relinquish. You become the bridge for all beings to depart the city of birth and death. Your merit and virtue are inconceivable."

The Heavenly Venerable again addressed King Great Citadel: "Elder, good son, you practice compassion for the sake of all beings; you practice relinquishing the body because you are free from afflictions; you practice generosity because you are free from poverty; you practice purity because you are free from greed and anger; you practice listening to the Dharma because you are free from ignorance; you relinquish the royal throne because you are free from notions of noble and base; you relinquish wife and children because you are free from attachment and love; you practice great compassion to reveal the One Vehicle; you practice diligence to ferry all beings; you practice wisdom to understand all beings; you practice skillful means to manifest the Dharma; you practice merit and virtue to liberate all beings; you practice upholding precepts to extinguish the three poisons; you practice Oceanic Emptiness because you fear birth and death; you practice right mindfulness to eradicate evil causes; you practice construction to generate blessings and virtue."

Having spoken these words, suddenly from the four directions of the city, thirty-three celestial youths and jade maidens, hearing the Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable expound the Dharma to the king, instantly manifested their forms. Descending from the sky, they scattered lotus blossoms over the assembly, swirling and drifting like a great snowfall, filling the entire seating area. Then came wondrous sounds of fragrant flowers, zithers, harps, and lutes—resonant and harmonious, softly echoing throughout the gathering. Phoenixes, peacocks, and parrots soared in orderly flight, circling the assembly.

King Fangcheng and his ministers, seized with great awe, addressed the Heavenly Venerable: “Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, why do these celestial beings, youths, and jade maidens scatter such wondrous flowers? Is this fragrant blossom from heaven, or does it arise naturally? Does it grow from trees, or does it exist in empty space?”

Then the Heavenly Venerable, having heard these words, replied: “Not so, great king. These flowers are all pure and inconceivable blossoms. Why? When I speak of purity, it is neither internal nor external, neither born of heaven nor arising naturally, neither growing from trees nor existing in empty space, neither born of being nor born of emptiness. Because it transcends both emptiness and being, this flower is said to arise. Why? All teachings are pure; this purity is the wondrous flower. For this reason, it is neither born of heaven nor arising naturally, neither born of emptiness nor being, nor growing from trees. Why? If there were a birth of birth, there would be verification and faith; with verification and faith, slander would arise. To know this teaching is to destroy the *One Vehicle Great Compassion Sutra*.”

The Heavenly Venerable further addressed King Fangcheng: “Noble one, within this city, such flowers are ever-present, and celestial beings and jade maidens from other realms gather here without cease. Phoenixes, peacocks, parrots, zithers, harps, and rare wonders are always here. Do not doubt. These pure and inconceivable flowers, these rare blossoms, are difficult to conceive and express.”

Hearing this, King Fangcheng rejoiced greatly and asked: “How does the Compassionate Venerable say that celestial flowers are born of purity and freedom from afflictions? If this is so, then all beings who offer these celestial flowers to the Compassionate Venerable would attain realization of birth free from afflictions. If realization is attained solely through flowers, why speak of cultivating Oceanic Emptiness to attain realization?”

The Heavenly Venerable replied to the king: “Good son, when I speak of realization, if one offers these celestial flowers to Oceanic Emptiness, then to say one attains realization is to speak of Oceanic Emptiness itself. Oceanic Emptiness is realization, which is this flower. If one cultivates Oceanic Emptiness and attains realization, one is free from afflictions. Even in hell, there are no afflictions; though manifesting in hell, there is no hell, no body to suffer punishment. Though manifesting as a hungry ghost, there is no hungry ghost, no hunger or thirst, only the perfection of merit and virtue, no body of a hungry ghost. Though manifesting in desire, there is no thought of desire, abiding constantly in radiant light, illuminating the body of afflictions. Though manifesting in anger, there is no thought of anger, only pure and subtle contemplation, no root of anger. Though manifesting in stinginess, there is no thought of stinginess, only vast joy and great compassion, relinquishing the body in generosity, no thought of stinginess. Though manifesting in laziness, there is no thought of laziness. Though entering the demon realm, there is no thought of demons. Though manifesting in teaching the Dharma, there is no thought of teaching. Though dwelling in a jeweled city, there is no thought of a jeweled city. Though manifesting illness, there is no thought of illness. Such a practitioner is one who has realized Oceanic Emptiness. You should make offerings to this flower, for it is the offering to the One Vehicle Oceanic Emptiness, the path of constant bliss. Through skillful means, one enters the city of Oceanic Emptiness and abides immovably.”

Having spoken these words, King Fangcheng and his assembly rose, bowed, knelt, and prostrated, addressing the Heavenly Venerable: “How is it that the Oceanic Emptiness true person of great virtue is our great teacher, expounding for us the wondrous Dharma with various parables, beyond conception? Who are the parents, wife, children, relatives, friends, companions, brothers, and sisters of the Oceanic Emptiness being? Who are the servants, attendants, elephants, horses, chariots, cities, villages, and dwellings? Where are they? Who are the sovereign, the people, the queen, and the crown prince? To whom do they belong? We beseech the Compassionate Venerable to explain and clarify for us.”

Then the Heavenly Venerable, having heard these words, smiled faintly, leaned on his armrest, and replied to the king: “Excellent, excellent, good son! Great king, you have skillfully inquired about the being of Oceanic Emptiness. I shall explain and clarify for you, so that all may understand the *Oceanic Emptiness Sutra*.”

Then the Heavenly Venerable responded in verse:
“You, King Fangcheng,
Listen single-mindedly,
For I shall expound for you.”

“To hear and see directly is already difficult,
How then to realize the empty city of wisdom’s Oceanic Emptiness?
Liberation is taken as mother,
Skillfully expounding the marks of the Dharma—
All are the Oceanic Emptiness’s compassion.
Virtue is taken as wife,
Compassion as eldest daughter,
Great filial piety and wisdom as sons.
The empty city is their dwelling,
Good faith their servants and companions,
Cultivation their spiritual friends.
Quiescence is their kin,
Penetrating understanding their good fields,
Clouds and dragons their galloping elephants and horses.
The constellations are their attendants,
Sun and moon their chariots,
The Six Perfections their neighbors,
The Four Immeasurables their children and grandchildren.
Chanting and singing are their family,
Eternal joy their abode.
The gardens of the Seven Treasures,
The dark capital’s forests,
Coral and wondrous blossoms,
The sweet fruits of expedient means.
The pools of Eightfold Refinement,
The great dew of the Six Superknowledges.
The One Vehicle is their body,
Complete with marks of adornment.
Teaching is their great kindness,
Absorbing essence their Dharma food,
Swallowing saliva their Dharma drink,
Repentance their garments.
Extinction is their funeral director,
Heaven and earth their coffin and outer casket,
The jeweled terrace their tomb,
Wisdom’s sun and moon their light,
Dew and mist their funeral robes and hearse,
Gold and silver their bricks and foundations.
Temporarily ashamed of compassion and filial piety,
Preaching the Dharma to repay kindness—
Pines and cypresses their great wealth.
Yellow essence on clear islets,
The quiet mind their bed and seat,
Extensive learning their marrow of wisdom,
Pure mind their bathing.
Contemplating Oceanic Emptiness in sleep,
Upholding precepts to guard the wise.
The formless is their sovereign lord,
Immortal youths their people,
Sages and perfected ones their ministers,
The Jade Capital their golden city.

You, King Fangcheng,
With a good heart as your companion,
Simply extinguish the thieves of affliction,
And bravely know the Way yourself.
Dispel the four kinds of Māra,
And triumphantly lay the foundation for ten thousand paths.
Oceanic Emptiness has no arising or ceasing,
Yet manifests when there is birth.
Universally appearing in all lands,
Like the sun shining without partiality.
Preaching the Dharma to liberate the ten directions,
Countless beings attain deliverance.
Compassion for others and oneself—
No discriminating thoughts.
Though knowing the eternal honor of eternal joy,
The lands and beings are empty,
Yet constantly practicing purity,
Teaching and transforming sentient beings.
With the power of good expedient means,
All can be accomplished as wished.
Sometimes manifesting old age, sickness, and death,
Perfecting the bodies of beings,
Understanding the Dharma as illusion.
Devas, humans, immortals, and jade maidens,
Attendants scattering flowers.
Princes and ministers,
Seeing the flowers, all are astonished and doubtful.
Comforting all beings,
Offering celestial flowers and food.
Beings cling to permanence,
Yet now realize impermanence.
All beings gather,
Together entering the empty city,
Surrounding the Oceanic Emptiness’s bed,
Asking after illness with sorrowful weeping.
To console and instruct beings,
Expounding the order of Oceanic Emptiness.
Scriptures and mantras,
Benefiting all beings.
The world’s heterodox teachings—
At that time, all leave the household life.
Thereby attaining right wisdom,
False views all vanish.
Sometimes as the light of sun and moon,
Pervading the three realms’ abodes;
Sometimes as wind, water, or fire,
Withering trees so they do not bloom.
When the world suffers from epidemics,
Manifesting as good physicians.
Those who can take the medicine
Dispel illness and the three poisons.
When beings suffer hunger and famine,
Manifesting bodies to provide food.
Dry bones can live again,
And quench thirst in times of drought.
Kings and people,
All rejoice and pay reverence,
Abiding in the Oceanic Emptiness’s city,
Listening to the Dharma without fixed time.”

At that time, the Heavenly Worthy, having spoken this verse, addressed King Fangcheng: “Good son, you should know that the Oceanic Emptiness Body is truly ineffable. The body of past, future, and present abides ever in the city, unshaken and unmoved, neither going nor coming, neither born nor dying. For all beings, it expounds the treasury of teachings, the manifold doctrines and subtle scriptures, ever constant as before. Yet it is not aware, nor holds notions of going or coming.

Sometimes it appears in the form of an elder, revealing to beings the Dharma of impermanence—birth, aging, sickness, and death. Sometimes it takes the form of apes, monkeys, elephants, or horses. Sometimes it manifests its true body, adorned with seventy-two marks and eighty-one excellences, its appearance wondrous and unique, its wisdom unmatched, its virtue profoundly deep. Skillfully expounding the Dharma, for all beings it employs manifold expedient means to transform and guide the Three Vehicles. Following the needs of beings, it manifests bodies, proclaiming the One Vehicle Treasury, universally ferrying beings to transcend the body of afflictions and rebirth, all entering the gateway of Oceanic Emptiness wisdom.”

Thereupon, the four assemblies, having heard this teaching, all rose to bow and praise: “The One Vehicle Oceanic Emptiness True One, for our sake, has distinguished and expounded it. Within our assembly, each of us pays reverence, all receiving the teachings, transmitting and transforming what was unheard before, universally enabling mastery of the unimpeded scriptures, profound comprehension of their mysterious meaning, and realization of the true Dharma ground.”

Then, the four assemblies, having heard the Great Compassionate Venerable One conclude the sutra, gazed upon the honored countenance, took leave, and withdrew.

Thus concludes *Fascicle Nine of the Supreme One Vehicle Oceanic Emptiness Wisdom Treasury Sutra*.
*Fascicle Ten of the Supreme One Vehicle Oceanic Emptiness Wisdom Treasury Sutra* begins.

**Chapter on Universal Record**

At that time, the Heavenly Venerable manifested divine power within the Jeweled City, transforming it into a mysterious terrace, supremely subtle and wondrous. Upon this terrace appeared seven treasures, exquisitely adorned and uniquely splendid, with hanging silken banners and canopies filling the entire space.

Then, the Heavenly Venerable radiated great luminosity from within the terrace, illuminating the ten directions and boundless worlds, so that all lands in the ten directions became resplendently bright. At that moment, the celestial great sages, flying deva-kings, cinnabar immortals of the primordial beginning, supreme celestial lords, the August Emperor of the Fusang Jade Dawn, all heavenly perfected ones, the left and right perfected ones, perfected youths, earthly immortals and Daoist adepts, demon-kings of the three realms, dragon-kings of the myriad seas, good men and good women, both human and non-human, all gathered at the seat to hear the Great Compassionate Venerable expound the *Oceanic Emptiness Wisdom Treasury of the One Vehicle*. Overjoyed in their hearts, each brought hundred-fold blended incense that emitted fragrance without burning. Celestial musicians played in unison, circumambulating and praising, offering priceless treasures.

Then, the Heavenly Venerable, wishing to withdraw the divine radiance, returned to the unshakable abode of the Jade Capital’s Ever-Joyful Lodge. He addressed Oceanic Emptiness, saying: “If any have doubts, now is the time to ask and resolve them swiftly. The supreme Dharma treasure will soon enter samādhi. Among you, if any harbor uncertainties, speak now without regret.”

At that time, among the assembly was a Daoist named Precious Radiance. Hearing the Great Compassionate Venerable’s words, he wept bitterly, unable to restrain himself: “Alas, Compassionate Venerable, why do you return to the unshakable abode? We lesser immortals are left desolate and exposed.”

Then, from among the assembly arose a divine youth of inconceivable, supreme perfection. Rising from his seat, he bowed deeply, prostrated twice, and knelt to address the Heavenly Venerable: “I wish to ask a question—will there still be time? I pray the Compassionate Venerable will not deem it an offense.”

Thereupon, the Heavenly Venerable praised the youth, saying: “Excellent, youth! Your merit and virtue are inconceivable. You are the wellspring of human and divine wisdom, fully equipped to transform and guide all beings.”

Then the youth addressed the Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable: “After the Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable’s passing in the past, all beings no longer beheld the Compassionate Venerable’s physical form, nor could they hear the true Dharma of Oceanic Emptiness. Why is this? In the future world, people will grow shallow and insincere, wholesome Dharma will gradually decline, and unwholesome Dharma will flourish.”

At that time, teaching all beings to cultivate the fruits of merit and virtue was most sublime, enabling them to cross beyond the city of afflictions. Yet I pray the Compassionate Venerable will take special pity—though they expend vast wealth, the share of merit and fruit is meager, not even matching a fraction.

Good man, if there are beings who make offerings to the Heavenly Venerables of the ten directions and the Three Realms, to all the Great Sages, the Three Heavenly Perfected Ones, and the earthbound immortals and Daoist adepts, such offerings do not compare to one who, with a heart of compassion for all, gives even a single mouthful of food to a beast, saving its life and ensuring its peace. Such merit is most supreme, surpassing the former by a hundred thousand myriad times. Such a mind of giving yields boundless, immeasurable merit and virtue.

Good man, in all the true scriptures of the Dharma where I expound on giving, my aim is to inspire newly practicing earthbound immortals, Daoist adepts—whether ordained or lay—good men and good women, to awaken the mind of Oceanic Emptiness, cultivate the practice of compassion, and give alms to the poor, the orphaned, the aged, the sick, the distressed, the imprisoned, those suffering from hunger and cold, and all who are destitute and starving, so that all may be fully sated. Such givers are called bridges, ferrying beings across the sea of birth and death.

Good man, in the future, beings will fail to comprehend my Dharma, focusing solely on the Field of Reverence while neglecting the Field of Compassion. Good man, what is the Field of Reverence? When beings pay homage to the Heavenly Venerables of the ten directions and the Three Realms and make offerings to the Three Treasures, this is called the Field of Reverence. What is the Field of Compassion? Good man, when beings make offerings with a heart of compassion, without discrimination, even to beasts, this is called the Field of Compassion.

Good man, of these two fields, the Field of Compassion is most supreme. If one gives to the Field of Compassion, such a person’s merit and virtue are vast beyond measure, unbounded by the empty sky.

Good man, if there are beings with abundant wealth who practice giving alone, from birth until old age without ceasing, such a person does not compare to one who, regardless of poverty or wealth, nobility or lowliness, wisdom or folly, whether ordained or lay, exhorts others together, each contributing money and goods, pooling them in one place, and distributing them as needed to the poor, the orphaned, the aged, those with grave illnesses, the severely sick, and those in dire straits, ensuring all are treated equally. Such merit is greatest and immeasurable. Even if one does not give, with every thought, the power of giving constantly arises, never exhausted.

Good man, in the future, my disciples—newly practicing Daoist adepts—will delight in fine clothing, crave rich flavors, seek profit and support, hoard with stinginess, and fail to cultivate a heart of compassion, indulging instead in anger and resentment. Seeing others do good, they harbor jealousy, feigning mockery and scorn, claiming such people seek fame and gain, not the way of our Daoist adepts. When they see alms given to the poor and beggars, they grow even more resentful. Such thoughts are not the mind of one who has left the household life.

Those who follow my Dharma yet practice stinginess, clinging to defiled attachments, seek only immediate results to sustain themselves. Seeing my true Dharma, they utter all manner of evil words, generating disbelief. They lead households and convert the people, yet only cultivate the lesser vehicle’s conditioned practices. Why trouble others with such disturbances, causing them to see only superficial clarity?

Then the Heavenly Venerable addressed the youth, saying: “You are able to inquire thus, building bridges of Dharma, constructing stairways of Dharma. Excellent, good man! The beings of the future world are most pitiable. Why is this?”

All beings, though they possess faith and exert themselves in ascetic practices, fail to grasp the true principle. Though they amass merit ever more, their reward remains meager.

Good man, in the world to come, Daoists of the Three Realms—male and female officials, kings and great ministers, the wealthy and the honored, men and women, humans and non-humans—will scorn my Dharma, belittle the Three Treasures, and regard them as insubstantial. Though they perform many good deeds, they seek only fame and profit, or strive to surpass others. Not one among them will generate a single thought of transcendence.

Good man, it is like an entertainer who displays various skills to delight the crowd—yet such an entertainer does not act from a heart of true joy. Good man, the Daoists of the Three Realms who practice the Dharma in its latter age are likewise.

After my passing, the true Dharma will fade and vanish, while demonic forces arise. Perverse minds flourish, cunning schemes proliferate, and calamities and poisons vie to emerge.

Good man, what constitutes perversity? All Daoists and laypeople, ignorant of the Dharma’s norms, perform good deeds by hosting gatherings in their homes. They invite masters out of attachment, listing names for separate invitations, sending attendants to guard the gates to bar outside masters from entering. Even the poor or sick who come seeking alms are blocked and denied entry. Such gatherings waste food and drink, yielding no merit whatsoever.

There are also those who seek only their own goodness, refusing to teach others. Seeing others perform good deeds, they cannot rejoice or contribute even a small portion. The merit of such people is meager and inferior.

Others, upon seeing temples, images, or scriptures in disrepair, refuse to restore them, instead uttering evil words: “This was not built by my ancestors’ legacy. Why repair what is already ruined? I would rather build something new than restore what stands.” Such people act from self-regard, not from regard for me; their merit is self-serving, not for my sake.

Why is this? For all beings, building anew does not compare to repairing what exists—the merit is far greater. Those who restore the old will behold my form and enter the boundless treasury of the Dharma, the empty and true ground.

Good man, there are also beings who, seeing others gather to perform meritorious deeds, seek only fame and renown, expending their entire households’ wealth in giving. Yet when they see the poor and destitute, they scold and drive them away, offering not even a hair’s worth. Such people are inverted in their goodness, deluded in their practice of giving, falsely cultivating the mind of generosity while harboring no true compassion or intention to give. Their giving is not true, their merit not pure. They sow the seeds of hell and reap the fruits of the three evil destinies.

Such beings are most pitiable. Their efforts are futile, their merit lost. Better to guard and transform the people’s resources—this is the greatest merit.

Good man, those who harbor such thoughts are not true renunciates; they are minions of Māra, their minds those of outsiders, not my disciples. When such people die, they fall into the great hells, enduring suffering for ages. Emerging from hell, they enter the realm of hungry ghosts, suffering great torment. Leaving the hungry ghosts, they take five hundred births as oxen, horses, pigs, or sheep, or even as dogs. After leaving the dog’s body, they endure five hundred lifetimes in poverty and lowliness, afflicted by hunger, thirst, and manifold sufferings, never knowing a moment of ease. Why? Because when they saw others giving, they did not rejoice.

Good man, my attainment of the Dao arose from countless eons of practicing compassion and giving, aiding the poor and those in distress. All the Heavenly Venerables of the ten directions who have attained the true Dao did so through giving, thereby reaching the realm of eternal joy and immovability.

For this reason, I expound in manifold ways to all beings, teaching equanimity, compassion, joy, and renunciation as the foundation for beginners.

Good man, it is like a man whose legs are both broken, yet who wishes to travel far. He cannot advance, but instead falls in one place, and no matter how he strives, he cannot proceed.

Good man, stingy Daoists are likewise. Though they practice as Daoists and don the great Dharma robes, even after eons of practice, if they do not give, they cannot reach the empty and true ground of the Dharma.

Good man, if a Daoist does not practice giving, their Dharma is incomplete. If their Dharma is incomplete, they lack the heart of compassion. Without compassion, they lack the heart of forbearance. Without forbearance, they lack the heart of diligence. Without diligence, they lack the heart of skillful means. Without skillful means, they lack the heart of wisdom. Without wisdom, they will constantly endure afflictions, taking birth as oxen or horses, subject to others’ commands, unable to speak, walking on four legs, devoid of human consciousness, ever suffering.

Good man, if even one person gives of the Dharma, all the Heavenly Venerables of the ten directions will praise, revere, and honor them, teaching them the true treasury of the One Vehicle. For this reason, among all meritorious deeds, giving of wealth is supreme.

Good man, I have also taught in manifold skillful ways: entering fire to temper the body and receive the Dharma; entering the great sea to transform the dragon kings; manifesting as the sick to harmonize medicine; appearing as the poor to share in dedication; expounding talismans and diagrams to subdue the cunning and violent; exhorting the acceptance of precepts to protect my Dharma; encouraging forbearance to refine the mind and cultivate diligence; praising wisdom to skillfully teach all beings and lead them out of the city of afflictions.

Good man, in the future, Daoists will not understand my intent. They will employ various expedients, each clinging to their own views, proclaiming their own abilities, deceiving and confusing the people, and envying one another. Such people are evil Daoists, not to be approached. They extinguish the true Dharma and destroy my empty nature.

When assemblies gather to expound the Dharma, if they fail to grasp its profound meaning and merely assert their own interpretations, slandering the One Vehicle’s treasury of oceanic emptiness and wisdom—claiming that one should cling to the text alone, thus violating true reality and the supreme true Dharma, while boasting, “My words alone accord with right principle”—good man, such evil Daoists who speak thus are demonic kin, masters of external paths, practitioners of the lesser vehicle who lead households to convert the people. Those who do so will forever sink into the three wretched destinies, shuttling back and forth beneath the wind’s blades, dying and being reborn day after day, beaten relentlessly with metal cudgels, never resting to eat or breathe. Hungry, they eat charcoal; thirsty, they drink fiery essence. After ten thousand kalpas, they may be reborn among humans, yet deaf, blind, mute, and dumb—possessing human form but lacking human sentiment.

Good man, these evil Daoists further declare, “Such people are foolish, like stumps or stones. You seek fame and reputation—yet the Dao resides in the heart. Why study scriptures and treatises? What practice do you cultivate?” Those who speak thus are evil companions, not to be approached; they are demonic deviants, taking demons as their kin.

Good man, these evil Daoists, for the sake of fame and profit, slander one another, disregarding the scriptures and Dharma. They insist on their own views, taking falsehood for truth, unable to distinguish right from wrong. They go among Daoists and laypeople, declaring, “I know what is right; I alone can recognize what is wrong.” Those who speak thus destroy my Dharma; they are evil companions, not to be approached.

Good man, when evil Daoists fail to grasp the profound meaning of the scriptures, they claim, “In the Great Vehicle, I am permitted to eat meat.” Those who speak thus are evil companions, teachers of perverse views, not to be approached.

Good man, if there are Daoists who comprehend my true nature—emptiness without the form of eating, emptiness without distinction—who employ various expedient means to transform beings: for those who can be liberated through a lustful form, they manifest a lustful form; for those who can be liberated through an ordinary form, they manifest an ordinary form; for those who can be liberated through a sick form, they manifest a sick form; for those who can be liberated through the form of a king, they manifest the form of a king; for those who can be liberated through the form of a Daoist, they manifest the form of a Daoist. For those who can be liberated, they manifest the appropriate form, constantly expounding the Dharma. Though their minds remain unmoved, they display movement; though they do not manifest a body, they display manifestation; though they do not assume a true body, they display true appearance; though they do not transform beings, they display transformation. Those who speak thus are great Dharma masters, eternally abiding in the “Seven-Treasure City” within the oceanic emptiness, expounding the Dharma for others, liberating beings, and guiding them into the treasury of the One Vehicle’s true emptiness.

Good man, today, among the countless youths in this assembly, each perceives me differently. Some see my body on Mount Xuandu, serene and unmoving; some see my body dwelling in the world, expounding the Dharma; some see my body, sixteen feet tall, supremely dignified; some see a small body, some a large one; some see my body seated upon a jeweled lotus; some see my body liberating beings, guiding them into the treasury; some see the inconceivable oceanic emptiness.

Good man, my teaching and transformation adapt to impermanent forms, whether wandering, abiding, or acting—all far removed from worldly appearances, yet without departing from worldly manifestations, unfolding the forms of Dharma-expounding. Even if one speaks but a single verse, a single line, or a single phrase of the oceanic emptiness Dharma, should someone chant it with kind words and great joy, such merit, suited to the roots of beings, brings manifold benefits: flourishing households, prosperous descendants—merits beyond reckoning.

Good man, evil Daoists who do not understand my meaning expound the Three Caverns and the thirty-six divisions of scriptures, clinging to the text for meaning and forming fixed views on existence and non-existence. Know that such people destroy my Dharma.

Good man, newly ordained Daoists who boast, “I am capable,” calling themselves Dharma masters, liberation masters, or scripture masters—those who, within my Dharma gate, engage in mutual praise or slander—these three kinds of people will enter hell without relinquishing their minds. Such beings are truly pitiable.

Then, the four assemblies, having heard the Great Compassionate Venerable One speak these words, each rose, weeping and bowing, kneeling to prostrate themselves and receive the prediction.

At that time, among the assembly, the youthful Perfected Ones again addressed the question: “Greatly Virtuous Heavenly Worthy, you have expounded that evil Daoists destroy my Dharma. When will such Dharma appear? When will these evil Daoists perish? We beseech the Heavenly Worthy to explain this for our sake.”

Then the Heavenly Worthy replied to the youths: “Good man, after my passing, the true Dharma will spread universally, the people will flourish, kings will practice the Dao, free from premature death, harm, killing, greed, and love. The people, men and women alike, will be without jealousy. Good man, after eight thousand years, the true Dharma will retreat into hiding, and evil Dharma will gradually arise. Kings will lack the Dao, the people will delight in harm, jealousy will prevail, greed and malice will lurk in the shadows, attacking roots and overthrowing rulers, killing without measure. After eight hundred and seventy years, evil Daoists will pervade the land, failing to practice the Dao and Dharma, seeking wealth instead, engaging in unlawful acts, amassing the eight kinds of impure goods. Lacking talent and wisdom, they gather disciples, create their own teachings, transmit inappropriate ordinations, fabricate scriptures, and disseminate them throughout the realm. For these reasons, all laypeople will despise the Three Treasures, defile and insult the Heavenly Lords, slander in various ways, cultivate disbelief, destroy heavenly texts, shatter talismans and diagrams, and demolish halls, dwellings, images, and Dharma bodies.”

For these reasons, the sun and moon will lose their radiance, yin and yang will fall out of harmony, the five grains will fail to ripen, wind and rain will come unseasonably, and dragons will long remain in the depths. The people will harbor malice and envy, delight in killing, vie in ostentation and extravagance, and covet wealth and rank. Benevolence and righteousness will cease to be practiced, and even those with meager riches will be grudged. The noble and the base, each according to their station, will be consumed by thoughts of sensual desire.

At such a time, even if one person should arouse the slightest good intention—erecting halls, fashioning images of the Three Treasures, transcribing true Dharma scriptures, or constructing terraces, halls, and cloisters—such a person will still be unable to generate a heart of reverence, unable to cultivate the mind of offering to Dharma masters, and unwilling to relinquish food, clothing, or bedding. Instead, they will further borrow and beg, consuming the master’s sustenance, without ever reflecting in dread upon the suffering of the three evil destinies in future lives.

Good man, when all laypeople set their minds to doing good, they do so solely to encroach upon and diminish the property of the Three Treasures. Such people, though they feign merit-making, will forever fall into the bodies of the three evil destinies and hungry ghosts.

Good man, in the future age, all laypeople will falsely assume official titles, disbelieve in the consequences of sin and blessing, and show no reverence for the Three Treasures. They will plunder the belongings of masters—food, clothing, and utensils—even levying taxes on the grain, rice, and prepared meals of the monastic community, seizing so much as a single hair of the Three Treasures’ property. Or they will forcibly drive the Three Treasures’ servants and slaves, or compel the Three Treasures’ oxen and horses to bear them, greedily taking slaves and servants for their own use, coercing monastics into becoming wives and concubines, without ever reflecting upon the copper pillars and iron beds that await them in future lives, nor considering that their own bodies are like dead dogs on the road, like illusion, like dream, like lightning, like a flash of light.

Good man, if in this evil age there should be one person who, through manifold expedient means, liberates sentient beings, cultivates the heart of compassion and the heart of wisdom, receives and upholds the *Sutra of the Ocean-Emptiness Treasury of Single-Vehicle Wisdom*, and recites it single-mindedly day and night without cease—such a practitioner is one who truly brings forth the Dharma to act in the world.

Good man, after the reign of the Three Dragons, the Dharma King will appear to govern and transform. Then I, too, will once more expound the Dharma for sentient beings. At such a time, the true Dharma will prevail in the world.

Good man, in the future age, the reason all monastics and laypeople will despise the Dharma is precisely because those evil, greedy, and lustful Daoists fail to practice the Dharma. Though they don the robes of the Dharma, they pursue worldly entanglements: some haunt markets and bazaars, selling goods to sustain themselves; others travel the roads, trading for profit; still others take up the work of painters or skilled artisans.

Some act as physiognomists, divining the fortunes of men and women; others serve as diviners, revealing to people good and ill omens; still others pose as spirit-mediums, compelling others to bow in worship. Through manifold deceptions, they drink wine to the point of intoxication and disorder, singing and dancing for pleasure. Some, flattering and distorting the Dharma, preach to curry favor; others chant spells and incantations to cure diseases; or else they dwell in the mountains yet cling to worldly greed, employing perverse meditative methods to divine fortune and misfortune. Some practice acupuncture and moxibustion or compound various medicines to secure clothing and food. For these reasons, when such evils are extinguished, my Dharma too shall perish—hence it is called the extinction of the Dharma.

Good man, after my passing, when eight hundred million kalpas have elapsed, all such evil Daoists will at last be utterly destroyed.

Good man, in the future age, monastics and laypeople will fashion images—some large, some small, of gold, silver, bronze, or wood—and sell them for money to sustain themselves. Therein, the foolish, unable to discern sin from merit, will purchase and make offerings to them. Such people, both buyer and seller, incur guilt, and for three lifetimes shall be sold by others, reduced to slavery and servitude, beaten and abused at will.

Good man, if there are beings of even the slightest good intention who fashion images yet fail to complete them, leaving them lacking in proper features—some half-formed, with hands and feet unfinished—or who begin new images elsewhere without finishing them, such people shall suffer the torments of the three evil destinies, reborn as serpents without limbs.

Good man, if there are beings who, within their kitchens, jointly decree prohibitions, barring mendicants from approaching their places of food, such people, upon death, shall be reborn in hell, as hungry ghosts, or among beasts, forever partaking of filth and walking on all fours.

Good man, if there are beings who treat the Three Treasures as their own possessions, taking and using them at will, consuming them untimely and without restraint, and who, having left the household life together, regard one another as spiritual companions—such people, in future lives, shall be born far from the realms of humans and gods, dwelling perpetually among border tribes, never hearing the Dharma. Upon death, they shall fall into the three evil destinies, with no ground for repentance.

Good man, if those who have left the household life dwell with such people, though they may perform meritorious deeds in their hearts, their merit shall not come to fruition, and they shall be broken by others. Such people, upon death, shall enter the great flaming cart of hell, burned and boiled by others, with no possibility of repentance. Even if someone advocates for their rescue, that person too shall incur guilt.

Good man, if there are beings who, seeing Daoists cultivate compassion and, upon witnessing living creatures being bought and sold, release them, mock them, saying, “These Daoists seek fame. What merit lies in the lives of these creatures that you would set them free?”—such people shall meet with sudden death, their souls reborn as starving vultures in desolate mountains.

Good man, if in this evil age there is one who arouses the resolve to cultivate and study, embodying great compassion and forbearance, enduring the vexations of others, and diligently reciting the scriptures, let them reflect thus: “All sentient beings, from beginningless time, have been my parents; all sentient beings, from beginningless time, have been my brothers, my sisters, my wives and children, all my kin. For this reason, all sentient beings are my flesh and blood, all sentient beings are my very life.” In accordance with their capacity, let them refrain from consuming raw or cooked meat, abandon the thought of killing, cultivate great compassion, abstain from impure flavors, eat but once a day, refuse additional offerings, and rescue sentient beings from distress and suffering through manifold expedient means, sparing neither body nor life.

Then, the gods, kings, and ministers shall all rejoice, and with their divine powers, they shall protect and assist such a person, ensuring they do not regress. They shall also lend their strength to prevent evil people from obstructing them or seizing their possessions. The merit of such assistance is beyond measure.

Good man, if there is one who, with a heart of compassion, practices equitable giving to all the destitute and distressed, without partiality, such merit is supreme and foremost.

Good man, were I to expound the gates of merit through giving for kalpas unending, I could not exhaust them. Now, as the wheel of impermanence turns, I vow to enter extinction for your sake, briefly entrusting these words to you. You must apply yourselves diligently to ascetic practice, uphold and contemplate the teachings, fathom their profound meaning, expound them to others, and distinguish the gates of meaning, that they may attain the foremost.

Thereupon, the assembly of the Fourfold Assembly and the Perfected Youths, having heard the Great Compassionate One speak these words, foreseeing the future age when the true Dharma would decline, beset by manifold calamities and evil Daoists who would defile the true Dharma gate, stood with hair standing on end in reverence. Gazing upon the Honored One’s countenance, they wept in sorrow, unable to restrain themselves: “Alas, O Compassionate One! We are orphaned and exposed, bereft of the root of the Dharma, bereft of our great refuge and teacher. What shall we do? What shall we do?”

Then the Heavenly Worthy addressed the great assembly: “Perfected Youths, restrain yourselves, do not weep. You must understand that the world is impermanent: the good must turn to evil, the flourishing must decline, the existent must become nonexistent, the strong must grow old. Again, I say to you, set aside these matters. By what marks do you perceive my embodied form that you weep? By what marks do you perceive the bodies of sentient beings that you lose the root of your lineage? By what marks do you perceive all dharmas that you lament thus?”

Thereupon, the Perfected Youths wiped their tears, rose, and knelt, addressing the Heavenly Worthy: “We observe that the Compassionate One does not arise from a prior limit, does not reach the other shore, does not abide in the world, nor is he existent or nonexistent, neither existent nor nonexistent, neither non-existent nor non-nonexistent. He is neither manifest nor hidden, neither form nor formless, neither conditioned nor unconditioned, neither in birth-and-death nor in cessation-and-permanence. He is equal to empty space, without marks of discrimination.”

From the first attainment of the Dao to final quiescence—
I have never seen the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy utter a single word of dharma.
Yet when I observe sentient beings, I see the Great Compassionate One emerging and vanishing, expounding the dharma to liberate them.
The boundless realm of joy of the Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy is inconceivable, unknowable by cognition, ungraspable by discernment.
For this reason, tears flow.
I only beseech the Heavenly Worthy to expound and distinguish these matters for us.

Now, observing sentient beings again, I ask: which of the four great elements constitutes the self?
They are like clouds in empty space, like mirages in the heat, like the flash of flint, like the moon in water, like illusion, like transformation, like reflections in a mirror, like echoes in the void.
Form, perception, volition, and consciousness—all are thus.
The nature of sentient beings’ minds is inconceivable, beyond the ken of the Two Vehicles.
The nature of sentient beings, O Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, is likewise:
neither coming nor going, neither existent nor nonexistent, neither internal nor external.
Coming from nowhere, going nowhere, yet constantly flowing and turning,
falsely suffering affliction—all because sentient beings, from beginningless time, have clung to the notion of a self,
nurturing evil roots and enduring boundless afflictions.

The nature of sentient beings is the source of smoldering delusion,
yet the spirit’s essence is originally pure, serene and unstained.
All dharmas arise from this.
For this reason, all the good and evil karma of sentient beings is created by the one mind alone; no other dharma exists.
Thus, sentient beings neither come nor go, neither exist nor do not exist,
equal to empty space, without discriminating thoughts.

O Great Compassionate Heavenly Worthy, such is my observation of the nature of sentient beings and dharmas.

Thereupon, the Heavenly Worthy praised the Perfected Youth, saying:
“Excellent, excellent! O Perfected Youth, you have spoken well.
Among all who understand the dharma, you are foremost.
One who comprehends the nature of sentient beings is most venerable,
skilled in expounding the marks of the dharma, no different from myself.
I approve and confirm your teaching, which brings benefit.
You shall be named *Sea of Empty Dharma Treasury*, a Heavenly Worthy accomplished in the dharma.

Good son, you have understood that sentient beings have neither coming-and-going nor existence-and-nonexistence.
You should know that equanimous giving is called for.
When giving, observe whether the field is one of merit or not.
If you see impoverished, suffering, or ailing beings, bestow upon them the finest medicines.
When practicing giving, contemplate thus:
neither giver nor recipient is seen; the wealth is likewise empty.
At that time, the three factors—giver, recipient, and gift—are all empty, equanimous, and unimpeded.
Why? All dharmas are pure and selfless.
When giving, do not expect reward, nor seek future joys in the human or heavenly realms.
Rather, seek the great fruit of liberation and supreme peace for sentient beings.
When giving, do so to gather in evil beings and establish them in wholesome dharmas.

Further, contemplate thus:
the Three Realms are empty, the Three Times are empty.
Knowing the Three Times are empty, one’s own body is also empty.
Knowing one’s body is empty, all dharmas are also empty.
Because dharmas are empty, this is called *Sea of Emptiness*.
Relying on scriptural words, one liberates sentient beings,
abiding in the true ground of the *Sea of Emptiness*,
attaining spiritual powers and perceiving manifold forms.

Good son, it is like a man dreaming at night of various events:
he dreams of being bound by officials, enduring manifold sufferings, filled with great sorrow and distress, then suddenly freed.
Moments later, he dreams of becoming a great king, wielding sovereign power and enjoying boundless bliss.
In the dream, he thinks: ‘Just now I suffered so, and now I am free, experiencing such joy.’
Having thought thus, he suddenly awakens—
the suffering and joy of the dream vanish without a trace.
Such dream-events are neither existent nor nonexistent.
All dharmas are likewise.

Good son, having attained spiritual powers and comprehended the nature of sentient beings—
this is right contemplation, this is right view.”

Now you have advanced to the *Sea of Emptiness* dharma-position, and countless youths have entered the seat of the One Vehicle’s wisdom treasury. Whatever they cultivate, they all attain the gateway to superior wisdom. Countless beings arouse the mind to leave the household life; countless beings arouse the mind of generosity. Whether human or non-human, male or female, all attain spiritual powers.

Then, having spoken these words, the Heavenly Venerable addressed the youths: “Good son, in the future, if even one being hears this sutra and generates a joyful mind, the merit such a one gains will be boundless and immeasurable, beyond all speech. If, moreover, someone delights in receiving and upholding it, seals it within the heart, memorizes it with clarity, and contemplates it day and night—reading, reciting, expounding, and teaching it for the benefit of beings—receiving the prediction of enlightenment, know that this sutra universally bestows upon the solitary and destitute. Such a person is my true child; all their words are my own speech. Through this causal condition, the words and language become my boundless [expression].

I shall now return my spirit to the quiescent samadhi-position. Moved by compassion for all beings, adrift and exposed, I entrust this to you, to succeed me as Dharma King and broadly proclaim the true path for all beings. Good son, it is like a king who, wishing to travel through his realms and inspect his myriad subjects, entrusts the treasuries of his domain to the crown prince, to succeed him in the royal enterprise.

Good son, I now entrust this to you in the same way.”

Upon hearing this entrustment, the great assembly rose, made obeisance, wept and wailed, their heads touching the ground, their voices shaking the realm—whether human or non-human—snapping their fingers and lamenting: “Alas! Alas! How could the Venerable One abandon us, losing the root of the Dharma?” Then, having wept and grieved, each knelt in sorrow, their lamentation stilled.

At that time, the youth of Auspicious Marks, from within the great assembly, stepped before the Venerable One and offered this gatha:

“Supreme Venerable One of the primordial heavens,
Marvelous, subtle, most true mark—
Manifesting bodies upon bodies in manifold forms,
Permeating the true Dharma, eternally boundless.

For me, for conditions, universally equal,
Ultimately resolved, entering impermanence—
Entrusting the Dharma King, foremost in the Dharma,
Your skillful words of instruction—do not forget!

Among us, the four assemblies of conditions,
Weeping and shedding tears, utterly without thought—
How could the Great Compassionate, Great Merciful One
Abandon conditions, abandon us, quiescent and formless?

Alas! We are ever adrift and exposed—
Only wish for your compassion, pity us!
Like a newborn calf,
Feeble in drinking the Dharma-milk, weak in strength—
How could you, in a single moment, forsake your original vow?
The world’s exposure cannot be compared!

We beseech the true Dharma-taste of the *Sea of Emptiness*,
Universally sprinkling the sweet dew-medicine upon all beings.
Whether human or non-human, equally benefiting,
The four demons and three poisons extinguished without remainder.

Benefiting humans, devas, and those among humans,
No longer dwelling forever in hell or empty space.
Karmic retribution clearly and distinctly understood—
Together transcending birth and death, ascending to the celestial abode.

O true one of the *Sea of Emptiness*, through great compassion,
For us, beseech the Great Master—
Universally benefiting all beings to perfect fulfillment,
The demon kings of the three realms extinguished without end.

Devas and jade maidens come to praise and admire,
The Jeweled Terrace Mountain manifests marvelous marks.
Fragrant flowers fill the empty sky and fall,
At that time, the assembly of humans and devas all pay reverence.

Suddenly ascending to the ninefold heavens,
Bowing in homage to the Master of the Mystic Capital of Eternal Joy.
Looking down upon the city of beings below,
All aspire to the treasure realm of the *Sea of Emptiness*—
Universally receiving, whether human or non-human.”

Then, having spoken this gatha, the youth of Supreme Perfection knelt, prostrated, and addressed the Heavenly Venerable: “Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable, for our sake, you return your spirit to impermanence, expounding the Dharma of no-self. For the sake of no-self, you speak of self. Through this, there is permanence and impermanence, joy and non-joy, birth and non-birth, lord and non-lord, emptiness and non-emptiness. For this causal condition, you entrust the Dharma King to succeed in guiding beings, that they not grow lax, exhorting them to seek future wisdom and broadly proclaim the One Vehicle’s treasury of *Sea of Emptiness* wisdom.

We reflect: the Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable,
Unborn yet born—birth has no dharma to abide;
Undying yet dying—death has no dharma to extinguish.
For our sake, there is birth and death;
For our sake, there is the return of spirit,
Entering the treasury of the *Sea of Emptiness*,
Abiding in the realm of eternal joy, beyond thought.”

Then, having heard these words, the Heavenly Venerable emitted a subtle and wondrous sound, praising the youth: “Good sons, your wisdom surpasses even mine. You are worthy to be Dharma Lords, to succeed in guiding beings, causing them to dwell in the city of bliss within the *Sea of Emptiness*, and to accomplish the source of all beings’ wisdom. Now, wait but a moment, and you shall see me.”

Having spoken thus, he suddenly vanished, seated in emptiness without a master.

The four assemblies wept in unison, their eyes straining in all directions, yet unable to see him. Lifting their heads to the heavens, they wailed in anguish: “Alas! We are now orphaned and exposed, having lost the root of the Dharma, without refuge or resting place—like newborn infants bereft of their great compassionate mother, cut off in the prime of life. The Great Compassionate Heavenly Venerable! We are now as they are, having lost the Great Compassionate Venerable, severed from the milk of the Dharma, just so.”

Then, having heard these words, the four assemblies snapped their fingers in unison, paid their respects, and withdrew.

*The Supreme One Vehicle Sūtra of the Treasury of Wisdom in the Sea of Emptiness, Scroll Ten, concludes.*
